Are Toes Part of the Wiping Area? An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Discusses whether the toes are included in the wiping area for the three-finger condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether toes are considered part of the wiping area (mahall al-masḥ) in Hanafi law and apply the three-finger condition correctly.

Core Idea
Toes are not counted for the three-finger minimum; the wiping area excludes the toes and includes only the upper foot proper.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles an intra-Hanafi dispute: whether the toes are included in the wiping area (mahall al-masḥ) when measuring the three-finger condition for a torn khuff. Some authorities, like Qadi Khan, hold that the toes are not part of the upper foot for this condition, while others, like the author of al-Nahr, argue they are included. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq sides with Qadi Khan.

Guided Path
1
Define the wiping area (mahall al-masḥ)
According to the Hanafi school, the wiping area is the upper foot (zahr al-qadam) from the tips of the toes to the ankle, excluding the sole. This definition is from al-Muntaba.
The dispute is whether the toes themselves are part of this area for the condition of three fingers.
2
Identify the dispute
Locate the passage from al-Khaniyya and Qadi Khan. They rule that if the part outside the top of the khuff is three fingers including the toes, it is not sufficient.
The three fingers must be from the upper foot (the instep) excluding the toes.
3
Analyze the counter-argument
The author of al-Nahr argues that al-Khulasa does not exclude the toes; it only excludes the sole. He claims that exit of most of the foot is the cause, not the toes.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq refutes this by showing that if exit of most were the cause, the logic would be inconsistent.
4
Derive the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon view is that toes are not counted in the three-finger minimum for the exposed area. This is supported by al-Siraj.
Practical application: If the remaining part of the upper foot is three fingers excluding the toes, wiping is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والخرق الكبير يمنعه قال المصنف في المستصفى : يجوز بالباء بنقطة من تحت والثاء بثلاث من فوق والتفاوت بينهما أن الأول يستعمل في الكمية المتصلة، والثاني في المنفصلة، والثاني منقول عن العالم الكبير بدر الدين .اهـ. وفي المغرب أن الكثرة خلاف القلة وتجعل عبارة عن السعة ومنها قولهم الخرق الكثير .اهـ. فأفاد أن الكثير يستعمل للكمية المنفصلة أيضاً. وصحح في السراج الوهاج رواية المثلثة بدليل قول القدوري : وإن كان أقل. وفي شرح منية المصلي عن خواهر زاده الصحيح الرواية بالباء الموحدة لأن في الكم المنفصل تستعمل الكثرة والقلة وفي الكم المتصل يستعمل الكبر والصغر والخف كم متصل فلا يذكر إلا الكبير لا الكثير .اهـ. وقد علمت عن المغرب استعمال الكثير لهما والأمر في ذلك قريب، وعلى التقدير الأول أو رد عليه أن الخرق واحد فكيف يوصف بالكثرة. وأجيب بأنه اسم مصدر وهو يقع على القليل والكثير. ثم كون الخرق الكبير مانعاً دون القليل قول علمائنا استحسان، والقياس أن يمنع القليل أيضاً وهو قول زفر والشافعي في الجديد لأنه الثلاثة وهو (وهذا يفيد أن الأصابع غير داخلة في المحلية الخ) قال في النهر : هذا وهم إذ ما في الخلاصة إنما يفيد دخولها في المسح لأن أطرافها أو آخرها يوافق ما مر عن المبتغى أي من قوله «ظهر القدم من رؤوس الأصابع إلى معقد الشراك وقوله في الخلاصة وموضع المسح ظهر القدم إنما يحترز بذلك عن باطنه وما في الخانية لا يدل لما ذكره بل إنما لا يجوز المسح في الصورة المذكورة لما أن خروج أكثر القدم نزع وهذا فوقه على أن هذه مقالة عن محمد والمذهب اعتبار الأكثر في الخروج كما ستراه . اهـ. أقول : ما حمل عليه كلام الخلاصة محتمل وهو الظاهر، وأما ما حمل عليه كلام الخانية فلا إذ لو كانت العلة خروج أكثر القدم لم يبق فرق بين المسألتين المذكورتين في الخانية إذ في كل منهما وجد خروج أكثر القدم كما لا يخفى. ويدل على ما ذكره المؤلف من الحكم ما في السراج حيث قال : وإن كان القطع أسفل الكعب إن كان بقي من ظهر القدم قدر ثلاث أصابع أو أكثر يجوز المسح عليهما،
His statement: (And the large tear prevents wiping). The author of al-Mustasfa said: It is permissible with a ba' with one dot below and a tha' with three dots above. The difference between them is that the first is used for continuous quantity, and the second for discontinuous quantity. The second is transmitted from the great scholar Badr al-Din. In al-Mughrib: 'al-kathra (abundance) is the opposite of qilla (littleness) and is used to denote spaciousness, from which comes their saying 'al-kharq al-kathir' (the abundant tear).' So it indicates that 'kathir' is used for discontinuous quantity as well. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, the reading with tha' is corrected, using the evidence of al-Quduri's statement: 'and if it is less (aqall).' In Sharh Munyat al-Musalli from Khwahar Zadah: the correct reading is with the unpointed ba' because for discontinuous quantity, 'kathir' and 'qalil' are used, and for continuous quantity, 'kabir' and 'saghir' are used; the khuff is a continuous quantity, so only 'kabir' not 'kathir' is used. And you have learned from al-Mughrib that 'kathir' is used for both, and the matter is close. According to the first interpretation, an objection is raised: the tear is one thing, so how can it be described as 'kathir'? It is answered that it is a verbal noun and applies to both little and much. Then, that the large tear is preventative while the small tear is not is the saying of our scholars based on istihsan, and qiyas would require that the small tear also be preventative, which is the saying of Zufar and al-Shafi'i in the new (view) because it is the three... And (this indicates that the fingers are not included in the place, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: This is a misunderstanding, for what is in al-Khulasa only indicates their inclusion in wiping because its extremities or its end corresponds to what previously passed from al-Muntaba, i.e., his statement 'the upper foot from the tips of the toes to the place of the shoelace'. And his saying in al-Khulasa 'the place of wiping is the upper foot' only guards against the sole. And what is in al-Khaniyya does not indicate what he mentioned; rather, wiping is not permissible in the mentioned case only because the exit of most of the foot is removal (which invalidates the masḥ) and this is additional, and this is a statement from Muhammad, and the madhhab considers the majority in (the issue of) exit as you will see. I say: what he attributed to the statement of al-Khulasa is probable and it is apparent. As for what he attributed to the statement of al-Khaniyya, it is not, for if the cause was the exit of most of the foot, there would be no difference between the two mentioned cases in al-Khaniyya, since in each of them the exit of most of the foot occurred, as is not hidden. And what indicates the ruling mentioned by the author is what is in al-Siraj where he said: If the cut is below the ankle and what remains of the upper foot is the measure of three fingers or more, wiping on them is permissible.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage addresses two interconnected issues. First, the correct reading of 'al-kharq al-kabir' (the large tear) or 'al-kharq al-kathir'. The author of al-Mustasfa preferred the variant with ba' (kabir) for connected quantity, while others used tha' (kathir) for disconnected quantity. The author of al-Mughrib stated that kathra (abundance) is used for both. The preferred view in Sirāj al-Wahhāj is the reading with tha', citing al-Quduri's phrase 'wa in kāna aqall' (if it is less), which uses qilla (littleness). Others argue for kabir because the khuff is a continuous quantity, so terms of size (kabir/saghir) are used, not quantity (kathir/qalil). The author concludes that the matter is close. Second, the issue of whether the toes are included in the area to be wiped when the khuff is wide at the top. Some scholars, including Qadi Khan, rule that if the part of the foot outside the top of the khuff is three fingers including the toes, it is not sufficient; the three fingers must be from the foot proper (the upper foot) excluding the toes. This is because the toes are not considered part of the wiping area (mahall al-masḥ). The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq responds to a misunderstanding: al-Khulasa does not exclude the toes; rather, it says the location of wiping is the upper foot, which excludes the sole, not the toes. A passage from al-Khaniyya is cited: the reason for invalidity in some cases is the exit of most of the foot, which constitutes removal (which invalidates the masḥ). The author supports the ruling that if the sole of the foot is cut below the ankle, and three finger-widths of the upper foot remain, wiping is valid. This is an intra-madhhab dispute with various authorities.

Key Terms
الخرق الكبير (al-kharq al-kabir): A large tear in the khuff that prevents the validity of wiping; this is the ruling according to the Hanafi madhhab.
محل المسح (mahall al-masḥ): The area of the khuff upon which wiping is performed; specifically the upper foot (zahr al-qadam) from the tips of the toes to the ankle.
خروج الأكثر (khuruj al-akthar): The condition where most of the foot protrudes from the khuff, which nullifies the masḥ because it is considered a removal of the khuff.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi madhhab, if a khuff is torn and the remaining upper part of the foot (excluding toes) is two finger-widths, what is the ruling on wiping?
A) Valid because the toes add up to three.
B) Invalid because the upper foot is less than three fingers.
C) Valid if the toes are also covered.
D) Invalid regardless.

Key Takeaway
Toes are not counted in the three-finger minimum for the wiping area; the condition applies to the upper foot (instep) only.

The Relyed-Upon Measure for Tears in the Front of the Khuff
Intra-Hanafi dispute on front tear measure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the permissible tear in the front of the khuff (three smallest toes) and explain the basis in istihsan and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding hand vs. foot measurement.

Core Idea
A tear exposing three smallest toes or less does not invalidate masah – the khuff remains a valid covering for travel.

This lesson examines the central Hanafi ruling on the size of a tear (kharq) in the front of the khuff. Small tears are common and do not hinder travel, so the school uses istihsan to tolerate them. The dividing line is set at three smallest toes of the foot, based on a narration from Abu Hanifa and adopted by the majority. We will explore the reasoning and why an alternative narration using hand fingers is not relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
Wiping over the khuff is a substitute for washing the foot. The khuff must be a covering that allows normal walking. A tear exposes the foot; the ruling depends on size.
The khuff's function in travel is key.
2
Understand istihsan and the need for a limit
Khuffs inevitably have small tears. Insisting on a completely intact khuff would cause hardship. Istihsan sets a limit between negligible and significant tears.
Hardship is negated by law (haraj marfu').
3
Locate the established measure
Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa: 'It is the measure of three smallest toes of the foot.' This is because that amount prevents consecutive walking, and the majority of toes has the ruling of the whole.
Caution (ihtiyat) dictates using the smallest toe.
4
Analyze the alternative narration (hand fingers)
Some narrations from Abu Hanifa consider the hand's fingers. The text rebuts this: the tear prevents walking (foot action), not wiping (hand action). Attribution to agent over site is the principle, but here the site matters.
The act of wiping is by hand, but the condition is on the foot.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
Sahib al-Hidayah and later scholars prefer the foot measure. The smallest toes are used for caution, and the ruling is settled.
In practice, measure against the wearer's own smallest toes.

Source Text

في التبيين. والأوجه الثاني من الأصابع ما يكون طويلاً ويكون قصيراً فلا يعتبر بأصابع غيره كما لا يخفى. وفي هذا السراج الوهاج وكبر القدم دليل على كبرها وصغره دليل على صغرها فيعرف من الوجه اهـ. وإنما يعتبر الأصغر إذا انكشف موضع غير موضع الأصابع، وأما إذا انكشف أصابع نفسها يعتبر أن ينكشف الثلاث أيتها كانت ولا يعتبر الأصغر لأن كل أصبع أصل بنفسها فلا يعتبر بغيرها حتى لو انكشف الإبهام مع جارتها وهما قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغرها يجوز المسح وإن كان مع جارتها لا يجوز وهذا هو الأصح. كذا في تتمة الفتاوى الصغرى. وحكى القدوري عن الحاكم أنه جعل الإبهام كأصبعين وإن لم يبق مثل ذلك فلا بد من الغسل اهـ فتدبر قوله : ( والأوجه الثاني) قال في النهر: تقديم الزيلعي وغيره للأول يفيد أنه الذي عليه المعول، ويراد بالغير من له أصابع تناسب قدمه صغراً وكبراً لا مطلقه لأن الاعتبار بالموجود أولى من غيره .اهـ وفيه أنه على هذا لا يظهر الفرق بين القولين حتى يكون المعول على الأول منهما قوله (وتعقبه في فتح القدير (الخ قال في النهر : ولقائل منعه لأن الأصابع كذا وهو مردود.

شرح منية المصلي. والخرق المانع هو المنفرج الذي يرى ما تحته الرجل أو يكون منضماً من لكن ينفرج عند المشي أو يظهر القدم منه عند الوضع بأن كان الخرق عرضاً، وإن كان طولاً يدخل فيه ثلاث أصابع وأكثر لكن لا يرى شيئاً من القدم ولا ينفرج عند المشي لصلابته لا يمنع المسح. ولو انكشفت الظهارة وفي داخلها بطانة من جلد أو خرقة مخروزة بالخف لا يمنع والخرق أعلى الكعب لا يمنع لأنه لا عبرة يلبسه والخرق في الكعب وما تحته هو المعتبر في المنع ، ولو كان الخرق تحت القدم فإن كان أكثر القدم منع . كذا في الاختيار وذكره الزيلعي عن الغاية بلفظ (قيل وعلله بأن مواضع الأصابع يعتبر بأكثرها فكذا القدم. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه لو صح هذا التعليل لزم أن لا يعتبر قدر ثلاث أصابع أصغرها إلا إذا كان عند أصغرها لأن كل موضع حينئذ إنما يعتبر بأكثره اهـ. وظاهره اختيار اعتبار ثلاث أصابع مطلقاً وهو ظاهر المتون كما لا يخفى حتى في العقب وهو اختيار السرخسي. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان: هذا إذا كان الخرق في مقدم الخف أو في أعلى القدم أو أسفله، وإن كان الخرق في موضع العقب إن كان يخرج أقل من نصف العقب جاز عليه المسح، وإن كان أكثر لا يجوز، وعن أبي حنيفة في رواية أخرى يمسح حتى يبدو أكثر من نصف العقب اهـ. وعلى هذه الرواية مشى في شرح الجامع الصغير مقتصراً عليها فقال : وإن كان الخرق من مؤخر الخف بإزاء العقب، فإن كان يبدو منه أكثر العقب منع المسح وإلا فلا اهـ. وفي اعتبار المصنف : الأصابع تبعاً لصاحب الهداية رداً لما اختاره صاحب البدائع وشمس الأئمة السرخسي فإنهما قالا : واختلف مشايخنا فيما إذا كان يبدو ثلاثة من الأنامل والأصح أنه لا يجوز المسح عليه اهـ . في الكتاب صاحب الهداية والنهاية والمحيط والأنامل أطراف الأصابع، وصحح صحة الأصابع اعتبرت عضواً على حدة بدليل وجوب الدية بقطعهما، وكان الأصل أن تكون تبعاً للقدم لكن لاعتبارها على حدة اعتبروا فيها الثلاث واعتبار ذلك في العقب على الأصل وليس في غيرها هذا المعنى اهـ. وحاصله أنه إنما اعتبر خروج أكثر الأصابع لأنهم اعتبروها عضواً على حدة واعتبروا خروج أكثر القدم لأن الأصابع في الأصل تابعة له فاعتبروا أكثره بناء على الأصل، وأما غير القدم فيعتبر بالأصابع إذ ليست تابعة له كما في القدم فاندفع اللزوم. أقول : ولا يخفى عليك عدم هذا المنع وذلك لأن المحقق في فتح القدير ذكر أولاً أن الخرق في العقب يمنع بظهور أكثره وأن اعتبار أصغر الأصابع فيما إذا كان في غير موضعها، ثم نقل أنه لو كان تحت القدم يعتبر أكثره فإذا اعتبر أكثر العقب وأكثر القدم لم يبق موضع غير جهة الأصابع يعتبر فيه أصغر الأصابع، فلزم أن لا تعتبر إلا إذا كان الخرق عندها لأن كل موضع حينئذ اعتبر بأكثره. والذي حمل صاحب النهر على ما قال اشتباه العقب بالقدم وظنه أن الكلام في العقب كما يتضح لمن راجع بقية كلامه وليس كما ظن فتنبه. قوله: (رد لما اختاره صاحب البدائع الخ) أي من المنع بظهور الأنامل وهو ما ذكره بقوله :
Book of Purity - Chapter on Wiping over the Khuff. When anything of the foot appears, even if little, washing it becomes apparent because the hadath (ritual impurity) has occurred on it, and the foot is indivisible with respect to washing, so washing all of it is obligatory. The basis of istihsan (juristic preference) is that khuffs are usually not free from a little tearing, and the Law has attached wiping to the name 'khuff,' which is the particular covering by which one traverses distance. Whatever is like this, this meaning exists in it, and the name is absolutely applied to it, so the tearing is considered non-existent. Unlike a khuff that contains many tears, for this meaning is absent, and even if expression of it as a khuff is retained by restricting it to a torn one, it is intended for the absolute meaning, so it is not an absolute khuff, and because one cannot traverse distance by it since consecutive walking is not possible, and the absolute khuff is that by which one traverses, so it is not one. Also, hardship would be necessary upon adopting the first view, since most khuffs are not usually free from it, and hardship is negated by the Law. The matter remained in need of a dividing limit between little and much, so al-Hasan related from Abu Hanifa his statement: 'It is the measure of three toes of the foot, the smallest of them' i.e., the large tear, because when this amount is exposed it prevents traversing distance, and because it is the majority of fingers, and the majority has the ruling of the whole. Then they differed: it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that the consideration is from the hand; then regarding whether they are considered closed or spread, there is difference among the mashayikh. It is mentioned in al-Ajnas. Muhammad said in al-Ziyadat: from the toes of the man, the smallest of them. Sahib al-Hidayah and others declared it sound, and the smallest was considered for caution. For this reason, the toes of the foot are considered in the tear, and the fingers of the hand in the wiping, because the tear prevents traveling and consecutive walking, and that is the action of the foot. As for the act of wiping, it is performed by the hand, and the foot is its site; attribution of the act to the agent rather than the site is the principle, and there is no deviation from the principle without cause, and there is no cause here. In the case of one with amputated fingers, the tear is considered with the fingers of another; it is said with his own fingers if they remain, as in al-Tabyin. The second view is that fingers may be long or short, so it is not considered with the fingers of another, as is not hidden. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: the bigness of the foot is evidence of its bigness, and its smallness is evidence of its smallness, so it is known from the face. The smallest is considered only when a place other than the place of the fingers is exposed. As for when the fingers themselves are exposed, it is considered that three are exposed regardless of which, and the smallest is not considered because each finger is a limb in itself, so it is not considered with another. Thus, if the thumb and its neighbor are exposed and they are the measure of three smallest fingers, wiping is permitted; if with its neighbor it is not permitted. This is the most correct. As in Tatimmat al-Fatawa al-Sughra. Al-Quduri narrated from al-Hakim that he made the thumb like two fingers; if less than that remains, washing is necessary. Reflect on his statement: 'and the second view.' He said in al-Nahr: Al-Zayla'i and others giving precedence to the first indicates that it is the relied-upon. By 'other' is meant one whose fingers suit his foot in smallness and bigness, not absolutely, because consideration of what exists is prior to something else. But it is not apparent from this any difference between the two statements, so that the first is relied upon. His statement: 'and he objected to it in Fath al-Qadir.' He said in al-Nahr: one may forbid it because the fingers are like that, and it is rejected. Explanation of Munyat al-Musalli. The tear that prevents is the open one through which the foot underneath is seen, or one that is closed but opens during walking, or the foot appears from it when placed, if the tear is width-wise. If it is lengthwise, three fingers or more fit into it but nothing of the foot is seen and it does not open during walking due to its stiffness, it does not prevent wiping. If the outer layer is exposed and inside there is a lining of leather or cloth sewn to the khuff, it does not prevent. A tear above the ankle does not prevent because there is no consideration wearing it. The tear at the ankle and below it is what is considered for prevention. If the tear is under the foot, if it is the majority of the foot, it prevents. As in al-Ikhtiyar, and al-Zayla'i mentioned it from al-Ghayah with the wording 'it is said,' and he reasoned that the place of the fingers is considered by their majority, so too the foot. Fath al-Qadir objected: if this reasoning were sound, then the measure of three smallest fingers would not be considered except when at the smallest, because then every place is considered by its majority. Apparently he chooses the absolute consideration of three fingers, which is apparent from the texts, even in the heel, and it is the choice of al-Sarakhsi. In Fatawa Qadikhan: this is if the tear is in the front of the khuff, or on the top of the foot, or its bottom. If the tear is at the place of the heel, if less than half of the heel comes out, wiping over it is permissible; if more, it is not. From Abu Hanifa in another narration: he may wipe until more than half of the heel appears. Following this narration is the author of Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, confining himself to it, he said: if the tear is from the back of the khuff opposite the heel, if more than half of the heel appears, it prevents wiping; otherwise no. In the consideration of the author: the fingers, following Sahib al-Hidayah, is a refutation of what the author of al-Bada'i' and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi chose, for they said: our mashayikh differed regarding when three fingertips appear, and the most correct is that wiping over it is not permissible. In the book, Sahib al-Hidayah, al-Nihayah, and al-Muhit: fingertips are the tips of fingers. He declared sound that the fingers are considered a limb separately, as evidenced by the obligation of blood money for cutting them, and the principle was that they are dependent on the foot, but due to considering them separately, three are considered in them, and consideration of that in the heel is upon the principle, and there is not this meaning in other than it. The gist is that he only considered the exposure of most of the fingers because they considered them a separate limb, and considered exposure of most of the foot because the fingers are originally dependent on it, so they considered its majority based on the principle. As for other than the foot, it is considered by the fingers since they are not dependent on it as in the foot, so the necessary consequence is repelled. I say: the rejection is not hidden from you, because the investigator in Fath al-Qadir first mentioned that a tear in the heel prevents by appearance of its majority, and that consideration of the smallest fingers is when it is in a place other than their place. Then he narrated that if it is under the foot, its majority is considered. So if most of the heel and most of the foot are considered, no place remains other than the direction of the fingers where the smallest fingers are considered, so it necessarily follows that it is not considered except when the tear is at them, because then every place is considered by its majority. What led the author of al-Nahr to say this was confusion between the heel and the foot, and his assumption that the discussion is about the heel, as becomes clear for one who reviews the rest of his statement. It is not as he thought, so be attentive. His statement: 'a refutation of what the author of al-Bada'i' chose' i.e., the prohibition due to appearance of fingertips, which is what he mentioned with his statement.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissible size of a tear (kharq) in a leather sock (khuff) for the validity of wiping (masah) over it. It begins with the general principle that if any part of the foot appears through the tear, washing that part becomes necessary because the foot is indivisible in washing (ghusl). However, the school adopts istihsan (juristic preference) because khuffs commonly have small tears; the law attaches wiping to the name 'khuff', which implies a covering that enables travel. A small tear does not negate this meaning, so it is considered non-existent. But a large tear prevents travel, so it negates the ruling. The dividing line is set by the narration from al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa: it is the measure of three smallest toes of the foot. This is because that amount prevents walking consecutively, and because it is the majority of toes, and the majority has the ruling of the whole. Then the text reports a difference: a narration from Abu Hanifa considers the hand's fingers; there is also difference among later mashayikh on whether the fingers are considered closed or spread. Imam Muhammad, in al-Ziyadat, specifies the smallest toes of the foot, and this is adopted by Sahib al-Hidayah for caution (ihtiyat). The reasoning distinguishes between the tear (which hinders walking, an act of the foot) and wiping (an act of the hand). The passage then provides further details: for a person with amputated toes, the tear is estimated by another's toes; if the tear exposes the toes themselves, then three toes regardless of size are considered, not the smallest, because each toe is an independent limb. A critical refinement appears from Fath al-Qadir, which objects to the reasoning that considers the majority in all cases. The text then addresses tears in different locations: on the top, bottom, or heel. For the heel, the majority view is that less than half of the heel appearing permits wiping, while more prevents; a narration from Abu Hanifa allows wiping until more than half appears. The passage ends with a discussion reconciling the different positions, especially regarding the heel vs. front of the foot. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the measure for tears in the front is three smallest toes, and for the heel it is more than half of the heel.

Key Terms
خرق (kharq): A tear or hole in the khuff (leather sock) that may affect the validity of wiping over it.
أصابع الرجل (asābi' al-rijl): The toes of the foot, used as the standard measure for tear size in the front of the khuff.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the maximum size of a tear in the front of the khuff that still permits wiping (masah)?
A) Three hand fingers closed
B) Three smallest toes of the foot
C) More than half of the heel
D) Any tear that reveals the foot

Key Takeaway
For tears in the front of the khuff, the measure is three smallest toes of the foot—this is the mufta bihi position based on caution and the function of the khuff in travel.

Taharah — Purification

10 min
Tears in the Heel and the Critical Refinement of the Majority Principle
Intra-Hanafi dispute on heel tear and refinement of reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the ruling for heel tears from front tears and explain the critical refinement from Fath al-Qadir that challenges uniform application of the majority principle.

Core Idea
For heel tears, the measure is half the heel; caution prevents wiping when more than half appears, but a narration permits until more than half, reflecting a nuanced application of the majority principle.

This lesson extends the analysis to tears in the heel of the khuff. Unlike the front, the heel is not directly involved in walking, leading to a different threshold. We will examine the main view (less than half permits) and the alternative narration (more than half permits). Additionally, we will analyze the critical objection from Fath al-Qadir which argues that the majority principle cannot be applied uniformly across all locations, and how the school reconciles these positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the location and its significance
The heel is a different area of the khuff. It does not bear weight during walking like the front. Therefore, a tear in the heel is less disruptive to travel.
The function of the khuff in travel is key.
2
State the main ruling for heel tears
From Fatawa Qadikhan: if less than half of the heel appears through the tear, wiping is permissible; if more than half appears, wiping is not permissible. This is the majority view.
Some later scholars like al-Sarakhsi adopt a uniform three-finger rule for all locations.
3
Examine the alternative narration
A narration from Abu Hanifa allows wiping until more than half of the heel appears. Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir follows this more lenient view.
This shows the scope of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Understand the critique of Fath al-Qadir
Fath al-Qadir objects to the reasoning that applies the majority principle to the heel. If the majority is considered in every location, then the specific rule of three smallest toes would only apply when the tear is exactly at the toes, contradicting the established measure.
This is a critical refinement (naqd) of the istidlal.
5
Synthesize the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position differentiates: front - three smallest toes; heel - half the heel. The alternative narration is known but not preferred due to caution, though some leniency exists.
In practice, one should follow the stricter view to avoid invalid wudu.

لما ظهر شيء من القدم وإن قل ظهر غسله لحلول الحدث به والرجل في حق الغسل غير متجزئه فوجب غسلها كلها ووجه الاستحسان أن الخفاف لا تخلو عن قليل الخرق عادة والشرع علق المسح بمسمى الخف والشرع علق المسح بمسمى انكشف منع من قطع المسافة، ولأنه أكثر الأصابع وللأكثر حكم الكل. ثم اختلفوا فروى عن أبي حنيفة أن المعتبر كونها من اليد ثم في اعتبارها مضمومة أو منفرجة اختلاف المشايخ. ذكره في الأجناس. وقال محمد في الزيادات من أصابع الرجل أصغرها، وصححه صاحب الهداية كغيره واعتبر الأصغر للاحتياط وإنما اعتبر على هذا أصابع الرجل في الخرق وأصابع اليد في المسح لأن الخرق يمنع قطع السفر وتتابع المشي وإنه فعل الرجل، فأما فعل المسح فإنه يتأدى باليد والرجل محله وإضافة الفعل إلى الفاعل دون المحل هي الأصل ولا عدول عن الأصل بلا موجب ولا موجب هنا، وفي مقطوع الأصابع يعتبر الخرق بأصابع غيره وقيل بأصابع نفسه لو كانت قائمة كذا في التبيين. والأوجه الثاني من الأصابع ما يكون طويلاً ويكون قصيراً فلا يعتبر بأصابع غيره كما لا يخفى. وفي هذا السراج الوهاج وكبر القدم دليل على كبرها وصغره دليل على صغرها فيعرف من الوجه اهـ. وإنما يعتبر الأصغر إذا انكشف موضع غير موضع الأصابع، وأما إذا انكشف أصابع نفسها يعتبر أن ينكشف الثلاث أيتها كانت ولا يعتبر الأصغر لأن كل أصبع أصل بنفسها فلا يعتبر بغيرها حتى لو انكشف الإبهام مع جارتها وهما قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغرها يجوز المسح وإن كان مع جارتها لا يجوز وهذا هو الأصح. كذا في تتمة الفتاوى الصغرى. وحكى القدوري عن الحاكم أنه جعل الإبهام كأصبعين وإن لم يبق مثل ذلك فلا بد من الغسل اهـ فتدبر قوله : ( والأوجه الثاني) قال في النهر: تقديم الزيلعي وغيره للأول يفيد أنه الذي عليه المعول، ويراد بالغير من له أصابع تناسب قدمه صغراً وكبراً لا مطلقه لأن الاعتبار بالموجود أولى من غيره .اهـ وفيه أنه على هذا لا يظهر الفرق بين القولين حتى يكون المعول على الأول منهما قوله (وتعقبه في فتح القدير (الخ قال في النهر : ولقائل منعه لأن الأصابع كذا وهو مردود.

شرح منية المصلي. والخرق المانع هو المنفرج الذي يرى ما تحته الرجل أو يكون منضماً من لكن ينفرج عند المشي أو يظهر القدم منه عند الوضع بأن كان الخرق عرضاً، وإن كان طولاً يدخل فيه ثلاث أصابع وأكثر لكن لا يرى شيئاً من القدم ولا ينفرج عند المشي لصلابته لا يمنع المسح. ولو انكشفت الظهارة وفي داخلها بطانة من جلد أو خرقة مخروزة بالخف لا يمنع والخرق أعلى الكعب لا يمنع لأنه لا عبرة يلبسه والخرق في الكعب وما تحته هو المعتبر في المنع ، ولو كان الخرق تحت القدم فإن كان أكثر القدم منع . كذا في الاختيار وذكره الزيلعي عن الغاية بلفظ (قيل وعلله بأن مواضع الأصابع يعتبر بأكثرها فكذا القدم. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه لو صح هذا التعليل لزم أن لا يعتبر قدر ثلاث أصابع أصغرها إلا إذا كان عند أصغرها لأن كل موضع حينئذ إنما يعتبر بأكثره اهـ. وظاهره اختيار اعتبار ثلاث أصابع مطلقاً وهو ظاهر المتون كما لا يخفى حتى في العقب وهو اختيار السرخسي. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان: هذا إذا كان الخرق في مقدم الخف أو في أعلى القدم أو أسفله، وإن كان الخرق في موضع العقب إن كان يخرج أقل من نصف العقب جاز عليه المسح، وإن كان أكثر لا يجوز، وعن أبي حنيفة في رواية أخرى يمسح حتى يبدو أكثر من نصف العقب اهـ. وعلى هذه الرواية مشى في شرح الجامع الصغير مقتصراً عليها فقال : وإن كان الخرق من مؤخر الخف بإزاء العقب، فإن كان يبدو منه أكثر العقب منع المسح وإلا فلا اهـ. وفي اعتبار المصنف : الأصابع تبعاً لصاحب الهداية رداً لما اختاره صاحب البدائع وشمس الأئمة السرخسي فإنهما قالا : واختلف مشايخنا فيما إذا كان يبدو ثلاثة من الأنامل والأصح أنه لا يجوز المسح عليه اهـ . في الكتاب صاحب الهداية والنهاية والمحيط والأنامل أطراف الأصابع، وصحح صحة الأصابع اعتبرت عضواً على حدة بدليل وجوب الدية بقطعهما، وكان الأصل أن تكون تبعاً للقدم لكن لاعتبارها على حدة اعتبروا فيها الثلاث واعتبار ذلك في العقب على الأصل وليس في غيرها هذا المعنى اهـ. وحاصله أنه إنما اعتبر خروج أكثر الأصابع لأنهم اعتبروها عضواً على حدة واعتبروا خروج أكثر القدم لأن الأصابع في الأصل تابعة له فاعتبروا أكثره بناء على الأصل، وأما غير القدم فيعتبر بالأصابع إذ ليست تابعة له كما في القدم فاندفع اللزوم. أقول : ولا يخفى عليك عدم هذا المنع وذلك لأن المحقق في فتح القدير ذكر أولاً أن الخرق في العقب يمنع بظهور أكثره وأن اعتبار أصغر الأصابع فيما إذا كان في غير موضعها، ثم نقل أنه لو كان تحت القدم يعتبر أكثره فإذا اعتبر أكثر العقب وأكثر القدم لم يبق موضع غير جهة الأصابع يعتبر فيه أصغر الأصابع، فلزم أن لا تعتبر إلا إذا كان الخرق عندها لأن كل موضع حينئذ اعتبر بأكثره. والذي حمل صاحب النهر على ما قال اشتباه العقب بالقدم وظنه أن الكلام في العقب كما يتضح لمن راجع بقية كلامه وليس كما ظن فتنبه. قوله: (رد لما اختاره صاحب البدائع الخ) أي من المنع بظهور الأنامل وهو ما ذكره بقوله :
Book of Purity - Chapter on Wiping over the Khuff. When anything of the foot appears, even if little, washing it becomes apparent because the hadath (ritual impurity) has occurred on it, and the foot is indivisible with respect to washing, so washing all of it is obligatory. The basis of istihsan (juristic preference) is that khuffs are usually not free from a little tearing, and the Law has attached wiping to the name 'khuff,' which is the particular covering by which one traverses distance. Whatever is like this, this meaning exists in it, and the name is absolutely applied to it, so the tearing is considered non-existent. Unlike a khuff that contains many tears, for this meaning is absent, and even if expression of it as a khuff is retained by restricting it to a torn one, it is intended for the absolute meaning, so it is not an absolute khuff, and because one cannot traverse distance by it since consecutive walking is not possible, and the absolute khuff is that by which one traverses, so it is not one. Also, hardship would be necessary upon adopting the first view, since most khuffs are not usually free from it, and hardship is negated by the Law. The matter remained in need of a dividing limit between little and much, so al-Hasan related from Abu Hanifa his statement: 'It is the measure of three toes of the foot, the smallest of them' i.e., the large tear, because when this amount is exposed it prevents traversing distance, and because it is the majority of fingers, and the majority has the ruling of the whole. Then they differed: it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that the consideration is from the hand; then regarding whether they are considered closed or spread, there is difference among the mashayikh. It is mentioned in al-Ajnas. Muhammad said in al-Ziyadat: from the toes of the man, the smallest of them. Sahib al-Hidayah and others declared it sound, and the smallest was considered for caution. For this reason, the toes of the foot are considered in the tear, and the fingers of the hand in the wiping, because the tear prevents traveling and consecutive walking, and that is the action of the foot. As for the act of wiping, it is performed by the hand, and the foot is its site; attribution of the act to the agent rather than the site is the principle, and there is no deviation from the principle without cause, and there is no cause here. In the case of one with amputated fingers, the tear is considered with the fingers of another; it is said with his own fingers if they remain, as in al-Tabyin. The second view is that fingers may be long or short, so it is not considered with the fingers of another, as is not hidden. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: the bigness of the foot is evidence of its bigness, and its smallness is evidence of its smallness, so it is known from the face. The smallest is considered only when a place other than the place of the fingers is exposed. As for when the fingers themselves are exposed, it is considered that three are exposed regardless of which, and the smallest is not considered because each finger is a limb in itself, so it is not considered with another. Thus, if the thumb and its neighbor are exposed and they are the measure of three smallest fingers, wiping is permitted; if with its neighbor it is not permitted. This is the most correct. As in Tatimmat al-Fatawa al-Sughra. Al-Quduri narrated from al-Hakim that he made the thumb like two fingers; if less than that remains, washing is necessary. Reflect on his statement: 'and the second view.' He said in al-Nahr: Al-Zayla'i and others giving precedence to the first indicates that it is the relied-upon. By 'other' is meant one whose fingers suit his foot in smallness and bigness, not absolutely, because consideration of what exists is prior to something else. But it is not apparent from this any difference between the two statements, so that the first is relied upon. His statement: 'and he objected to it in Fath al-Qadir.' He said in al-Nahr: one may forbid it because the fingers are like that, and it is rejected. Explanation of Munyat al-Musalli. The tear that prevents is the open one through which the foot underneath is seen, or one that is closed but opens during walking, or the foot appears from it when placed, if the tear is width-wise. If it is lengthwise, three fingers or more fit into it but nothing of the foot is seen and it does not open during walking due to its stiffness, it does not prevent wiping. If the outer layer is exposed and inside there is a lining of leather or cloth sewn to the khuff, it does not prevent. A tear above the ankle does not prevent because there is no consideration wearing it. The tear at the ankle and below it is what is considered for prevention. If the tear is under the foot, if it is the majority of the foot, it prevents. As in al-Ikhtiyar, and al-Zayla'i mentioned it from al-Ghayah with the wording 'it is said,' and he reasoned that the place of the fingers is considered by their majority, so too the foot. Fath al-Qadir objected: if this reasoning were sound, then the measure of three smallest fingers would not be considered except when at the smallest, because then every place is considered by its majority. Apparently he chooses the absolute consideration of three fingers, which is apparent from the texts, even in the heel, and it is the choice of al-Sarakhsi. In Fatawa Qadikhan: this is if the tear is in the front of the khuff, or on the top of the foot, or its bottom. If the tear is at the place of the heel, if less than half of the heel comes out, wiping over it is permissible; if more, it is not. From Abu Hanifa in another narration: he may wipe until more than half of the heel appears. Following this narration is the author of Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, confining himself to it, he said: if the tear is from the back of the khuff opposite the heel, if more than half of the heel appears, it prevents wiping; otherwise no. In the consideration of the author: the fingers, following Sahib al-Hidayah, is a refutation of what the author of al-Bada'i' and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi chose, for they said: our mashayikh differed regarding when three fingertips appear, and the most correct is that wiping over it is not permissible. In the book, Sahib al-Hidayah, al-Nihayah, and al-Muhit: fingertips are the tips of fingers. He declared sound that the fingers are considered a limb separately, as evidenced by the obligation of blood money for cutting them, and the principle was that they are dependent on the foot, but due to considering them separately, three are considered in them, and consideration of that in the heel is upon the principle, and there is not this meaning in other than it. The gist is that he only considered the exposure of most of the fingers because they considered them a separate limb, and considered exposure of most of the foot because the fingers are originally dependent on it, so they considered its majority based on the principle. As for other than the foot, it is considered by the fingers since they are not dependent on it as in the foot, so the necessary consequence is repelled. I say: the rejection is not hidden from you, because the investigator in Fath al-Qadir first mentioned that a tear in the heel prevents by appearance of its majority, and that consideration of the smallest fingers is when it is in a place other than their place. Then he narrated that if it is under the foot, its majority is considered. So if most of the heel and most of the foot are considered, no place remains other than the direction of the fingers where the smallest fingers are considered, so it necessarily follows that it is not considered except when the tear is at them, because then every place is considered by its majority. What led the author of al-Nahr to say this was confusion between the heel and the foot, and his assumption that the discussion is about the heel, as becomes clear for one who reviews the rest of his statement. It is not as he thought, so be attentive. His statement: 'a refutation of what the author of al-Bada'i' chose' i.e., the prohibition due to appearance of fingertips, which is what he mentioned with his statement.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissible size of a tear (kharq) in a leather sock (khuff) for the validity of wiping (masah) over it. It begins with the general principle that if any part of the foot appears through the tear, washing that part becomes necessary because the foot is indivisible in washing (ghusl). However, the school adopts istihsan (juristic preference) because khuffs commonly have small tears; the law attaches wiping to the name 'khuff', which implies a covering that enables travel. A small tear does not negate this meaning, so it is considered non-existent. But a large tear prevents travel, so it negates the ruling. The dividing line is set by the narration from al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa: it is the measure of three smallest toes of the foot. This is because that amount prevents walking consecutively, and because it is the majority of toes, and the majority has the ruling of the whole. Then the text reports a difference: a narration from Abu Hanifa considers the hand's fingers; there is also difference among later mashayikh on whether the fingers are considered closed or spread. Imam Muhammad, in al-Ziyadat, specifies the smallest toes of the foot, and this is adopted by Sahib al-Hidayah for caution (ihtiyat). The reasoning distinguishes between the tear (which hinders walking, an act of the foot) and wiping (an act of the hand). The passage then provides further details: for a person with amputated toes, the tear is estimated by another's toes; if the tear exposes the toes themselves, then three toes regardless of size are considered, not the smallest, because each toe is an independent limb. A critical refinement appears from Fath al-Qadir, which objects to the reasoning that considers the majority in all cases. The text then addresses tears in different locations: on the top, bottom, or heel. For the heel, the majority view is that less than half of the heel appearing permits wiping, while more prevents; a narration from Abu Hanifa allows wiping until more than half appears. The passage ends with a discussion reconciling the different positions, especially regarding the heel vs. front of the foot. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the measure for tears in the front is three smallest toes, and for the heel it is more than half of the heel.

Key Terms
العقب (al-'aqib): The heel; a different location where the tear measure is based on half the heel appearing.
الأنامل (al-anāmil): Fingertips; the tips of the fingers. In this passage, some scholars considered that if three fingertips appear, it prevents wiping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, when does a tear at the heel of the khuff prevent wiping?
A) When more than half of the heel appears.
B) When any part of the heel appears.
C) When three fingertips appear through the heel.
D) When the tear exposes the entire heel.

Key Takeaway
For tears in the heel, the measure is half the heel—less than half permits wiping, more than half prevents, reflecting the distinct function of the heel in walking.

The Basic Definition of a Hole That Prevents Wiping over the Khuff
Defines the characteristics of a hole that prevents wiping.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which holes in a khuff invalidate wiping and apply the exceptions.

Core Idea
A hole that exposes the foot, even if only when walking, invalidates wiping unless it is small, stiff, above the ankle, or has an inner lining.

Wiping over the khuff is a special dispensation in wudu, but it relies on the khuff being a proper covering. Understanding what constitutes a hole that breaks this coverage is crucial for the validity of your wudu. This lesson unpacks the definition from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
Wiping over khuff is valid only if the khuff covers the foot. A hole may negate this covering.
The act is the wiping, the condition is the integrity of the khuff.
2
Distinguish types of holes
Holes that are wide open (either constantly or when walking) prevent wiping. Holes that are lengthwise and stiff do not prevent if they don't expose the foot.
Widthwise vs. lengthwise is key.
3
Apply exceptions
Inner lining or patched leather negates the hole. Holes above the ankle are ignored. The hole must be at ankle level or below.
These are defined in the text.
4
Handle under-foot holes
For the bottom of the khuff, the criterion is whether the hole exposes the majority of the foot.
This is a different measure than the top.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة - باب المسح :
شرح منية المصلي. والخرق المانع هو المنفرج الذي يرى ما تحته الرجل أو يكون منضماً من لكن ينفرج عند المشي أو يظهر القدم منه عند الوضع بأن كان الخرق عرضاً، وإن كان طولاً يدخل فيه ثلاث أصابع وأكثر لكن لا يرى شيئاً من القدم ولا ينفرج عند المشي لصلابته لا يمنع المسح. ولو انكشفت الظهارة وفي داخلها بطانة من جلد أو خرقة مخروزة بالخف لا يمنع والخرق أعلى الكعب لا يمنع لأنه لا عبرة يلبسه والخرق في الكعب وما تحته هو المعتبر في المنع ، ولو كان الخرق تحت القدم فإن كان أكثر القدم منع . كذا في الاختيار وذكره الزيلعي عن الغاية بلفظ (قيل وعلله بأن مواضع الأصابع يعتبر بأكثرها فكذا القدم. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه لو صح هذا التعليل لزم أن لا يعتبر قدر ثلاث أصابع أصغرها إلا إذا كان عند أصغرها لأن كل موضع حينئذ إنما يعتبر بأكثره اهـ. وظاهره اختيار اعتبار ثلاث أصابع مطلقاً وهو ظاهر المتون كما لا يخفى حتى في العقب وهو اختيار السرخسي. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان: هذا إذا كان الخرق في مقدم الخف في مقدم الخف أو في أعلى القدم أو أسفله، وإن كان الخرق في موضع العقب إن كان يخرج أقل من نصف العقب جاز عليه المسح، وإن كان أكثر لا يجوز، وعن أبي حنيفة في رواية أخرى يمسح حتى يبدو أكثر من نصف العقب اهـ. وعلى هذه الرواية مشى في شرح الجامع الصغير مقتصراً عليها فقال : وإن كان الخرق من مؤخر الخف بإزاء العقب، فإن كان يبدو منه أكثر العقب منع المسح وإلا فلا اهـ. وفي اعتبار المصنف : الأصابع تبعاً لصاحب الهداية رداً لما اختاره صاحب البدائع وشمس الأئمة السرخسي فإنهما قالا : واختلف مشايخنا فيما إذا كان يبدو ثلاثة من الأنامل والأصح أنه لا يجوز المسح عليه اهـ . في الكتاب صاحب الهداية والنهاية والمحيط والأنامل أطراف الأصابع،
وصحح
ما
صحة
الأصابع اعتبرت عضواً على حدة بدليل وجوب الدية بقطعهما، وكان الأصل أن تكون تبعاً للقدم لكن لاعتبارها على حدة اعتبروا فيها الثلاث واعتبار ذلك في العقب على الأصل وليس في غيرها هذا المعنى اهـ. وحاصله أنه إنما اعتبر خروج أكثر الأصابع لأنهم اعتبروها عضواً على حدة واعتبروا خروج أكثر القدم لأن الأصابع في الأصل تابعة له فاعتبروا أكثره بناء على الأصل، وأما غير القدم فيعتبر بالأصابع إذ ليست تابعة له كما في القدم فاندفع اللزوم. أقول : ولا يخفى عليك عدم . هذا المنع وذلك لأن المحقق في فتح القدير ذكر أولاً أن الخرق في العقب يمنع بظهور أكثره وأن اعتبار أصغر الأصابع فيما إذا كان في غير موضعها، ثم نقل أنه لو كان تحت القدم يعتبر أكثره فإذا اعتبر أكثر العقب وأكثر القدم لم يبق موضع غير جهة الأصابع يعتبر فيه أصغر الأصابع، فلزم أن لا تعتبر إلا إذا كان الخرق عندها لأن كل موضع حينئذ اعتبر بأكثره. والذي حمل صاحب النهر على ما قال اشتباه العقب بالقدم وظنه أن الكلام في العقب كما يتضح لمن راجع بقية كلامه وليس كما ظن فتنبه. قوله: (رد لما اختاره صاحب البدائع الخ) أي من المنع بظهور الأنامل وهو ما ذكره بقوله :
والقدم من الرجل ما يطأ عليه الإنسان من لدن الرسغ إلى ما دون ذلك وهي مؤنثة والعقب بكسر القاف مؤخر القدم.
Book of Purification - Section on Wiping: Explanation of Munyat al-Musalli. The hole that prevents is the wide one through which the foot underneath is seen, or it is narrow but spreads during walking, or the foot appears from it when placing [the foot] if the hole is widthwise. But if it is lengthwise, three fingers and more can enter but nothing of the foot is seen and it does not spread during walking due to its stiffness, it does not prevent wiping. And if the outer layer is uncovered but inside it has a lining of leather or a patch sewn to the khuff, it does not prevent. A hole above the ankle does not prevent because no consideration is given to it; the hole at the ankle and below is what is considered in prevention. And if the hole is under the foot, then if it is the majority of the foot it prevents. This is in al-Ikhtiyar; al-Zayla'i mentioned it from al-Ghayah with the wording: 'It was said, and he reasoned that the place of the fingers is considered by their majority, so too the foot.' It was objected to in Fath al-Qadir: 'If this reasoning were correct, it would necessitate not considering the measure of three smallest fingers except when the hole is at the smallest finger, because then every place would be considered by its majority.' The apparent [meaning] is the choice of considering three fingers absolutely, which is apparent from the texts, even at the heel, and it is the choice of al-Sarakhsi. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: 'This is if the hole is in the front of the khuff, or in the top of the foot, or its bottom. And if the hole is at the heel, if less than half of the heel is exposed, wiping upon it is permissible; if more, it is not.' And from Abu Hanifa in another narration: 'He may wipe until more than half of the heel appears.' And upon this narration, [the author] proceeded in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, confining himself to it, and said: 'And if the hole is from the back of the khuff opposite the heel, then if more than the heel appears from it, it prevents wiping; otherwise no.' And in the author's consideration: fingers are, following the author of al-Hidayah, a refutation of what was chosen by the author of al-Bada'i' and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, for they said: 'Our scholars differed regarding when three finger-tips appear, and the most correct is that wiping upon it is not permissible.' In the book, the author of al-Hidayah, al-Nihayah, and al-Muhit: 'Finger-tips' are the ends of fingers, and he corrected: 'Fingers are considered a separate organ, as evidenced by the obligation of blood-money for cutting them, and the original [rule] was that they are subsidiary to the foot, but due to considering them separately, they considered three [fingers] in them, and considering that in the heel is upon the original, and in other than it this meaning does not exist.' The summary: He only considered exposure of the majority of the fingers because they considered them a separate organ, and considered exposure of the majority of the foot because the fingers are originally subsidiary to it, so they considered its majority based on the original. As for other than the foot, it is considered by the fingers since it is not subsidiary to it as in the foot, so the implication is repelled. I say: It is not hidden from you that this prevention is absent. That is because the verifier in Fath al-Qadir first mentioned that the hole in the heel prevents by the appearance of its majority, and that considering the smallest fingers is when [the hole] is not in its place. Then he narrated that if [the hole] is under the foot, its majority is considered. So if the majority of the heel and the majority of the foot are considered, no place remains other than the direction of the fingers where the smallest fingers are considered, so it is necessary that it is not considered unless the hole is at them. What led the author of al-Nahr to say this was his confusion of the heel with the foot, thinking that the discussion is about the heel, as is clear to whoever reviews the rest of his words, and it is not as he thought, so beware. His statement: 'A refutation of what was chosen by the author of al-Bada'i' etc.' i.e., the prohibition due to the appearance of finger-tips, and that is what he mentioned by his statement: 'And the foot of a man is what he treads upon from the wrist to below that, and it is feminine, and the heel (al-'aqib) with a kasra on the qaf is the back of the foot.'
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the precise definition of a hole (khurq) in a khuff that invalidates the permissibility of wiping over it. The author begins by stating the general rule from Munyat al-Musalli: a hole that prevents wiping is one that is wide open, exposing the foot underneath, or is narrow but spreads open when walking, or from which the foot appears when the foot is placed, if the hole is lengthwise. However, if the hole is lengthwise and can accommodate three fingers but does not expose any part of the foot due to stiffness and does not spread during walking, it does not prevent wiping. The commentary then details specific scenarios: if the outer layer is torn but there is an inner lining, it does not prevent; a hole above the ankle is ignored; a hole at or below the ankle is what counts. If the hole is under the foot, the criterion is the majority of the foot. The text then presents a disagreement among Hanafi scholars: al-Zayla'i reports from al-Ghayah that the measure is the majority of the foot, by analogy with toes. But Fath al-Qadir objects: if that reasoning were sound, one would never use the three smallest fingers measure except when the hole is exactly there, because everywhere else the majority would apply. The author then notes that the apparent view of the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) and other major texts is to absolutely consider three fingers, even at the heel, and that this is the choice of al-Sarakhsi. Fatawa Qadikhan distinguishes between front of khuff, top/bottom of foot (three fingers), and heel (half of heel). Another narration from Abu Hanifa permits wiping until more than half the heel appears. The commentary then discusses the reasoning: fingers are considered a separate organ (hence three fingers), while the foot is considered by majority because fingers are subsidiary to it; the heel is treated like the foot (majority), not like fingers. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq then criticizes the author of al-Nahr for confusing heel with foot and wrongly conflating the two. The passage ends with lexical definitions of 'foot' and 'heel' for clarity.

Key Terms
الخرق (al-khurq): A tear or hole in the khuff.
الكعب (al-ka'b): The ankle bone.
الأنامل (al-anamil): Finger-tips.
البطانة (al-bitanah): Inner lining.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which hole does NOT prevent wiping?
A) A widthwise hole that opens during walking showing the foot.
B) A lengthwise stiff hole that does not expose the foot.
C) A hole under the foot showing the majority of the foot.
D) A hole at the ankle that exposes the foot.

Key Takeaway
A hole in the khuff prevents wiping only if it exposes the foot, either widthwise or lengthwise that spreads, with exceptions for stiffness, lining, and above ankle.

The Internal Hanafi Dispute on the Heel and the Three-Finger Criterion
Examines internal Hanafi disagreement on the measure for holes at the heel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the internal Hanafi disagreement on whether the heel is treated like the foot (majority) or like fingers (three fingers), and identify the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
The heel's legal status: treated like the foot (majority) in some narrations, but the mufta bihi view applies the three-finger measure absolutely.

While the basic rule for holes in the khuff is clear, a dispute arose among Hanafi scholars regarding holes at the heel. This lesson unpacks the difference of opinion between Qadikhan's report and the majority view, the reasoning using the analogy of fingers as separate organs, and the final tarjih.

Guided Path
1
State the positions on the heel
Qadikhan reports that if less than half the heel is exposed, wiping is valid; if more, it is invalid. Another narration from Abu Hanifa allows wiping until more than half appears.
The difference is between a strict and a lenient measure.
2
Understand the reasoning for fingers
Fingers are considered separate organs (diyah is paid for them), so the measure is three fingers. The foot is one organ, so its majority is considered. The heel is part of the foot, so by analogy, majority should apply.
This is the reasoning of al-Hidayah.
3
Identify the opposing view of al-Bada'i' and al-Sarakhsi
They argued that if three finger-tips (anamil) appear, wiping is invalid, analogizing the foot to the hand.
This applies the three-finger measure to the whole foot.
4
Analyze the author's critique
Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq refutes al-Bada'i' by showing that the fingers are subsidiary to the foot, so the original rule (majority) applies to the foot; the three-finger rule is for separate organs.
This resolves the apparent contradiction.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is that three fingers (smallest) is the measure for any hole that does not expose the foot; for under-foot, majority; for heel, also three fingers, as chosen by the author of al-Hidayah and the matn.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq also supports this.

Source Text

Book of Purification - Section on Wiping: Explanation of Munyat al-Musalli. The hole that prevents is the wide one through which the foot underneath is seen, or it is narrow but spreads during walking, or the foot appears from it when placing [the foot] if the hole is widthwise. But if it is lengthwise, three fingers and more can enter but nothing of the foot is seen and it does not spread during walking due to its stiffness, it does not prevent wiping. And if the outer layer is uncovered but inside it has a lining of leather or a patch sewn to the khuff, it does not prevent. A hole above the ankle does not prevent because no consideration is given to it; the hole at the ankle and below is what is considered in prevention. And if the hole is under the foot, then if it is the majority of the foot it prevents. This is in al-Ikhtiyar; al-Zayla'i mentioned it from al-Ghayah with the wording: 'It was said, and he reasoned that the place of the fingers is considered by their majority, so too the foot.' It was objected to in Fath al-Qadir: 'If this reasoning were correct, it would necessitate not considering the measure of three smallest fingers except when the hole is at the smallest finger, because then every place would be considered by its majority.' The apparent [meaning] is the choice of considering three fingers absolutely, which is apparent from the texts, even at the heel, and it is the choice of al-Sarakhsi. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: 'This is if the hole is in the front of the khuff, or in the top of the foot, or its bottom. And if the hole is at the heel, if less than half of the heel is exposed, wiping upon it is permissible; if more, it is not.' And from Abu Hanifa in another narration: 'He may wipe until more than half of the heel appears.' And upon this narration, [the author] proceeded in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir, confining himself to it, and said: 'And if the hole is from the back of the khuff opposite the heel, then if more than the heel appears from it, it prevents wiping; otherwise no.' And in the author's consideration: fingers are, following the author of al-Hidayah, a refutation of what was chosen by the author of al-Bada'i' and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, for they said: 'Our scholars differed regarding when three finger-tips appear, and the most correct is that wiping upon it is not permissible.' In the book, the author of al-Hidayah, al-Nihayah, and al-Muhit: 'Finger-tips' are the ends of fingers, and he corrected: 'Fingers are considered a separate organ, as evidenced by the obligation of blood-money for cutting them, and the original [rule] was that they are subsidiary to the foot, but due to considering them separately, they considered three [fingers] in them, and considering that in the heel is upon the original, and in other than it this meaning does not exist.' The summary: He only considered exposure of the majority of the fingers because they considered them a separate organ, and considered exposure of the majority of the foot because the fingers are originally subsidiary to it, so they considered its majority based on the original. As for other than the foot, it is considered by the fingers since it is not subsidiary to it as in the foot, so the implication is repelled. I say: It is not hidden from you that this prevention is absent. That is because the verifier in Fath al-Qadir first mentioned that the hole in the heel prevents by the appearance of its majority, and that considering the smallest fingers is when [the hole] is not in its place. Then he narrated that if [the hole] is under the foot, its majority is considered. So if the majority of the heel and the majority of the foot are considered, no place remains other than the direction of the fingers where the smallest fingers are considered, so it is necessary that it is not considered unless the hole is at them. What led the author of al-Nahr to say this was his confusion of the heel with the foot, thinking that the discussion is about the heel, as is clear to whoever reviews the rest of his words, and it is not as he thought, so beware. His statement: 'A refutation of what was chosen by the author of al-Bada'i' etc.' i.e., the prohibition due to the appearance of finger-tips, and that is what he mentioned by his statement: 'And the foot of a man is what he treads upon from the wrist to below that, and it is feminine, and the heel (al-'aqib) with a kasra on the qaf is the back of the foot.'
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the precise definition of a hole (khurq) in a khuff that invalidates the permissibility of wiping over it. The author begins by stating the general rule from Munyat al-Musalli: a hole that prevents wiping is one that is wide open, exposing the foot underneath, or is narrow but spreads open when walking, or from which the foot appears when the foot is placed, if the hole is lengthwise. However, if the hole is lengthwise and can accommodate three fingers but does not expose any part of the foot due to stiffness and does not spread during walking, it does not prevent wiping. The commentary then details specific scenarios: if the outer layer is torn but there is an inner lining, it does not prevent; a hole above the ankle is ignored; a hole at or below the ankle is what counts. If the hole is under the foot, the criterion is the majority of the foot. The text then presents a disagreement among Hanafi scholars: al-Zayla'i reports from al-Ghayah that the measure is the majority of the foot, by analogy with toes. But Fath al-Qadir objects: if that reasoning were sound, one would never use the three smallest fingers measure except when the hole is exactly there, because everywhere else the majority would apply. The author then notes that the apparent view of the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) and other major texts is to absolutely consider three fingers, even at the heel, and that this is the choice of al-Sarakhsi. Fatawa Qadikhan distinguishes between front of khuff, top/bottom of foot (three fingers), and heel (half of heel). Another narration from Abu Hanifa permits wiping until more than half the heel appears. The commentary then discusses the reasoning: fingers are considered a separate organ (hence three fingers), while the foot is considered by majority because fingers are subsidiary to it; the heel is treated like the foot (majority), not like fingers. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq then criticizes the author of al-Nahr for confusing heel with foot and wrongly conflating the two. The passage ends with lexical definitions of 'foot' and 'heel' for clarity.

Key Terms
العقب (al-'aqib): The heel; the back of the foot.
الأنامل (al-anamil): Finger-tips; used in a minority opinion as a measure for the foot.
الدية (al-diyah): Blood-money; the dower for harming body parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view regarding a hole at the heel?
A) If less than half the heel appears, wiping is valid.
B) If more than half the heel appears, wiping is invalid.
C) If three smallest fingers of the heel appear, wiping is invalid.
D) Holes at the heel are always ignored.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a hole of three smallest fingers in the khuff, including at the heel, prevents wiping.

Combining Multiple Holes in the Khuff for Wiping
Rules on whether multiple small holes in one or both khuffs are combined to affect validity of wiping.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining holes in khuffs and explain the positions of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Small holes are excused, but multiple in one khuff are combined; if total exceeds three fingers, wiping is invalid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical issue for those who perform mash 'ala al-khuffayn: what happens when a khuff has multiple small holes? The matn states a clear rule, but the commentary reveals an important intra-Hanafi dispute. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply rulings based on necessity and the school's methodology.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
Identify the ruling from the matn: holes are combined in one khuff, not across two. This means the total area of all holes in a single khuff is summed.
The base text is Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentator explains that the concession for small holes is due to necessity (darurah) to avoid hardship, especially for the poor. However, the obligatory wipe must land on intact leather, not on the exposed foot.
3
Present Ibn al-Humam's objection
Ibn al-Humam (Kamal al-Din) argues that there is no need to combine small holes when they are scattered, because the khuff still covers the foot sufficiently for walking. Combining is not logically required.
This objection is based on the purpose of the khuff: covering the foot for walking.
4
Identify Abu Yusuf's view
Ibn Amir Haj supports Ibn al-Humam with a narration from Abu Yusuf that holes are not combined at all, whether in one khuff or two. This is recorded in Khizanat al-Fatawa.
Abu Yusuf's view is considered stronger in reasoning by some later scholars.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Despite the strong objection, the majority of Hanafi texts (al-Hidayah, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, al-Nahr) adopt the combining view (Imam Muhammad). The consensus of the texts indicates its preference, and it is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The reason: the original rule is that any hole prevents, but necessity requires excusing small holes and combining them to avoid hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ويجمع في خف لا فيهما أي ويجمع الخروق في خف واحد لا في خفين حتى لو كان الخرق في خف واحد قدر أصبعين في موضع أو موضعين وفي الآخر قدر أصبع جاز المسح عليهما بعد أن يقع المقدار الواجب على الخف نفسه فإن الظاهر أنه لو مسح مقدار ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد على الصحيح منه وعلى ما ظهر من الخرق اليسير كما في هذه المسألة أنه لا يجوز لأن المسح على ما ظهر من الخرق ليس بمسح على الخف حقيقة ولا حكماً. أما حقيقة فظاهر، وأما حكماً فلأن الخرق المذكور إنما جعل عفواً في جواز المسح على خف هو فيه لكن لا بحيث يكون ما يقع على ما ظهر منه محسوباً من القدر الواجب لما تقدم من أنه إنما اعتبر عفواً فيه لأن في اعتباره مانعاً من المسح حرجاً لازماً لما ذكرنا، ولا حرج في عدم احتساب ما يقع من المسح على ما ظهر منه من القدر الواجب لعدم العسر في فعله على غيره، فظهر أن عدم اعتباره مانعاً من المسح على خف هو فيه للضرورة وأنه لا ضرورة لاحتساب ما يقع إليه من القدر الواجب من المسح وما ثبت بالضرورة يتقدر بقدرها . كذا في شرح منية المصلي. وإذ امتنع المسح على أحدهما بجمع الخروق المتفرقة امتنع المسح على الآخر لما عرف حتى يلبس مكان المتخرق ما يجوز المسح عليه وهذا الحكم المذكور في الكتاب هو المشهور في المذهب، وقد بحث المحقق كمال الدين بحثاً عليه فقال : لقائل أن يقول لا داعي إلى جمع الخروق وهو اعتبارها كأنها في مكان واحد لمنع المسح لأن امتناعه فيما إذا اتحد المكان حقيقة لانتفاء الخف بامتناع قطع المسافة المعتادة لا لذاته، ولا به معنى لذات الانكشاف من حيث هو انكشاف وإلا لوجب الغسل في الخرق الصغير وهذا المعنى منتف عند تفرقها صغيرة كقدر الحمصة والفولة لإمكان قطعها ذلك وعدم وجوب غسل مع البادي اهـ. وقد قواه تلميذه ابن أمير حاج بأن هذه الدراية موافقة لرواية عن أبي يوسف مذكورة في خزانة الفتاوى، وفي بعض شروح المجمع أنه لا يجمع الخرق سواء كان في خف أو خفين اهـ. وقد رأيت في التوشيح أن هذه الرواية قول أبي يوسف وجعل الجمع قول محمد اهـ. ولا شك أن هذه الدراية أولى مما في المحيط من أن الخروق المتعددة في الخف قدر ثلاثة أصابع تمنع من تتابع المشي فيه إذ لا يخفى ما فيه من المنع الظاهر. ومما في البدائع من أن والأصح أنه لا يجوز المسح عليه، وفي هذه العبارة ركاكة والمراد ما ذكرنا . قوله: (ولا شك أن هذه الدراية أولى مما في المحيط قال في النهر : إطباق عامة المتون والشروح على الجمع مؤذن بترجيحه وذلك لأن الأصل أن الخرق مانع مطلقاً إذ الماسح عليه ليس ماسحاً على الخف لكن لما كانت الخفاف قد لا تخلو عن خرق لا سيما خفاف الفقراء قلنا إن الصغير عفو وجمعناه في واحد لعدم الحرج
His statement: 'And they are combined in one khuff, not in two' i.e., holes are combined in one khuff, not in two. So if the hole in one khuff is the size of two fingers in one place or two places, and in the other khuff the size of one finger, wiping on both is permissible provided that the obligatory amount falls on the khuff itself. For it is apparent that if he wipes the amount of three of the smallest fingers of the hand on the correct [khuff] and upon what appears of the small hole as in this case, it is not permissible because wiping on what appears of the hole is not wiping on the khuff in reality nor in legal effect. As for reality, it is obvious; as for legal effect, because the mentioned hole was only made excused in permitting wiping on a khuff in which it exists, but not such that what falls on what appears of it is counted from the obligatory amount. Since it was previously mentioned that it was only considered excused because considering it a preventer would cause unavoidable hardship, as we mentioned, and there is no hardship in not counting the wiping that falls on what appears from it from the obligatory amount because there is no difficulty in doing it on other [parts]. So it becomes clear that not considering it a preventer for wiping on a khuff containing it is due to necessity, and there is no necessity to count what falls on it from the obligatory amount of wiping, and what is established by necessity is limited to its extent. Thus in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And since wiping on one of them is prohibited by combining scattered holes, wiping on the other is prohibited for the known reason, until he wears in place of the torn one something upon which wiping is permissible. This ruling mentioned in the book is the well-known [view] in the school. The verifier Kamal al-Din researched against it and said: 'One could say there is no need to combine holes, i.e., considering them as if in one place to prevent wiping, because prohibition when holes are truly in one place is due to the impossibility of the khuff [functioning] due to inability to cover the usual walking distance, not due to the exposure itself; otherwise washing would be obligatory in a small hole. This meaning is absent when they are scattered and small, like the size of a chickpea or a bean, because it is possible to cover that distance and there is no obligation to wash the exposed part.' His student Ibn Amir Haj strengthened this, saying that this narration agrees with a narration from Abu Yusuf mentioned in Khizanat al-Fatawa. And in some commentaries of al-Majma' it says that holes are not combined, whether in one khuff or two. I have seen in al-Tawshih that this narration is the view of Abu Yusuf, and combining is the view of Muhammad. Without doubt, this narration is more worthy than what is in al-Muhit that multiple holes in a khuff of the size of three fingers prevent consecutive walking in it, for the clear prevention in it is not hidden. And what is in al-Bada'i' that 'the most correct is that it is not permissible to wipe upon it' – this expression is feeble, and the intended meaning is what we mentioned. His statement: 'And there is no doubt that this narration is more worthy than what is in al-Muhit.' He said in al-Nahr: 'The agreement of most texts and commentaries on combining indicates its preference, because the original rule is that a hole is absolutely a preventer, since the one wiping on it is not wiping on the khuff, but since khuffs, especially those of the poor, are rarely free from holes, we said a small hole is excused and we combine them into one to avoid hardship.'
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the issue of combining (جمع) multiple small holes in a khuff for the purpose of determining whether the khuff is legally acceptable for wiping. The matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states: 'And they are combined in one khuff, not in two.' The commentator explains: If one khuff has two holes totaling two finger-widths, and the other khuff has a one-finger hole, then wiping on both is permissible because the total in one khuff is less than three fingers. However, the obligatory amount of wiping (three fingers' length) must be performed on the intact part of the khuff, not on the exposed foot. The justification is that the small holes are excused due to necessity (to avoid hardship for poor people whose khuffs often have tears), but the wiped area must actually be on the khuff, not on the foot. The author then presents a significant intra-Hanafi dispute: The verifier Kamal al-Din (Ibn al-Humam) objects to combining holes. He argues that if the holes are scattered and small, the khuff still covers the foot sufficiently for walking, so there is no need to combine them. His student Ibn Amir Haj supports this with a narration from Abu Yusuf that holes are not combined at all, whether in one khuff or two. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq then notes that this narration (Abu Yusuf's) is stronger than the view in al-Muhit that multiple holes of three-finger total prevent walking. However, the majority of texts (including al-Hidayah, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and most commentaries) adopt the combining view (attributed to Imam Muhammad) as the relied-upon position because it avoids hardship. The passage ends by quoting al-Nahr: the consensus of the texts indicates the preference for combining, because the original rule is that any hole prevents, but necessity allows excusing small holes and combining them into one, preventing undue hardship.

Key Terms
جمع الخروق (jam' al-khuruq): The legal principle of combining multiple holes in a single khuff to determine if the total size reaches the threshold that prevents wiping.
الخرق الصغير (al-khurq al-saghir): A small hole that is excused and does not prevent wiping; size less than three smallest fingers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the well-known (mashhur) Hanafi position, what happens if a khuff has two holes: one of two fingers and one of two fingers on different parts of the same khuff?
A) Wiping is valid because each hole is less than three fingers
B) Wiping is invalid because the combined total is four fingers (more than three)
C) Wiping is valid only if the holes are exactly opposite each other
D) Wiping is invalid only if the holes are on the front of the khuff

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, multiple small holes in a single khuff are combined to determine if they exceed the excused limit; this is the mufta bihi despite a strong opposing view from Abu Yusuf.

Basic Ruling on Combining Holes in Khuffs
Explaining the basic rule of combining holes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining holes in khuffs and apply it to determine the validity of masah.

Core Idea
Holes are combined only within one khuff; the obligatory measure must fall on the khuff skin.

When performing masah over khuffs, small holes are common. The Hanafi school teaches that such holes are excused but must be combined to ensure the obligatory wiping area is on the khuff itself. This lesson covers the basic rule and its logical basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping (masah) over khuffs. The ruling is that it is valid only if the obligatory measure (three smallest fingers) touches the khuff skin, not exposed skin through holes.
The passage begins by defining the foot to set anatomical context.
2
Understand the combining rule
Multiple small holes in one khuff are combined and treated as a single hole. Holes from two different khuffs are not combined.
Example: If one khuff has holes totalling two fingers and the other has one finger, masah is valid.
3
Apply the rule to an example
If the combined holes in one khuff reach three fingers, masah on that khuff is invalid. The other khuff may still be valid if its holes are less.
The obligatory measure must appear on the khuff itself, not on exposed skin.
4
State the rationale
Wiping on exposed skin is not wiping on the khuff in reality or legally. Holes are excused only due to necessity (prevalence of holes, especially for the poor). Necessity is measured by its extent.
Thus, the excuse does not extend to counting the wiped area on exposed skin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقدم من الرجل ما يطأ عليه الإنسان من لدن الرسغ إلى ما دون ذلك وهي مؤنثة والعقب بكسر القاف مؤخر القدم. قوله (ويجمع في خف لا فيهما أي ويجمع الخروق في خف واحد لا في خفين حتى لو كان الخرق في خف واحد قدر أصبعين في موضع أو موضعين وفي الآخر قدر أصبع جاز المسح عليهما بعد أن يقع المقدار الواجب على الخف نفسه فإن الظاهر أنه لو مسح مقدار ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد على الصحيح منه وعلى ما ظهر من الخرق اليسير كما في هذه المسألة أنه لا يجوز لأن المسح على ما ظهر من الخرق ليس بمسح على الخف حقيقة ولا حكماً. أما حقيقة فظاهر، وأما حكماً فلأن الخرق المذكور إنما جعل عفواً في جواز المسح على خف هو فيه لكن لا بحيث يكون ما يقع على ما ظهر منه محسوباً من القدر الواجب لما تقدم من أنه إنما اعتبر عفواً فيه لأن في اعتباره مانعاً من المسح حرجاً لازماً لما ذكرنا، ولا حرج في عدم احتساب ما يقع من المسح على ما ظهر منه
