المحقق كمال الدين بحثاً عليه فقال : لقائل أن يقول لا داعي إلى جمع الخروق وهو اعتبارها كأنها في مكان واحد لمنع المسح لأن امتناعه فيما إذا اتحد المكان حقيقة لانتفاء الخف بامتناع قطع المسافة المعتادة لا لذاته، ولا به معنى لذات الانكشاف من حيث هو ا انكشاف وإلا لوجب الغسل في الخرق الصغير وهذا المعنى منتف عند تفرقها صغيرة كقدر الحمصة والفولة لإمكان قطعها ذلك وعدم وجوب غسل مع البادي اهـ. وقد قواه تلميذه ابن أمير حاج بأن هذه الدراية موافقة لرواية عن أبي يوسف مذكورة في خزانة الفتاوى، وفي بعض شروح المجمع أنه لا يجمع الخرق سواء كان في خف أو خفين اهـ. وقد رأيت في التوشيح أن هذه الرواية قول أبي يوسف وجعل الجمع قول محمد اهـ. ولا شك أن هذه الدراية أولى مما في المحيط من أن الخروق المتعددة في الخف قدر ثلاثة أصابع تمنع من تتابع المشي فيه إذ لا يخفى ما فيه من المنع الظاهر. ومما في البدائع من أن والأصح أنه لا يجوز المسح عليه، وفي هذه العبارة ركاكة والمراد ما ذكرنا . قوله: (ولا شك أن هذه الدراية أولى مما في المحيط قال في النهر : إطباق عامة المتون والشروح على الجمع مؤذن بترجيحه وذلك لأن الأصل أن الخرق مانع مطلقاً إذ الماسح عليه ليس ماسحاً على الخف لكن لما كانت الخفاف قد لا تخلو عن خرق لا سيما خفاف الفقراء قلنا إن الصغير عفو وجمعناه في واحد لعدم الحرج فيهما بخلاف النجاسة والانكشاف وينقضه ناقض الوضوء ونزع خف ومضى المدة إن الخرق إنما منع جواز المسح لظهور مقدار فرض المسح فإذا كان متفرقاً . في الخفين لم يظهر مقدار فرض المسح من كل منهما فإن ظهور مقدار فرض المسح من كل منهما لا يظهر له أثر في المنع بعد إمكان قطع المسافة به وتتابع المشي فيه وبقاء شيء من ظهر القدم يقع فيه مقدار الواجب من المسح فكان الظاهر ما بحثه المحقق والله أعلم وأقل الخرق الذي يجمع ما يدخل فيه المسلة، وأما ما دونه فلا الحاقاً بمواضع الخرز ذكره في جوامع الفقه . قوله (بخلاف النجاسة والانكشاف) أي بخلاف النجاسة المتفرقة حيث تجمع وإن كانت متفرقة في خفيه أو ثوبه أو بدنه أو مكانه أو في المجموع. وبخلاف انكشاف العورة المتفرق كانكشاف شيء من فرج المرأة وشيء من ظهرها وشيء من فخذها وشيء من ساقها حيث يجمع لمنع جواز الصلاة لأن المانع في العورة انكشاف القدر المانع وفي النجاسة هو كونه حاملاً لذلك القدر المانع وقد وجد فيهما، وأما الخروق في الخف فإنما منع لامتناع قطع المسافة معه وهذا المعنى مفقود فيما إذا لم يكن في كل خف مقدار ثلاث أصابع. إليه أشار في الهداية وقد تقدم ما فيه وسيأتي في باب شروط الصلاة كيفية الجمع وما فيه. هذا وقد ذكر في الخلاصة أن النجاسة لو كانت في ثوب المصلي أقل من قدر الدرهم وتحت قدميه أقل من قدر الدرهم ولكن لو جمع بلغ أكثر من قدر الدرهم لا يجمع ، ولا يخفى أنه مخالف لما قدمناه وهو مذكور في التبيين وغيره. وفي الخلاصة أيضاً والخرق في أذني الأضحية هل يجمع؟ اختلف المشايخ فيه وأعلام الثوب تجمع اهـ.
The foot of the man is what a person treads upon from the wrist (ankle) to below that, and it is feminine, and al-'aqib (with kasra of qaf) is the back of the foot. His statement (He combines upon one khuff, not upon both): meaning he combines the holes in one khuff, not in two khuffs. So if the hole in one khuff is the size of two fingers in one place or two places, and in the other the size of one finger, it is permissible to wipe over both after the obligatory measure falls upon the khuff itself. The apparent is that if he wiped the measure of three fingers from the smallest fingers of the hand upon the correct opinion and upon what appears of the small hole as in this issue, it is not allowed, because wiping upon what appears of the hole is not wiping upon the khuff in reality or legally. As for reality, it is apparent. As for legally, because the mentioned hole was made excused regarding permissibility of wiping upon a khuff in which it exists, but not such that what falls upon what appears of it is counted from the obligatory measure. This is because, as mentioned earlier, it was considered excused therein because considering it a preventer from wiping would cause necessary hardship. There is no hardship in not counting what falls of wiping upon what appears of it from the obligatory measure due to the lack of difficulty in doing it upon other than it. Thus it becomes clear that not considering it a preventer from wiping upon the khuff in which it is is due to necessity, and there is no necessity for counting what falls upon it from the obligatory measure of wiping. And what is established by necessity is restricted to its extent. As in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. Since wiping on one of them is prevented by combining the scattered holes, wiping on the other is prevented as known, until he puts on in place of the holed one what is permissible to wipe upon. And this ruling mentioned in the book is the well-known in the madhhab. The investigator Kamal al-Din made an inquiry upon it and said: One may say there is no cause to combine holes and consider them as if in one place to prevent wiping, because its prevention when the place is united in reality is due to the khuff being non-existent by inability to traverse the usual distance, not due to its essence, nor due to the meaning of exposure itself as exposure, otherwise washing would be obligatory for the small hole. And this meaning is absent when they are scattered small like the size of a chickpea and a fava bean because it is possible to traverse that and there is no obligation to wash with al-Badi? He said. And his student Ibn Amir Hajj strengthened it by saying this report is consistent with a narration from Abu Yusuf mentioned in Khizanat al-Fatawa. And in some commentaries of al-Majma' it states: He does not combine holes whether in one khuff or two. And I saw in al-Tawshih that this narration is the saying of Abu Yusuf, and combining is the saying of Muhammad. There is no doubt that this report is more appropriate than what is in al-Muhit that multiple holes in the khuff of the size of three fingers prevent continuity of walking in it, because the apparent prevention in it is not hidden. And from what is in al-Bada'i' that the most correct is that it is not permissible to wipe upon it, and in this expression there is weakness and the intended is what we mentioned. His statement: (There is no doubt that this report is more appropriate than what is in al-Muhit) said in al-Nahr: The consensus of most texts and commentaries on combining indicates its preference. This is because the principle is that the hole is absolutely a preventer, since the one wiping upon it is not wiping upon the khuff. But since khuffs may not be free of holes, especially the khuffs of the poor, we said the small is excused and we combine it into one due to lack of difficulty in them, unlike impurity and exposure. And it is nullified by the nullifier of wudu', removal of the khuff, and passage of the period. Indeed, the hole only prevents permissibility of wiping because of the appearance of the obligatory measure of wiping. So if it is scattered in the two khuffs, the obligatory measure of wiping does not appear from each of them. The appearance of the obligatory measure of wiping from each of them has no effect on prevention after possibility of traversing the distance with it and continuity of walking in it and the remaining of part of the top of the foot upon which the obligatory measure of wiping falls. So what the investigator researched is apparent. And Allah knows best. The smallest hole that is combined is what includes the needle. As for less than that, no, analogizing to the places of stitching. Mentioned in Jawami' al-Fiqh. His statement (Unlike impurity and exposure): meaning unlike scattered impurity which is combined even if scattered in his two khuffs or his garment or his body or his place or in the total. And unlike scattered exposure of the 'awrah such as exposure of some of the woman's private part and some of her back and some of her thigh and some of her leg, which is combined to prevent permissibility of prayer, because the preventer in 'awrah is exposure of the preventing amount, and in impurity it is being a carrier of that preventing amount, and it has occurred in them. As for holes in the khuff, it is prevented because of inability to traverse the distance with it, and this meaning is absent when in each khuff there is not the amount of three fingers. This is indicated in al-Hidayah, and what is in it has preceded, and how to combine will come in the chapter on conditions of prayer. This and it has been mentioned in al-Khulasa: If impurity is on the garment of the worshipper less than the size of a dirham and under his feet less than the size of a dirham, but if combined it reaches more than the size of a dirham, it is not combined. It is not hidden that it contradicts what we have presented, and it is mentioned in al-Tabyin and others. And in al-Khulasa also: And the hole in the ears of the udhiyah, is it combined? The mashayikh differed on it. And the silk patches of a garment are combined.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the Hanafi ruling on combining multiple small holes in khuffs for the validity of wiping (masah). The author begins by defining the foot (al-qadam) and its parts, setting the anatomical context for masah. The central ruling is that if a khuff has multiple small holes, they are combined (ja‘ma) and treated as a single hole when determining the obligatory measure (qadr al-wajib) for wiping. However, this combining is only done within one khuff (khuff wahid), not across both khuffs. For example, if one khuff has holes totalling two fingers' width and the other has one finger's width, wiping is permitted because the obligatory measure (three smallest fingers) falls on the intact skin of the khuff itself. But if the holes in one khuff reach three fingers' width when combined, wiping becomes invalid. The text explains that wiping on the exposed skin through the hole is not considered wiping on the khuff in reality or by legal fiction. Initially, the author presents the well-known (mashhur) ruling that holes are combined. Then he introduces a criticism by al-Muhaqqiq Kamal al-Din, who argues that combining is unnecessary when the holes are not in the same place, because the prevention of wiping is due to inability to walk, not to the exposure itself. This position is supported by a narration from Abu Yusuf, while combining is attributed to Imam Muhammad. The author acknowledges the strength of this narration but notes that the majority of texts and commentaries side with combining due to the principle that a hole is a preventer, though small holes are excused and combined to avoid hardship (haraj). The passage concludes by contrasting holes with impurity (najasa) and exposure of ‘awrah (inkishaf al-‘awrah), which are combined across the whole body or garment because the preventer is the existence of impurity or exposure itself, not the ability to walk. The Hanafi school's relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the combination of holes in one khuff, and the minimum hole considered is one that admits a needle; smaller holes are ignored by analogy to stitching holes.

Key Terms
الخرق (al-kharq): A hole or tear in the khuff (leather sock) that exposes the foot.
الجمع (al-jam‘): The legal fiction of treating multiple small holes as if they were a single contiguous hole for the purpose of measuring their total size.
العفو (al-‘afw): The excused status of small holes that would otherwise prevent masah, allowed due to the prevalence of such holes and to avoid hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the well-known Hanafi position, how are multiple small holes in khuffs treated for the validity of masah?
A) They are ignored completely.
B) They are combined within each khuff separately.
C) They are combined across both khuffs.
D) Only holes that prevent walking are considered.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, small holes in khuffs are combined within each khuff individually; masah is invalid if the combined hole area in one khuff equals the obligatory measure of three smallest fingers.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Combining Holes – Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
Discussing the intra-Hanafi dispute on combining holes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding combining holes, evaluate their proofs, and state the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf holds that scattered small holes do not invalidate masah; Muhammad holds they are combined. The majority adopts combining.

The Hanafi school itself has an internal debate on whether small holes should be combined. Imam Muhammad supports combining, while Abu Yusuf (in a narration) argues that only the ability to walk matters. This lesson examines their proofs and the final relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Muhammad: holes are combined within one khuff. Abu Yusuf: holes are not combined at all; only a single hole large enough to prevent walking invalidates masah.
The passage attributes the non-combining view to Abu Yusuf in some works.
2
Understand Abu Yusuf's proof
He argues that the prevention of masah is due to inability to walk (imtina' qat' al-masafa), not due to exposure itself. Scattered small holes do not impede walking, so they do not prevent masah.
If exposure were the cause, even a small hole would require washing the foot.
3
Understand Muhammad's proof
The principle is that any hole prevents masah because wiping on exposed skin is not wiping on the khuff. Small holes are excused only by necessity, and necessity is measured by its extent. Combining prevents the obligatory measure from appearing on exposed skin.
The majority of texts adopt this view.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Muhammad's view, if scattered holes in one khuff total three fingers, masah is invalid. Under Abu Yusuf's view, if walking is possible, masah is valid even if total hole area is large.
Practical difference in daily practice.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author notes that the majority (mashhur) is combining. The narration from Abu Yusuf is strong but not adopted. The mufta bihi is combining.
Later texts like al-Hidayah and al-Bahr al-Ra'iq side with combining.

Source Text

أصبعين في موضع أو موضعين وفي الآخر قدر أصبع جاز المسح عليهما بعد أن يقع المقدار الواجب على الخف نفسه فإن الظاهر أنه لو مسح مقدار ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد على الصحيح منه وعلى ما ظهر من الخرق من القدر الواجب لعدم العسر في فعله على غيره، فظهر أن عدم اعتباره مانعاً من المسح على خف هو فيه للضرورة وأنه لا ضرورة لاحتساب ما يقع إليه من القدر الواجب من المسح وما ثبت بالضرورة يتقدر بقدرها . كذا في شرح منية المصلي. وإذ امتنع المسح على أحدهما بجمع الخروق المتفرقة امتنع المسح على الآخر لما عرف حتى يلبس مكان المتخرق ما يجوز المسح عليه وهذا الحكم المذكور في الكتاب هو المشهور في المذهب، وقد بحث المحقق كمال الدين بحثاً عليه فقال : لقائل أن يقول لا داعي إلى جمع الخروق وهو اعتبارها كأنها في مكان واحد لمنع المسح لأن امتناعه فيما إذا اتحد المكان حقيقة لانتفاء الخف بامتناع قطع المسافة المعتادة لا لذاته، ولا به معنى لذات الانكشاف من حيث هو ا انكشاف وإلا لوجب الغسل في الخرق الصغير وهذا المعنى منتف عند تفرقها صغيرة كقدر الحمصة والفولة لإمكان قطعها ذلك وعدم وجوب غسل مع البادي اهـ. وقد قواه تلميذه ابن أمير حاج بأن هذه الدراية موافقة لرواية عن أبي يوسف مذكورة في خزانة الفتاوى، وفي بعض شروح المجمع أنه لا يجمع الخرق سواء كان في خف أو خفين اهـ. وقد رأيت في التوشيح أن هذه الرواية قول أبي يوسف وجعل الجمع قول محمد اهـ. ولا شك أن هذه الدراية أولى مما في المحيط من أن الخروق المتعددة في الخف قدر ثلاثة أصابع تمنع من تتابع المشي فيه إذ لا يخفى ما فيه من المنع الظاهر. ومما في البدائع من أن والأصح أنه لا يجوز المسح عليه، وفي هذه العبارة ركاكة والمراد ما ذكرنا . قوله: (ولا شك أن هذه الدراية أولى مما في المحيط قال في النهر : إطباق عامة المتون والشروح على الجمع مؤذن بترجيحه وذلك لأن الأصل أن الخرق ونزع خف ومضى المدة إن الخرق إنما منع جواز المسح لظهور مقدار فرض المسح فإذا كان متفرقاً . في الخفين لم يظهر مقدار فرض المسح من كل منهما فإن ظهور مقدار فرض المسح من كل منهما لا يظهر له أثر في المنع بعد بمواضع الخرز ذكره في جوامع الفقه . قوله (بخلاف النجاسة والانكشاف) أي بخلاف النجاسة المتفرقة حيث تجمع وإن كانت متفرقة في خفيه أو ثوبه أو بدنه أو مكانه أو في المجموع. وبخلاف انكشاف العورة المتفرق Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the Hanafi ruling on combining multiple small holes in khuffs for the validity of wiping (masah). The author begins by defining the foot (al-qadam) and its parts, setting the anatomical context for masah. The central ruling is that if a khuff has multiple small holes, they are combined (ja‘ma) and treated as a single hole when determining the obligatory measure (qadr al-wajib) for wiping. However, this combining is only done within one khuff (khuff wahid), not across both khuffs. For example, if one khuff has holes totalling two fingers' width and the other has one finger's width, wiping is permitted because the obligatory measure (three smallest fingers) falls on the intact skin of the khuff itself. But if the holes in one khuff reach three fingers' width when combined, wiping becomes invalid. The text explains that wiping on the exposed skin through the hole is not considered wiping on the khuff in reality or by legal fiction. Initially, the author presents the well-known (mashhur) ruling that holes are combined. Then he introduces a criticism by al-Muhaqqiq Kamal al-Din, who argues that combining is unnecessary when the holes are not in the same place, because the prevention of wiping is due to inability to walk, not to the exposure itself. This position is supported by a narration from Abu Yusuf, while combining is attributed to Imam Muhammad. The author acknowledges the strength of this narration but notes that the majority of texts and commentaries side with combining due to the principle that a hole is a preventer, though small holes are excused and combined to avoid hardship (haraj). The passage concludes by contrasting holes with impurity (najasa) and exposure of ‘awrah (inkishaf al-‘awrah), which are combined across the whole body or garment because the preventer is the existence of impurity or exposure itself, not the ability to walk. The Hanafi school's relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the combination of holes in one khuff, and the minimum hole considered is one that admits a needle; smaller holes are ignored by analogy to stitching holes.

Key Terms
الخرق (al-kharq): A hole in the khuff.
الجمع (al-jam‘): Treating multiple holes as one.
امتناع قطع المسافة (imtina' qat' al-masafa): Inability to traverse the usual distance (walk).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which two Hanafi imams disagree on combining holes, and what is the mufta bihi?
A) Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
B) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; mufta bihi is Abu Yusuf's view.
C) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; mufta bihi is Muhammad's view (combining).
D) Muhammad and al-Shaybani (same person); no dispute.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on combining holes centers on whether the preventer is exposure or walking inability; the relied-upon position is combining (Muhammad's view).

Comparing Holes with Impurity and Exposure of 'Awrah
Contrasting the rule for holes with rules for impurity and 'awrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi rules for combining holes from those for combining impurity and 'awrah exposure.

Core Idea
Impurity and 'awrah exposure are combined across the whole body/garment; holes are combined only per khuff due to different 'illal.

The Hanafi school has distinct rules for combining holes in khuffs, impurity on a garment or body, and exposure of 'awrah. Understanding the underlying causes (walking inability vs. impurity/exposure itself) explains why holes are treated differently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Holes: combined within one khuff. Impurity: combined across the entire garment or body. 'Awrah exposure: combined across the whole body.
The passage explicitly contrasts holes with impurity and exposure.
2
Understand the 'illah for impurity and exposure
Impurity prevents prayer because the person is a carrier of impurity. Exposure of 'awrah prevents prayer due to the act of exposure itself. In both cases, the preventer is the existence of the impurity or the exposure itself, regardless of location.
Thus, they are combined across the whole.
3
Understand the 'illah for holes
A hole prevents wiping not because of exposure per se, but because it indicates inability to walk (since a large hole makes walking difficult). Scattered small holes do not impede walking, so they are not combined.
But the majority view combines them to prevent the obligatory measure from appearing on exposed skin.
4
Apply the distinction
Impurity: even small amounts in different places are combined to check if total exceeds the excused amount. Holes: only within one khuff, and only if they interfere with walking or the obligatory measure.
Example: blood on shirt sleeve and pant leg combine for impurity; but holes in left and right khuff do not combine.

The foot of the man is what a person treads upon from the wrist (ankle) to below that, and it is feminine, and al-'aqib (with kasra of qaf) is the back of the foot. His statement (He combines upon one khuff, not upon both): meaning he combines the holes in one khuff, not in two khuffs. So if the hole in one khuff is the size of two fingers in one place or two places, and in the other the size of one finger, it is permissible to wipe over both after the obligatory measure falls upon the khuff itself. The apparent is that if he wiped the measure of three fingers from the smallest fingers of the hand upon the correct opinion and upon what appears of the small hole as in this issue, it is not allowed, because wiping upon what appears of the hole is not wiping upon the khuff in reality or legally. As for reality, it is apparent. As for legally, because the mentioned hole was made excused regarding permissibility of wiping upon a khuff in which it exists, but not such that what falls upon what appears of it is counted from the obligatory measure. This is because, as mentioned earlier, it was considered excused therein because considering it a preventer from wiping would cause necessary hardship. There is no hardship in not counting what falls of wiping upon what appears of it from the obligatory measure due to the lack of difficulty in doing it upon other than it. Thus it becomes clear that not considering it a preventer from wiping upon the khuff in which it is is due to necessity, and there is no necessity for counting what falls upon it from the obligatory measure of wiping. And what is established by necessity is restricted to its extent. As in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. Since wiping on one of them is prevented by combining the scattered holes, wiping on the other is prevented as known, until he puts on in place of the holed one what is permissible to wipe upon. And this ruling mentioned in the book is the well-known in the madhhab. The investigator Kamal al-Din made an inquiry upon it and said: One may say there is no cause to combine holes and consider them as if in one place to prevent wiping, because its prevention when the place is united in reality is due to the khuff being non-existent by inability to traverse the usual distance, not due to its essence, nor due to the meaning of exposure itself as exposure, otherwise washing would be obligatory for the small hole. And this meaning is absent when they are scattered small like the size of a chickpea and a fava bean because it is possible to traverse that and there is no obligation to wash with al-Badi? He said. And his student Ibn Amir Hajj strengthened it by saying this report is consistent with a narration from Abu Yusuf mentioned in Khizanat al-Fatawa. And in some commentaries of al-Majma' it states: He does not combine holes whether in one khuff or two. And I saw in al-Tawshih that this narration is the saying of Abu Yusuf, and combining is the saying of Muhammad. There is no doubt that this report is more appropriate than what is in al-Muhit that multiple holes in the khuff of the size of three fingers prevent continuity of walking in it, because the apparent prevention in it is not hidden. And from what is in al-Bada'i' that the most correct is that it is not permissible to wipe upon it, and in this expression there is weakness and the intended is what we mentioned. His statement: (There is no doubt that this report is more appropriate than what is in al-Muhit) said in al-Nahr: The consensus of most texts and commentaries on combining indicates its preference. This is because the principle is that the hole is absolutely a preventer, since the one wiping upon it is not wiping upon the khuff. But since khuffs may not be free of holes, especially the khuffs of the poor, we said the small is excused and we combine it into one due to lack of difficulty in them, unlike impurity and exposure. And it is nullified by the nullifier of wudu', removal of the khuff, and passage of the period. Indeed, the hole only prevents permissibility of wiping because of the appearance of the obligatory measure of wiping. So if it is scattered in the two khuffs, the obligatory measure of wiping does not appear from each of them. The appearance of the obligatory measure of wiping from each of them has no effect on prevention after possibility of traversing the distance with it and continuity of walking in it and the remaining of part of the top of the foot upon which the obligatory measure of wiping falls. So what the investigator researched is apparent. And Allah knows best. The smallest hole that is combined is what includes the needle. As for less than that, no, analogizing to the places of stitching. Mentioned in Jawami' al-Fiqh. His statement (Unlike impurity and exposure): meaning unlike scattered impurity which is combined even if scattered in his two khuffs or his garment or his body or his place or in the total. And unlike scattered exposure of the 'awrah such as exposure of some of the woman's private part and some of her back and some of her thigh and some of her leg, which is combined to prevent permissibility of prayer, because the preventer in 'awrah is exposure of the preventing amount, and in impurity it is being a carrier of that preventing amount, and it has occurred in them. As for holes in the khuff, it is prevented because of inability to traverse the distance with it, and this meaning is absent when in each khuff there is not the amount of three fingers. This is indicated in al-Hidayah, and what is in it has preceded, and how to combine will come in the chapter on conditions of prayer. This and it has been mentioned in al-Khulasa: If impurity is on the garment of the worshipper less than the size of a dirham and under his feet less than the size of a dirham, but if combined it reaches more than the size of a dirham, it is not combined. It is not hidden that it contradicts what we have presented, and it is mentioned in al-Tabyin and others. And in al-Khulasa also: And the hole in the ears of the udhiyah, is it combined? The mashayikh differed on it. And the silk patches of a garment are combined.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the Hanafi ruling on combining multiple small holes in khuffs for the validity of wiping (masah). The author begins by defining the foot (al-qadam) and its parts, setting the anatomical context for masah. The central ruling is that if a khuff has multiple small holes, they are combined (ja‘ma) and treated as a single hole when determining the obligatory measure (qadr al-wajib) for wiping. However, this combining is only done within one khuff (khuff wahid), not across both khuffs. For example, if one khuff has holes totalling two fingers' width and the other has one finger's width, wiping is permitted because the obligatory measure (three smallest fingers) falls on the intact skin of the khuff itself. But if the holes in one khuff reach three fingers' width when combined, wiping becomes invalid. The text explains that wiping on the exposed skin through the hole is not considered wiping on the khuff in reality or by legal fiction. Initially, the author presents the well-known (mashhur) ruling that holes are combined. Then he introduces a criticism by al-Muhaqqiq Kamal al-Din, who argues that combining is unnecessary when the holes are not in the same place, because the prevention of wiping is due to inability to walk, not to the exposure itself. This position is supported by a narration from Abu Yusuf, while combining is attributed to Imam Muhammad. The author acknowledges the strength of this narration but notes that the majority of texts and commentaries side with combining due to the principle that a hole is a preventer, though small holes are excused and combined to avoid hardship (haraj). The passage concludes by contrasting holes with impurity (najasa) and exposure of ‘awrah (inkishaf al-‘awrah), which are combined across the whole body or garment because the preventer is the existence of impurity or exposure itself, not the ability to walk. The Hanafi school's relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the combination of holes in one khuff, and the minimum hole considered is one that admits a needle; smaller holes are ignored by analogy to stitching holes.

Key Terms
النجاسة المتفرقة (al-najasah al-mutafarriqah): Scattered impurity across multiple locations.
انكشاف العورة المتفرق (inkishaf al-'awrah al-mutafarriq): Scattered exposure of the private parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between combining holes in khuffs and combining impurity on a garment?
A) Holes are combined across both khuffs; impurity is not.
B) Holes are combined per khuff; impurity is combined across the whole garment or body.
C) Both are combined per item.
D) Neither is combined.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses different combining rules for holes (per khuff based on walking inability) and for impurity or 'awrah (across the whole based on carrying/being exposed), highlighting the importance of 'illah in determining legal rules.

Three Nullifiers of Wiping over Khuffs
Listing and explaining the three nullifiers of masah over khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three nullifiers of wiping over khuffs according to the Hanafi school and explain the legal reasoning for each.

Core Idea
Three things nullify the state of wiping over khuffs: any nullifier of wudu, removing the khuff, and expiry of the time limit.

Wiping over khuffs (masah) is a concession in purification, but this state is fragile. The Hanafi school identifies exactly three events that break this concession and return you to the normal obligation of washing the feet. Understanding these nullifiers is essential for daily practice—whether you are a resident or traveler.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three nullifiers
Read the source text and list the three things that the author says nullify the state of masah. They are: (1) anything that nullifies wudu, (2) removing the khuff, (3) expiry of the defined period.
These are cumulative; any one of them ends the concession.
2
Understand the reasoning for each
For each nullifier, follow the author's legal reasoning. The first is because masah is part of wudu. The second is because the previous hadath spreads to the feet when the barrier is removed. The third is based on the Sunnah's time limits.
The text also addresses a potential objection regarding wiping over the head and shaving.
3
Explore the badal vs khalaf distinction
The author notes a scholarly difference: some consider masah a badal (substitute) for washing, like tayammum. But the preferred view is that it is a khalaf (deputy) because it is allowed even when able to wash. This affects the analogy, but not the nullifiers themselves.
This distinction becomes important later when differentiating from wiping over a splint (jabirah).
4
Apply the rules to a scenario
Take a practical case: a resident puts on khuffs at 10 AM Friday, wipes them at Dhuhr. Later Friday night he breaks wudu. When does the concession end? Answer: at 10 AM Saturday (24 hours) unless he removes the khuff or another nullifier occurs earlier.
If he removes a khuff before time, the state nullifies immediately.

His statement (And it is nullified by the nullifier of wudu'): meaning that every thing that nullifies wudu, whether real or legal, nullifies the masah (wiping), because masah is part of wudu. So what nullifies the whole nullifies the part. And it is reasoned in many books that it is a substitute (badal) for washing, so the nullifier of its original (i.e., washing) nullifies it, like tayammum. But it may be said that it is not a substitute as clarified in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and chosen by some virtuous scholars, because a substitute is not permissible while one is able to do the original, but masah is permissible while able to do the original. Rather the verification is that tayammum is a substitute and masah is a deputy (khalaf). His statement (And removal of the khuff): meaning that removal of the khuff also nullifies it, because the previous event (hadath) has spread to the feet due to the removal of the preventer. And it is not to be objected that if one wipes the head then shaves the hair, he is not required to repeat the masah, because the hair is part of the head, so wiping upon it is wiping upon the head, just as if he wiped upon the khuff then rubbed it off, unlike our case. This is from al-Nihayah. His statement (And expiry of the period): meaning that the expiry of the period also nullifies it due to the hadiths indicating the time limit. And know that removal of the khuff is unlike the two? His statement: (The mashayikh differed on it. He said in al-Manh: I say: The saying of combining should be preferred as a precaution in matters of worship. His statement: (And it may be said that it is not a substitute) will come soon with its explanation of the disagreement, and likewise what contradicts it will come at the end of the chapter, basing upon it the difference between it and wiping over the splint (jabirah). His statement: (Where he is not required to repeat the masah) in...
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the nullifiers (nawaqid) of the legal state of wiping over khuffs. The author comments on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. Three nullifiers are discussed: (1) Anything that nullifies wudu (naqid al-wudu), whether real (e.g., breaking wind, urination) or legal (e.g., sleeping that renders wudu null). The reasoning is that masah is part of wudu, so nullifying the whole nullifies the part. Some scholars consider masah a badal (substitute) for washing, analogizing to tayammum. However, a refinement is noted: masah is not a true badal because it is permitted even when able to wash the foot; rather it is a khalaf (deputy) with a different status. (2) Removing the khuff (naz' al-khuff) nullifies the masah because once the barrier is gone, the previous hadath (minor impurity) is deemed to have extended to the feet. A potential objection is raised: if a person wipes over the head then shaves the hair, they do not need to re-wipe the head. The answer is that hair is part of the head, so wiping on it is wiping on the head, whereas the khuff is not part of the foot. (3) Expiry of the prescribed period (madi al-mudda) — the time limit for which wiping over khuffs is valid (one day and night for a resident, three days and nights for a traveller) — nullifies the state. The text also briefly mentions a difference among mashayikh regarding whether the nullifiers combine or are considered separately, and notes that the issue of masah being a badal will be revisited later in the chapter to distinguish it from wiping over a splint. The passage ends mid-sentence referencing the case of shaving the head.

Key Terms
ناقض الوضوء (naqid al-wudu): Anything that invalidates the state of wudu, such as passing wind, urine, sleep, etc.
نزع الخف (naz' al-khuff): Removing the khuff(s) from the feet, which nullifies the masah state.
مضى المدة (madi al-mudda): The expiry of the time limit for which masah is valid (24 hours for resident, 72 for traveler).
بدل (badal): Substitute; here in the context of masah as a substitute for washing the feet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a nullifier of the state of wiping over khuffs?
A) Passing wind
B) Removing one khuff
C) Expiry of 24 hours for a resident
D) Getting the khuff wet

Key Takeaway
Three clear nullifiers end the concession of wiping over khuffs: any event that breaks wudu, removing a khuff, and the passing of the prescribed time limit.

Scattered Holes in Khuffs: Not Combined
Explaining why scattered holes in khuffs are not combined

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on scattered holes in khuffs and distinguish it from the rulings on impurity and 'awrah exposure based on the difference in 'illa.

Core Idea
Scattered holes in khuffs are not combined because the 'illa is walking ability, not mere exposure.

This lesson unpacks a nuanced ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: scattered small holes in leather socks (khuffs) are not combined to reach the threshold that prevents wiping. The key is understanding the effective cause ('illa) behind the prohibition. We'll see why the same logic does not apply to impurity or exposure of 'awrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on scattered holes
State clearly that scattered holes in each khuff are not combined; the mash is valid as long as each khuff individually does not have holes totaling three fingers' width.
The ruling applies per khuff, not per pair.
2
Identify the 'illa (effective cause)
The passage states that holes prevent mash due to inability to walk a significant distance. Scattered small holes do not hinder walking, so the 'illa is absent.
The 'illa is derived from ma'na (rationale), not direct text.
3
Contrast with impurity and 'awrah
Note that scattered impurity on the body or garment is combined to check if it exceeds the excusable amount (dirham). Similarly, scattered exposure of 'awrah from different limbs is combined to see if the prayer is invalid. The 'illa there is different: being a carrier of impurity or exposing the 'awrah sufficiently.
The distinction is purely based on the different 'illa.
4
Determine the minimum hole size
The smallest hole considered is the size of a needle's entry. Holes smaller than that are ignored by analogy to stitching places.
This is a legal convention (taqdir).
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a scenario with scattered holes, decide whether mash is valid. E.g., two small holes in each khuff, each less than three fingers: mash valid. One khuff with holes totaling three fingers: mash invalid.
The threshold is three fingers per khuff, not combined across both.

In them (the two khuffs) unlike impurity and uncovering. And it is nullified by the nullifier of wudu, and removal of a khuff, and expiry of the time limit. The hole only prevents the permissibility of wiping because the amount of obligatory wiping appears. So if it is scattered in the two khuffs, the amount of obligatory wiping from each of them does not appear. Because the appearance of the amount of obligatory wiping from each of them has no effect in prevention after the possibility of covering a distance with it and continuous walking in it and remaining of some of the top of the foot where the amount of obligatory wiping falls. So the apparent is what the researcher investigated, and Allah knows best. And the smallest hole that is combined is what a needle enters into. As for less than that, it is not, by analogy considering the places of stitching, mentioned in Jami' al-Fiqh. His statement: 'Unlike impurity and uncovering' i.e., unlike scattered impurity, which is combined even if it is scattered in his two khuffs or his garment or his body or his place or collectively. And unlike scattered uncovering of the 'awrah, like the uncovering of something of the woman's private part and something of her back and something of her thigh and something of her shank, which is combined to prevent the permissibility of prayer. Because the preventing factor in 'awrah is the uncovering of the preventing amount, and in impurity it is being a carrier of that preventing amount, and it has been found in both. As for holes in the khuff, the prevention is due to the inability to cover a distance with it, and this meaning is absent when there is not in each khuff the amount of three fingers. To this he referred in al-Hidayah, and what is in it has preceded, and will come in the chapter on conditions of prayer the manner of combining and what is in it. This and it has been mentioned in al-Khulasa that if impurity is on the garment of the worshipper less than a dirham and under his feet less than a dirham, but if combined it would amount to more than a dirham, it is not combined. And it is not hidden that it contradicts what we have presented, and it is mentioned in al-Tabyin and others. And in al-Khulasa also: 'And the hole in the ears of the udhiyah, is it combined? The mashayikh differed about it. And the patches of the garment are combined.' i.e., if in the garment there are patches of silk, and if combined they amount to more than four fingers, then they are combined and wearing it is not permissible, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The main ruling: scattered small holes in two khuffs are not combined to reach the threshold of three fingers that would prevent wiping. The author explains the reasoning: the prevention is due to inability to walk a distance, which is not affected by scattered small holes. He contrasts this with impurity (najasa) and exposure of 'awrah, which are combined even if scattered. For impurity, the preventing factor is being a carrier of more than a dirham in weight; for 'awrah, it is exposure of a limb that is necessary to cover. The text then discusses the minimum size of hole that is considered: the size of a needle's entry. It references al-Hidayah and other works like Jami' al-Fiqh and al-Khulasa. A note is made about silk patches ('alam) on a garment: if scattered but together exceed four fingers, they are combined and wearing such a garment is not permissible. This shows the principle that the rule differs based on the 'illa (effective cause).

Key Terms
خرق (khurq): A hole or tear in the khuff that exposes the foot.
فرض المسح (fard al-mash): The obligatory amount of foot that must be wiped (the front part).
المسح على الخفين (al-mash 'ala al-khuffayn): Wiping over leather socks during wudu.
نجاسة (najasa): Impurity that prevents the validity of prayer if it exceeds the excusable amount.
انكشاف العورة (inkishaf al-'awrah): Exposure of the private parts that invalidates prayer if beyond the permissible limit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, why are scattered holes in khuffs not combined to prevent wiping?
A) Because the holes are less than the size of a dirham.
B) Because the preventing factor is the inability to walk, which is not affected by scattered small holes.
C) Because impurity and 'awrah are not combined either.
D) Because the holes are in different khuffs.

Key Takeaway
Scattered holes in khuffs are not combined to invalidate mash; each khuff is assessed separately based on the ability to walk.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Nullifiers of the Mash: Nawaqid al-Mash (Wiping over Khuffs)
Expounding the nullifiers of mash with proofs and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three nullifiers of the mash and explain how the fear of cold exception changes the ruling.

Core Idea
The mash is nullified by three things: nullifier of wudu, removal of khuff, and expiry of time; but fear of cold turns it into a jabira requiring full wipe.

In this passage, the author details what invalidates the mash over khuffs. The discussion begins with the general principle that any nullifier of wudu also nullifies the mash, then examines the specific cases of removing the khuff and the expiry of the time limit. A key debate arises: is the mash a badal (substitute) or a khalaf (deputy)? Finally, the exception for fear of cold is addressed, where the khuff is treated like a splint (jabira). This lesson will walk you through these rulings and their practical applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three nullifiers
State the three things that nullify the mash: any nullifier of wudu, removing the khuff, and expiry of the time limit. Understand that the first is based on the mash being part of wudu, the second allows the previous hadath to spread, and the third is based on ahadith setting a time limit.
2
Analyze the badal vs khalaf dispute
Recognize the internal Hanafi disagreement: some consider the mash a badal (like tayammum) and others a khalaf. Note that despite the theoretical difference, the practical nullification by nawaqid al-wudu is agreed upon.
The dispute is theoretical; the ruling remains the same.
3
Examine the proof for the time limit
Identify the dalil for the time limit: ahadith that set a fixed duration for wiping over khuffs (e.g., one day for a resident, three for a traveler). Understand that this indicates expiry nullifies the mash.
The ahadith are ahad, so zanni al-thubut, but qati al-dalala.
4
Apply the fear of cold exception
When removing the khuff would harm the foot due to extreme cold, the expiry of time does not immediately nullify the mash. Instead, the khuff is treated like a jabira, and the entire khuff must be wiped (most of it).
This exception is from later fatawa; some earlier scholars had different views.
5
Resolve the practical ruling
Conclude that the mufta bihi is: three nullifiers normally; for fear of cold, wipe the entire khuff like a jabira until the fear ceases. Note that tayammum due to cold is only for janabah, not for minor impurity.
This ruling balances the need for purification with the hardship of cold.

المذكورة هنا فهي في المحدث إذ الجنب لا کشفه
His statement: 'And it is nullified by the nullifier of wudu' meaning the mash is nullified by everything that nullifies wudu, essentially or effectively, because the mash is part of wudu. So what nullifies the whole nullifies the part. It is reasoned in many books that it is a substitute for washing, so it is nullified by the nullifier of its original, like tayammum. But it may be said that it is not a substitute, as stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and chosen by some meritous scholars, because a substitute is not permissible while able to perform the original, and the mash is permissible while able to perform the original. Rather, the verification is that tayammum is a substitute and the mash is a deputy. His statement: 'And removal of a khuff' means it is also nullified by removal of a khuff, because the previous impurity spreads to the feet due to the removal of the barrier. And it does not follow from this that if one wiped his head then shaved his hair, he is not required to repeat the mash, because the hair is part of the head's creation. So wiping over it is wiping over the head, like if he wiped over the khuff then scratched it, unlike our case. Thus in al-Nihaya. His statement: 'And expiry of the time' means it is also nullified by the expiry of the time, due to the ahadith indicating the time limit. And know that removal of the khuff is unlike the two... (continued)... The mash and the expiry of time are not nullifiers in reality; rather, the nullifier is the previous impurity, but the impurity appears upon their occurrence, so nullification is attributed to them metaphorically, as mentioned in tayammum. If it is said: There is no impurity to spread because it was already in the khuff and then removed by the mash, so it does not return except by an external cause like impurity, we say: This is possible but the Law considers the removal of the impurity from the khuff as restricted by a time limit, and we know a similar occurrence in tayammum, where its removal with soil is restricted by a time limit of being unable to use water. And this is appropriate for the description of substitution, which is established in the mash, rather it has two aspects: the mash, though with water, substitutes for the function of washing, and the khuff for the foot. So the restriction by time is required, as a substitute that provides what the original provides, as in tayammum it is restricted by the time it is a substitute providing what the original provides, especially since the context is one of caution. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. His statement: 'If he does not fear losing his foot from cold' means the expiry of time nullifies on the condition that he does not fear harm to his foot from removal. Its implication is that if he fears, he may (keep the khuff on) absolutely without time restriction until that fear ceases, and apparently it is not nullified when there is fear. But this was criticized in Fath al-Qadir that fear of cold has no effect in preventing the spread, just as water does not prevent it. So at most, he should not remove it, but he should not wipe; rather, he should perform tayammum due to fear of cold. And on this, some mashayikh interpreted the mentioned mash as being like a splint (jabira), not like the mash of khuff. So according to this, he should wipe the entire (khuff) or most of it, and this is not understood from the interpreted wording, and it only applies if the name 'splint' applies to a covering that under it there is no site of pain but a healthy limb, but he fears illness from cold. And it necessitates the complete nullification of the issue of tayammum for fear of cold on a limb or its blackening, and it also implies, according to the apparent madhhab of Abu Hanifa, the permissibility of leaving it out entirely, which contradicts the ruling they gave. In Miraj al-Diraya: If the time passes while he fears cold on his foot from removal, he should wipe the entire (khuff) like splints. So it indicates completeness and that it is analogous to splints, not a real splint. As for the complete issue of tayammum, it is restricted to when there is no splint or what is analogous to it. And as for the permissibility of leaving it out entirely, the mufta bihi is its impermissibility in the case of a splint, as will come, and similarly for what is analogous to it. In Fatawa Qadikhan: If... some copies 'return the hair' but the correct is 'wipe'. His statement: 'the description of substitution' contradicts what has passed that it is not a substitute. His statement: 'and it is not understood' said al-Ramli: i.e., the interpretation mentioned. His statement: 'so it indicates completeness and that it is analogous to splints' is a response to the statement of the author of al-Fath that 'it only applies if' etc. And his statement: 'as for the complete issue of tayammum' is a response to his statement 'and it necessitates'. And his statement: 'and as for the permissibility of leaving it out entirely' is a response to his statement 'it also implies'. Al-Nahr said: It is not hidden that there is stiffness in these responses. Some meritous scholars answered the issue of completeness of tayammum by saying that the issue of tayammum for fear of cold is restricted to the janabah (major impurity). As for the hadath (minor impurity) who fears cold, tayammum is not permissible for him by consensus on the most correct view, as has preceded. And the issue of fear of cold mentioned here is in the case of hadath, because the person in janabah does not... [unclear]
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the nullifiers of the mash (wipe) over khuffs. It begins by explaining that any nullifier of wudu (whether real or effective) also nullifies the mash, because the mash is part of wudu. There is a debate whether the mash is a substitute (badal) for washing the feet or a deputy (khalaf). The author leans towards the latter, noting that the mash is permissible even when one can wash, unlike tayammum. Then it discusses the second nullifier: removing the khuff. The reason given is that the previous hadath (impurity) that was prevented from spreading by the khuff now spreads to the feet. The author distinguishes this from wiping the head and then shaving, which does not require repeating the mash. The third nullifier is the expiry of the time limit (one day for a resident, three days for a traveler), based on ahadith. The commentary notes that these are not actual nullifiers but rather the hadath appears at these events. A deep discussion follows about the condition when one fears cold: if removing the khuff would harm the foot due to cold, does the expiry of time still nullify the mash? The text presents views from Fath al-Qadir, Miraj al-Diraya, and others, concluding that in such a case, the khuff is treated like a splint (jabira), and one must wipe the entire khuff (or most of it) rather than just the front part. The issue of tayammum for fear of cold is also addressed, with a resolution that the tayammum permission for fear of cold only applies to janabah, not to minor impurity.

Key Terms
ناقض الوضوء (naqid al-wudu): Anything that invalidates wudu, such as passing wind, urination, etc.
بدل (badal): A substitute that replaces the original when the original cannot be performed.
خلف (khalaf): A deputy that stands in for the original even when the original is possible.
جبيرة (jabirah): A splint or bandage on a wound; here extended to the khuff when fear of cold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if the time for mash expires while the person fears cold on his foot if he removes the khuff?
A) The mash is nullified and he must perform wudu.
B) He must wipe the entire khuff like a jabira, and the mash is not nullified.
C) He must perform tayammum due to the cold.
D) He may leave the khuff on without any further action until the fear subsides.

Key Takeaway
Three things nullify the mash: anything that breaks wudu, removing the khuff, and expiry of the time limit; fear of cold converts the khuff to a jabira requiring full wipe.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Expiry of Wiping Period and the Exception for Fear of Cold
Explanation and proof that expiry does not invalidate wipe, with exception for fear of cold.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the expiry of the wiping period is not the actual invalidator, and apply the exception for fear of cold by distinguishing between tayammum and wiping like a bandage.

Core Idea
Expiry of the period does not invalidate the wipe; only the hadath does, but fear of cold allows indefinite wiping as a bandage.

In this passage, we explore a subtle point in the Hanafi law of wiping over khuffs: the expiry of the wiping period itself does not invalidate the wipe; rather, it is the underlying hadath that becomes manifest. The author then addresses an exceptional case where one fears cold on his foot if he removes the khuffs. This scenario triggers a debate: should he perform tayammum or can he continue wiping? The resolution treats the wipe as analogous to a bandage (jabirah), allowing indefinite wiping with complete coverage. Understanding this ruling requires careful analysis of the concept of substitution (badaliyya) and the limits of analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Main Legal Claim
Recognize that the author asserts that the expiry of the wiping period is not a true invalidator (naqid). The actual invalidator is the hadath that was concealed. The expiry simply allows the hadath to become manifest, so the nullification is metaphorically attributed to the expiry.
This is a key conceptual point: the wipe itself remains valid until a cause of hadath occurs.
2
Trace the Analogy to Tayammum
Follow the qiyas: Just as tayammum is a substitute (badal) for wudu and is restricted to a period (inability to use water), wiping over khuffs is a substitute for washing the feet and is also restricted by a period (24 hours for resident, 72 for traveler). The analogy establishes that the removal of hadath by the substitute is time-limited.
The attribute of badaliyya (substitution) is central to the analogy.
3
Examine the Exception for Fear of Cold
The matn states that expiry invalidates 'if he does not fear loss of his foot from cold.' The implication is that if he does fear, the expiry does not invalidate; he may continue wiping indefinitely until the fear ceases. This is derived from the logical converse (mafhum al-shart).
The condition of fear creates a special dispensation (rukhsah).
4
Understand the Critique and the Bandage Solution
The author of Fath al-Qadir objects: fear of cold does not prevent hadath transmission, so wiping is ineffective; tayammum is needed. In response, some mashayikh reinterpret the wipe as a bandage (jabirah), which requires complete coverage (isti'ab) of the foot and has no time limit. This resolves the tension: the wipe is not a regular substitute but a specific concession akin to a bandage.
Thus, the mufta bihi is complete wiping (isti'ab) without time limit, not tayammum.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi and Practical Consequence
After examining the arguments, the relied-upon position is that the person fearing cold wipes over the entire foot covering (like a bandage) and does not perform tayammum. This rule is specific to minor hadath (hadath asghar). The practical consequence is that he continues his prayers without needing to repeat wudu as long as the fear persists.
This is a case where istihsan (juristic preference) overrides strict analogy.

التكلف .اهـ وأجاب بعض الفضلاء عن مسألة كلية التيمم بأن مسألة التيمم لخوف البرد مقيدة بالجنب، وأما المحدث الخائف من البرد فلا يجوز له التيمم بالإجماع على الأصح كما تقدم. وأما مسألة خوف البرد المذكورة هنا فهي في المحدث إذ الجنب لا كشفه المدة وهو في الصلاة ولا ماء يمضي على الأصح في صلاته إذ لا فائدة في النزع لأنه للغسل ولا ماء خلافاً لمن قال من المشايخ تفسد اهـ. وفي التبيين : القول بالفساد أشبه لسراية الحدث إلى الرجل لأن عدم الماء لا يمنع السراية ثم يتيمم له ويصلي كما لو بقي من أعضائه لمعة ولم يجد ماء يغسلها به فإنه يتيمم فكذا هذا اهـ وتبعه المحقق في فتح القدير .
That the wipe over the khuff and the expiry of the period are not actually invalidators, rather the invalidator is the previous hadath, but the hadath appears when they (the two conditions, i.e., removal and expiry of period) exist, so the nullification is metaphorically attributed to them, as previously in tayammum. If it is said: No hadath can be transmitted because it had resided on the khuff and then ceased by the wipe, so it does not return except by its cause from an external impurity etc., we say: The Law considers the removal of hadath from the khuff as restricted to a period of prevention; then we know the occurrence of its like in tayammum with dust, where it considered its removal by using earth as restricted to a period of its being valid, i.e., the period of inability to use water. That is appropriate for the attribute of substitution, and it is established in wiping, rather it is in it from two aspects: for wiping, though with water, substitutes for the function of washing, and the khuff for the foot, so it is necessary to restrict the removal in it by the period of its being a substitute that benefits what the original benefits, just as in tayammum it is restricted by the period of its being a substitute benefitting what the original benefits, even though the context is one of caution. Thus is it in Fath al-Qadir. His statement: 'If he does not fear the loss of his foot from cold' means the expiry of the period invalidates on condition that he does not fear harm to his foot by removal; its implication is that if he fears, it is permitted for him absolutely without restriction of time until that fear ceases, and its apparent meaning is that it is not invalidated at the time of fear. He critiqued it in Fath al-Qadir by saying that fear of cold has no effect in preventing transmission, just as water does not prevent it. The upshot is that he does not remove, but he does not wipe; rather he performs tayammum due to fear of cold. On this, some mashayikh transmitted an interpretation of the mentioned wiping as a bandage, not like the wiping of the khuff. According to this, he covers what is better or most of it, which is not understood from the interpreted wording, though it is only valid if the term 'bandage' applies to a covering that has no painful area underneath but a healthy limb, except that he fears the onset of illness from cold. This entails the nullification of the entire issue of tayammum due to fear of cold on a limb or its blackening, and it also necessitates, according to the apparent madhhab of Abu Hanifa, permitting leaving it completely, contrary to what their giving the ruling of the issue indicates. In Miraj al-Dirayah: If the period passes while he fears cold on his foot due to removal, he covers the whole with wiping like bandages. So it indicates complete coverage and that it is annexed to bandages, not a true bandage. As for the entire issue of tayammum, it is specific to when he does not have a bandage or what is annexed to it. As for permitting leaving it completely, the mufta bihi is its non-existence in the bandage, as will come, similarly in the annexed. In Fatawa Qadikhan: ... His statement: (the attribute of substitution) contradicts what passed that it is not a substitute. His statement: (and it is not understood) al-Ramli said: meaning the mentioned interpretation. His statement: (so it indicates complete coverage and that it is annexed to bandages, etc.) is a response to the statement of the author of Fath that 'though it is only valid if ...' etc. And his statement: (and as for the entire issue of tayammum, etc.) is a response to his statement: 'it entails' etc. And his statement: (and as for permitting leaving it completely, etc.) is a response to his statement: 'it necessitates' etc. He said in al-Nahr: The effort in these responses is not hidden. One of the virtuous scholars responded to the issue of the entire tayammum by saying that the issue of tayammum due to fear of cold is restricted to the junub; as for the one with minor hadath who fears cold, tayammum is not permitted for him by consensus on the correct view as previously. And the issue of fear of cold mentioned here is about the one with minor hadath, for the junub does not ... the period while he is in prayer and there is no water passes on the correct view in his prayer, since there is no benefit in removal because it is for washing and there is no water, contrary to those mashayikh who said it becomes invalid. In al-Tabyin: The saying that it is invalid is more appropriate due to the transmission of hadath to the foot, because lack of water does not prevent transmission, then he performs tayammum for it and prays, just as if a part of his limbs remained (unwashed) and he found no water to wash it, he performs tayammum; so this is similar. The muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir followed him.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage begins by addressing the nature of the expiry of the wiping period (muddat al-mash) over khuffs. The author explains that the expiry itself is not the true invalidator; rather, it is the hadath (impurity) that was already present but concealed by the wipe. The expiry merely allows the hadath to become manifest. This is supported by an analogy (qiyas) to tayammum, where the allowance to use dust is restricted by the period of inability to use water. Since wiping over khuffs is a substitute (badal) for washing the feet, it must also be limited by a period, during which the concealment of hadath is effective. The text then discusses the condition mentioned in the matn: if one does not fear loss of his foot from cold, the expiry invalidates the wipe. If he does fear, he may continue wiping indefinitely until the fear subsides. However, this was critiqued by the author of Fath al-Qadir, who argued that fear of cold does not prevent the transmission of hadath, and thus the better course is to perform tayammum instead. In response, some scholars interpreted the 'wipe' in this case as a metaphorical bandage (jabirah), which requires covering the entire foot (isti'ab) without time restriction. The text assesses these views, noting that the correct position is that it is annexed to the ruling of bandages, not actual bandages, and thus requires complete wiping, not tayammum. The commentary also cites multiple authorities, including Miraj al-Dirayah and Fatawa Qadikhan, to support the view that wiping is the correct course. The passage concludes with a response to the objection about tayammum, stating that the tayammum due to cold is specific to the junub (major impurity), whereas the issue here concerns one with minor hadath, for whom tayammum is not permitted by consensus. Thus, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is to wipe completely, like a bandage.

Key Terms
البدلية (al-badaliyya): The attribute of being a substitute (badal); here it refers to the wiping over khuffs as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.
الجبيرة (al-jabirah): A bandage or splint; legally, a covering over a wound that may be wiped over in purification. Here, the wiping over khuffs when fearing cold is treated like a jabirah, requiring complete coverage (isti'ab) without time limit.
الاستيعاب (al-isti'ab): Complete coverage; in the context of wiping over a bandage, it means wiping the entire surface of the covering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct Hanafi ruling for a person who fears that removing his khuffs will harm his foot due to cold?
A) He must remove them and perform tayammum.
B) He must remove them and wash his feet with water if available.
C) He may continue wiping over his khuffs with complete coverage like a bandage, without time limit.
D) He must remove them and pray without any purification, since water and tayammum are unavailable.

Key Takeaway
Expiry of the wiping period does not invalidate wudu; the hadath does, but when fearing cold, the wipe is treated like a bandage and continues indefinitely.

Rulings After Removing Khuffs and Exposure Nullification
Two fiqh rulings on khuff: post-removal washing and exposure nullification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rulings after khuff removal and expiry of the wipe period, and explain the Hanafi ikhtilaf on the amount of foot exposure that nullifies the wipe.

Core Idea
After removing khuffs, only wash feet; the wipe is invalidated if the remaining covered area is less than the fard measure.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies two practical questions for those performing masah over khuffs. First, if the khuff is removed or the period expires, do you need to repeat the entire wudu? The answer is no—only the feet need washing because the hadath affected only the feet and muwalat is not a condition. Second, if part of the foot becomes exposed while wiping, at what point does the wipe become invalid? There is a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school, and the relied-upon view is explained.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers two distinct rulings: (a) what to do after khuff removal or expiry of the wipe period, and (b) how much foot exposure nullifies the wipe.
Note that the first ruling applies when the khuff is removed or the period ends, not during the period.
2
Understand the reasoning for the first ruling
After removal or expiry, only washing the feet is required because the hadath only affected the feet, and the other limbs were already washed. The missing element is muwalat (continuity), which is not a condition (shart) but a sunnah in the Hanafi school.
This contrasts with schools that consider muwalat obligatory.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on exposure
Abu Yusuf holds that exposure of more than half of the foot invalidates the wipe. Muhammad holds that the wipe is invalidated if the remaining covered part is less than the obligatory area (three fingers in length). Most mashayikh follow Muhammad's view.
The relied-upon position in al-Hidayah is Muhammad's view.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The correct view for fatwa is Muhammad's: the wipe becomes invalid if the exposed part is such that the remaining covered area is less than three fingers (the minimum fard area for wiping).
This is based on the weight of the majority of later scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وبعدهما غسل رجليه فقط) أي بعد النزع ومضي المدة غسل رجليه فقط وليس عليه إعادة بقية الوضوء إذا كان على وضوء لأن الحدث السابق وهو الذي حل بقدمه وقد غسل بعده سائر الأعضاء وبقيت القدمان فقط فلا يجب عليه إلا غسلهما، ولا معنى لغسل الأعضاء المغسولة ثانياً لأن الفائت الموالاة وهي ليست بشرط في الوضوء عندنا، وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى أن الماسح على الخف إذا أحدث فانصرف ليتوضأ فانقضت مدة مسحه بطلت صلاته على الصحيح. قوله ( وخروج أكثر القدم نزع وهو الصحيح كذا في الهداية وهو قول أبي يوسف، وعنه بخروج نصفه، وعن محمد إن كان الباقي قدر محل الفرض أعني ثلاثة أصابع اليد طويلاً لا ينتقض وإلا انتقض وعليه أكثر المشايخ كذا في الكافي والمعراج وهو
His statement: 'And after both, washing his two feet only' means after removal and the expiry of the period, he washes his two feet only, and he does not have to repeat the rest of the wudu if he had wudu, because the previous hadath is what had affected his foot, and after that he washed the other limbs, and only the two feet remained, so only their washing is obligatory. There is no meaning to washing the already-washed limbs a second time because what was lost is continuity (muwalat), and it is not a condition in wudu in our madhhab. It will come, Allah willing, that the one who wiped over the khuff, if he had a hadath and turned to perform wudu, and his wiping period expired, his prayer is invalid on the correct view. His statement: 'And exposure of most of the foot is removal, and it is the correct view' – thus in al-Hidayah, and it is the saying of Abu Yusuf. From him: by exposure of half of it. And from Muhammad: if the remaining part is the measure of the obligatory area, i.e., three fingers of the hand in length, it is not invalidated; otherwise it is invalidated. And most mashayikh follow this, as in al-Kafi and al-Mi'raj.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct rulings from the commentary on the matn. First, it explains that after the removal of the khuffs and the expiry of the period, the person only needs to wash his feet, not repeat the entire wudu. The reasoning is that the hadath (impurity) had only affected the feet, and since the other limbs were already washed, the only element that was omitted is the continuity (muwalat) between washing the parts of wudu. According to the Hanafi school, muwalat is a sunnah, not a condition (shart), so its omission does not invalidate the wudu; only the obligatory washing of the feet remains. The commentary also notes a future ruling about a person who had a hadath and then began wudu but the wiping period expired during that time, causing his prayer to become invalid (on the correct view). Second, the passage discusses the ruling on how much exposure of the foot from the khuff nullifies the wipe. The relied-upon position (from al-Hidayah) is that exposing most of the foot (more than half) constitutes removal, which ends the validity of the wipe. This is the view of Abu Yusuf. There is also a transmission from him that exposing half does it. According to Muhammad, the test is whether the remaining covered part is less than the obligatory area (which is about three fingers in length); if the uncovered part is equal to or larger than that, the wipe is invalidated. Most mashayikh adopt Muhammad's view. This ikhtilaf among the imams affects practical application.

Key Terms
الموالاة (al-muwalat): Continuity; in wudu, it means washing the limbs consecutively without significant delay. Here, it is noted that in the Hanafi school, muwalat is not a condition (shart) but a sunnah, so its omission does not necessitate repeating the wudu.
النزع (al-naz'): Removing the khuff from the foot. In the context of masah al-khuff, removal ends the validity of the wipe, and the ruling depends on the extent of exposure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, how much of the foot must be exposed from the khuff to invalidate the wipe?
A) Any amount of exposure invalidates the wipe.
B) More than half of the foot must be exposed.
C) The wipe is invalidated if the remaining covered part is less than three fingers in length (the measure of the fard area).
D) Exposure does not invalidate the wipe; only complete removal does.

Key Takeaway
After khuff removal/expiry, only wash feet; the wipe is invalidated if the remaining covered foot area is less than the fard measure of three fingers.

The Preponderant View: Wiping Like a Bandage over Tayammum
Super-commentary reinforcing wiping over tayammum with comprehensive citations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the final preponderant Hanafi ruling for a person who fears loss of feet from cold when removing khuffs, and explain why wiping like a bandage is preferred over tayammum.

Core Idea
Wiping completely like a bandage (isti'ab) without time limit is the rajih view, not tayammum.

After earlier debates on whether one should perform tayammum or wipe when fearing cold, this super-commentary settles the matter. Al-Ramli and later authorities cite numerous reliable texts confirming that the correct ruling is to wipe the entire foot like a bandage, with no time limit. This lesson walks through the evidence and the tarjih process.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
The core issue: for a person who fears losing his feet from cold if he removes his khuffs, should he perform tayammum or wipe over the khuffs? The passage initially mentions an opinion favoring tayammum (from al-Halabi and Ibn al-Humam).
2
Locate the primary texts
Al-Ramli states that the apparent meaning of core Hanafi texts like al-Kanz and al-Hidayah supports wiping, not tayammum. This sets the stage for tarjih.
3
Analyze the meaning of 'wiping'
Some scholars clarify that 'wiping' here means complete wiping (isti'ab) like a bandage, not the usual timed wipe. This is confirmed by explicit statements in al-Mujtaba, al-Zayla'i, and others.
4
Weigh the cumulative evidence
The passage lists over a dozen authorities (e.g., Miraj al-Diraya, Imdad al-Fattah, Sharh al-Haskafi) that explicitly adopt the wiping view without mentioning tayammum. This weight makes wiping the preponderant (rajih) position.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The super-commentary concludes that the relied-upon fatwa is wiping completely like a bandage, without time limit. This is the operative ruling for a mufti today.
