وفي التبيين القول بالفساد أشبه) قال الرملي قال العلامة الحلبي في شرح منية المصلي والذي يظهر أن الصحيح هو القول بالفساد ولا نسلم أن التيمم لا حظ للرجلين فيه بل هو طهارة لجميع الأعضاء وإن كان محله عضوين كما أن الوضوء طهارة لجميعها وإن كان محله أربعة أعضاء وكذا لو خاف إن نزعهما ذهاب رجليه من البرد فإنه يتيمم ولا يمسح على الخفين على ما حققه الشيخ كمال الدين بن الهمام وقد ذكرناه في الشرح اهـ. أي ذكره في الشرح الكبير لها. وأقول : ظاهر المتون كالكنز والهداية وغيرهما المسح لا التيمم في مسألة خوف ذهاب رجليه وليس الترجيح بالهين في ذلك فتأمل. وازداد نقلاً في كلامهم يظهر لك الراجح من المرجوح . اهـ كلام الرملي قال بعض الفضلاء نعم ظاهر المتون المسح لكن يراد بالمسح أن يمسح على جميعه كالجبيرة ولا يتوقت ويدل على ذلك صريح كلامهم في غير كتاب من الكتب المعتبرة قال في المجتبى : فإن مضت وهو يخاف البرد على رجليه بالنزع يستوعب المسح كالجبائر ويصلي وكذا في الزيلعي والإيضاح والحاوي ومختارات النوازل .اهـ. قلت: وكذا في معراج الدراية وإمداد الفتاح وشرحي العلامة الحصكفي على الملتقى والتنوير، فعلم بهذه النقول أن الراجح المسح لا التيمم. ونقله في السراج عن المشكل ومنلا خسرو عن الكافي وعيون المذاهب والقهستاني الخلاصة وفي الفتح عن جوامع الفقه والمحيط ولم يذكروا التيمم والله تعالى أعلم. قوله : (لأن الفائت الموالاة وهي ليست بشرط في الوضوء قال بعض محشي صدر الشريعة: اعلم أنه ينبغي أن يسن غسل الباقي أيضاً مراعاة للسنة أعني الولاء ولكن عبارته لا تفيد ذلك كما لا يخفى فتدبر اهـ. وقد يقال : قول المؤلف وليس عليه إعادة بقية الوضوء كما هو عبارة الهداية يشير إلى نفي الوجوب كما صرح به المؤلف ثانياً بقوله فلا يجب عليه إلا غسلهما وهو صادق بسنية غسل الباقي مراعاة عن
And in al-Tabyin: 'The saying that it is invalid is more appropriate' – al-Ramli said: al-Allama al-Halabi said in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: 'What appears is that the correct view is the saying of invalidity, and we do not concede that tayammum has no share for the feet; rather, it is purity for all limbs even though its place is two limbs, just as wudu is purity for all limbs even though its place is four limbs. Similarly, if he fears that removing them would cause loss of his feet from cold, he performs tayammum and does not wipe over the khuffs, according to what Shaykh Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam verified, and we have mentioned it in the commentary.' That is, he mentioned it in the large commentary. I (al-Ramli) say: The apparent meaning of the texts like al-Kanz and al-Hidayah and others is wiping, not tayammum, in the issue of fear of loss of his feet, and the tarjih is not easy in that, so contemplate. And more transmission in their statements will show you the preponderant from the preponderated. The end of al-Ramli's words. Some virtuous scholars said: Yes, the apparent meaning of the texts is wiping, but what is meant by wiping is that he wipes over all of it like a bandage, and it is not restricted by time, and the explicit statements of their books from the reliable books indicate that. He said in al-Mujtaba: 'If the period passes while he fears cold on his feet due to removal, he covers the whole with wiping like bandages and prays.' Similarly in al-Zayla'i, al-Idah, al-Hawi, and Mukhtarat al-Nawazil. I (the author) said: Similarly in Miraj al-Diraya, Imdad al-Fattah, and the two commentaries of al-Allama al-Haskafi on al-Multaqa and al-Tanwir. So by these transmissions it becomes known that the preponderant is wiping, not tayammum. It is transmitted in al-Siraj from al-Mushkil and Mulla Khusraw from al-Kafi, Uyun al-Madha'ib, and al-Qahistani, al-Khulasa, and in al-Fath from Jawami' al-Fiqh and al-Muhit, and they did not mention tayammum. And Allah knows best. His statement: (because what was lost is continuity (muwalat), and it is not a condition in wudu) – some on the hashya of Sadr al-Shari'a said: 'Know that it is desirable (yannabaghi) to also wash the remaining (limbs) out of consideration for the sunnah, i.e., continuity, but his phrase does not impart that, as is not hidden, so ponder.' And it may be said: The author's statement 'and he does not have to repeat the rest of the wudu' as is the phrase in al-Hidayah indicates the negation of obligation, as the author later made clear by his saying 'so only their washing is obligatory,' and it is true that washing the rest is sunnah out of consideration.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This final section serves as a super-commentary that reinforces the correct position on the fear-of-cold issue after the earlier debates. It begins by quoting al-Tabyin, which supports the view of invalidity (i.e., the wipe is invalid and tayammum is required), as held by al-Halabi and Ibn al-Humam. However, al-Ramli responds that the apparent meaning of the central texts (such as al-Kanz and al-Hidayah) is wiping, not tayammum. He then notes that additional transmitted sources clarify that the intended 'wiping' in these texts means complete wiping like a bandage, not the regular timed wipe. The passage then lists numerous authoritative works (al-Mujtaba, al-Zayla'i, etc.) that explicitly confirm the ruling: one should cover the entire foot with wiping like a bandage and pray, without time restriction. The cumulative weight of these sources leads to the conclusion that the preponderant (rajih) view is wiping, not tayammum. The passage then turns to a separate issue regarding the earlier ruling about washing only feet after removal. A marginal note from a commentator on Sadr al-Shari'a suggests that it is sunnah to also wash the other limbs out of consideration for continuity (muwalat), though the author's phrase only negates obligation. The text ends with a discussion of whether 'washing the rest' is sunnah. This final part serves as a subtle refinement of the earlier ruling, confirming that while only the feet are obligatory, washing the other limbs is recommended to follow the sunnah of continuity.

Key Terms
الراجح (al-rajih): The preponderant or preferred view after weighing evidence. Here, it refers to the view that one should wipe completely like a bandage, not perform tayammum.
الموالاة (al-muwalat): Continuity in wudu; discussed here as a sunnah, not a condition. The commentary clarifies that while only feet are obligatory, it is sunnah to wash the other limbs to observe muwalat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must perform tayammum because the wipe is invalid.

C) He must wipe completely over the khuffs like a bandage, without time limit, and this is the preferred view.

Key Takeaway
When fear of cold prevents removing khuffs, the preponderant Hanafi view is to wipe completely like a bandage without time limit, as confirmed by numerous later authorities.

Ruling on Prayer When Khuff Period Expires Without Water
Intra-Hanafi dispute on continuation of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the khuff period expires during prayer with no water, and evaluate the opposing view from al-Tabyeen.

Core Idea
If khuff period expires during prayer with no water, the correct view is to continue the prayer.

This lesson presents a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person in prayer whose khuff wiping period expires while water is unavailable. The preferred opinion (al-asahh) holds that the prayer continues, while some mashayikh argue for invalidation by analogy to tayammum. We will examine the reasoning behind both positions and identify the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and legal question
The person is in prayer and the duration of wiping over khuffs expires, with no water available. The question is whether the prayer becomes invalid.
2
State the asahh view and its rationale
The correct view (al-asahh) is that the prayer continues. The rationale is that removing the khuff serves no purpose because it is for washing, and there is no water.
The term 'al-asahh' indicates the preferred position within the madhhab.
3
Present the opposing view from al-Tabyeen
Some Hanafi mashayikh, supported by al-Tabyeen, hold that the prayer becomes invalid. Their evidence: the hadath spreads to the foot, and lack of water does not prevent spread; by analogy, tayammum is needed, similar to a dry limb.
This view is quoted and followed by al-Tahtawi in Fath al-Qadir.
4
Compare the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical consequence (thamarah) is whether the person must break the prayer and perform tayammum or continue. The tarjih (preferred ruling) according to al-Bahr al-Raiq is continuation, as it is 'ala al-asahh', though the opposing view is also recorded. The mufta bihi is continuation.
The preference is based on lack of benefit in removal when no water exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة - باب المسح على الخفين : المدة وهو في الصلاة ولا ماء يمضي على الأصح في صلاته إذ لا فائدة في النزع لأنه للغسل ولا ماء خلافاً لمن قال من المشايخ تفسد اهـ. وفي التبيين : القول بالفساد أشبه لسراية الحدث إلى الرجل لأن عدم الماء لا يمنع السراية ثم يتيمم له ويصلي كما لو بقي من أعضائه لمعة ولم يجد ماء يغسلها به فإنه يتيمم فكذا هذا اهـ وتبعه المحقق في فتح القدير .
The duration and he is in prayer and there is no water: he continues on the correct view in his prayer since there is no benefit in removing (the khuff) because it (removal) is for washing and there is no water, contrary to those from the mashayikh who said it becomes invalid. And in al-Tabyeen: the statement of invalidity is more appropriate because the hadath spreads to the foot, and the lack of water does not prevent the spread, then he does tayammum for it and prays, just as if there remained from his limbs a patch and he did not find water to wash it, he does tayammum; likewise this. And al-Tahtawi followed him in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where a person is in prayer and the duration of wiping over khuffs expires, and there is no water available. There is an ikhtilaf: the correct view (asah) is that he continues his prayer, because removing the khuff serves no purpose when there is no water. However, some mashayikh hold that the prayer becomes invalid. The author of al-Tabyeen supports the latter view by analogy: if a limb has a wet patch and no water, one does tayammum; similarly, the hadath has spread to the foot and tayammum is needed, so the prayer should be invalidated. This is quoted and accepted by al-Tahtawi in Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
الأصح (al-asahh): The most correct view, here indicating the preferred position among the Hanafi school.
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity, specifically the state that invalidates wudu, which spreads to the foot after khuff expiration.
النزع (al-naz'): Removing the khuff (leather socks) from the feet.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with earth performed when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Break the prayer and remove the khuffs.
B) Continue the prayer because removing the khuffs serves no purpose.
C) Do tayammum during the prayer.
D) Repeat the prayer later.

Key Takeaway
When khuff period expires during prayer with no water, the correct Hanafi view is to continue the prayer, as removal serves no purpose.

After Removal or Expiry of Khuff: Washing Only the Feet
Ruling with aqli proof about post-khuff wudu requirements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for wudu after khuff expiry or removal and explain why only the feet require washing based on the Hanafi position that muwalat is not a condition.

Core Idea
After khuff expiry or removal, only the feet need washing because muwalat is not a condition.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: a person who has been wiping over khuffs (leather socks) during wudu. When the wiping period expires or the khuffs are removed, only the feet must be washed; the rest of the wudu remains valid. The reasoning hinges on the Hanafi principle that sequential continuity (muwalat) is not a condition for wudu, contrary to the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing wudu after the khuff period has expired or after removing the khuffs. The ruling is that only the feet need to be washed; the rest of the limbs already washed remain valid.
The passage explicitly says 'wash only his two feet' and 'he is not required to repeat the rest of the wudu'.
2
Understand the reasoning: previous hadath
The hadath (ritual impurity) that invalidated wudu occurred only on the feet. The other limbs were already washed after that hadath, so they remain pure. Only the feet need washing to remove the hadath.
The passage states: 'the previous hadath which occurred to his foot—and he has washed the other limbs after that'.
3
Recognize the role of muwalat (sequential continuity)
The only thing lost by the interruption is muwalat (washing limbs in sequence without delay). In the Hanafi school, muwalat is not a condition for wudu; it is sunnah. Therefore, the interruption does not nullify the previous washes.
The passage explicitly says: 'what was lost was muwalat, and it is not a condition in wudu according to us.'
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school considers muwalat a condition. In this scenario, they would require a complete new wudu because the sequence was broken. The Hanafi position is based on a different usul principle.
The source notes that this is a point of ikhtilaf between the schools.
5
Apply the ruling to a related scenario
The passage also mentions that if one is in prayer and the wiping period expires while making wudu, the prayer becomes invalid. This shows the legal effect of the expiry during an act of worship.
This is a corollary: the prayer is invalid because the condition for wiping (maskh) no longer exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وبعدهما غسل رجليه فقط) أي بعد النزع ومضي المدة غسل رجليه فقط وليس عليه إعادة بقية الوضوء إذا كان على وضوء لأن الحدث السابق وهو الذي حل بقدمه وقد غسل بعده سائر الأعضاء وبقيت القدمان فقط فلا يجب عليه إلا غسلهما، ولا معنى لغسل الأعضاء المغسولة ثانياً لأن الفائت الموالاة وهي ليست بشرط في الوضوء عندنا، وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى أن الماسح على الخف إذا أحدث فانصرف ليتوضأ فانقضت مدة مسحه بطلت صلاته على الصحيح.
His statement: 'And after them two, washing only his two feet' i.e., after removal and expiry of the duration, he washes only his two feet, and he is not required to repeat the rest of the wudu if he was in a state of wudu, because the previous hadath which occurred to his foot—and he has washed the other limbs after that and only the two feet remain—so it is only obligatory for him to wash them. And there is no meaning in washing the already-washed limbs a second time because what was lost was muwalat (sequential continuity), and it is not a condition in wudu according to us. And it will come, God willing, that the person wiping over khuffs, if he invalidates his wudu and turns to perform wudu, and then the duration of his wiping expires, his prayer becomes invalid according to the correct view.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This is a ruling from the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining that when a person has been wiping over khuffs and then either removes them or the time period expires, he is only required to wash his feet when making wudu again. He does not need to repeat washing the other limbs because the previous hadath only affected the feet (since the head, hands, etc. were already washed after that hadath or the wudu was intact). The basis is that the sequence (muwalat) is not a condition for the validity of wudu in the Hanafi school, so the interruption does not require starting over. The passage also references a later discussion that if one was in prayer and the period expires while making wudu, the prayer is invalidated (on the correct view).

Key Terms
الموالاة (al-muwalāt): Sequential continuity without undue delay between washing limbs in wudu. It is not a condition for wudu in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wash the entire body in wudu order.
B) Wash only the feet.
C) Wash the feet and face.
D) Perform tayammum.

Key Takeaway
After khuff expiry or removal, only the feet need washing because muwalat is not a condition for wudu in the Hanafi school.

Emerging Foot from Khuff: Intra-Hanafi Thresholds
Presents three opinions on what quantity of foot exiting the khuff breaks the mash

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on the quantity of foot that invalidates the mash and explain the practical difference between them.

Core Idea
The mash over khuffs is invalidated when most of the foot emerges, but other criteria exist.

When a person wearing khuffs partially exposes his foot, does his wiping (mash) become invalid? The early Hanafi imams disagreed on the threshold. This lesson unpacks the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, along with the practical test of walking ability. Understanding this dispute equips you to apply the correct ruling in daily practice.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Define the problem: how much foot must emerge from the khuff to nullify the mash? This is a dispute among the Hanafi imams.
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's two narrations
Note that from Abu Yusuf we have two reports: most of the foot (akthar al-qadam) and half of the foot. The first is declared the correct view (al-sahih) in al-Hidayah.
Most of the foot is the relied-upon view for fatwa.
3
Identify Muhammad's criterion
Muhammad al-Shaybani focuses on the remaining portion inside: if what remains is less than the fard area (three fingers of the hand in length), the mash is invalid; otherwise it remains valid.
Most later mashayikh adopted this view.
4
Identify Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa said that invalidating emergence is the exit of most of the heel (akthar al-aqib) when done intentionally. If the heel naturally lifts and returns due to a wide khuff, the mash is not invalidated.
He also considers the lame person whose heel is constantly raised.
5
Apply the practical test
Some scholars recommended a walking test (istimsha): if the person can walk normally, the mash remains; otherwise it invalidates. This test aligns with Abu Yusuf's criterion of most of the foot.
The passage endorses this test as sound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وخروج أكثر القدم نزع وهو الصحيح كذا في الهداية وهو قول أبي يوسف، وعنه بخروج نصفه، وعن محمد إن كان الباقي قدر محل الفرض أعني ثلاثة أصابع اليد طويلاً لا ينتقض وإلا انتقض وعليه أكثر المشايخ كذا في الكافي والمعراج وهو لم يخف ذهاب رجله من البرد وبعدهما غسل رجليه فقط وخروج أكثر القدم نزع ولو الصحيح. كذا في النصاب. وقال أبو حنيفة : إن خرج أكثر العقب يعني إذا أخرجه قاصداً إخراج الرجل بطل المسح حتى لو بدا له إعادتها فأعادها لا يجوز المسح، وكذا لو كان أعرج يمشي على صدور قدميه وقد ارتفع عقبه عن موضع عقب الخف إلى الساق لا يمسح ، أما لو كان الخف واسعاً يرتفع العقب برفع الرجل إلى الساق ويعود بوضعها فإنه يجوز له المسح. كذا في فتح القدير. وقيده في المحيط بأنه يبقى فيه مقدار ثلاثة أصابع. وفي البدائع : وقال بعض مشايخنا : يستمشي فإن أمكنه المشي المعتاد يبقى المسح وإلا ينتقض، وهو موافق لقول أبي يوسف وهو اعتبار أكثر القدم ولا بأس بالاعتماد عليه لأن القصد من لبس الخف هو المشي فإذا تعذر المشي عدم اللبس فيما قصد له ولأن للأكثر حكم الكل اهـ. وهذا تصريح هذا القول وهو به جدير فإن الحكم إذا كان دائراً مع الأصل وجوداً وعدماً كان بترجيح الاعتبار له وحينئذ يظهر أن ما قاله أبو حنيفة صحيح متجه لأن بقاء العقب أو أكثرها في الساق يتعذر معه المداومة على المشي المعتاد مقدار ما يقطع به المسافة بواسطة ما فيه من الدوس على نفس الساق، وقد صرح بهذا في فتح القدير.
His statement: (And exit of most of the foot is [cause of] removal, and it is the correct view), thus in al-Hidayah, and it is the saying of Abu Yusuf. And from him (another narration): by exit of half of it. And from Muhammad: if the remaining (in the khuff) is the amount of the fard place, meaning three fingers of the hand in length, then it does not invalidate; otherwise it invalidates. And upon this are most of the mashayikh, thus in al-Kafi and al-Mi'raj. And he did not fear the loss of his foot from cold, and after them two, washing only his two feet, and exit of most of the foot is removal, and the correct one. Thus in al-Nisab. And Abu Hanifa said: If most of the heel exits—meaning if he brings it out intentionally to take out the foot—then the mash is invalidated; even if he intends to return it and returns it, the mash is not permissible. Likewise, if he is lame and walks on the fronts of his feet and his heel is raised from the place of the heel of the khuff to the leg, he does not wipe. But if the khuff is wide, the heel rises when lifting the foot to the leg and returns when placing it, then wiping is permissible for him. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And he restricted it in al-Muhit by that there remains in it the amount of three fingers. And in al-Bada'i: Some of our mashayikh said: Let him try to walk: if he can walk normally, the mash remains; otherwise it invalidates. And this is in agreement with the statement of Abu Yusuf, which is consideration of most of the foot, and there is no harm in relying upon it because the purpose of wearing the khuff is walking, so if walking becomes difficult, the wearing is nullified in terms of its intended purpose; and because the majority has the ruling of the whole. And this is a clear statement of this view and it is worthy of it, for when the ruling revolves around the foundation in existence and non-existence, then preference is given to considering it. And thus it becomes evident that what Abu Hanifa said is correct and sound, because the remaining of the heel or most of it in the leg makes it impossible to maintain normal walking for the distance, due to stepping on the leg itself. And this is expounded in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage details a major intra-madhhab dispute on what constitutes a nullification of the mash when part of the foot emerges from the khuff. The issue is: how much must come out for the mash to become invalid? The base text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states 'exit of most of the foot' is the invalidator, which is identified as the view of Abu Yusuf. Another narration from Abu Yusuf says half. Muhammad al-Shaybani says the determining factor is whether the remaining part inside is less than the fard area of washing (three fingers of the hand). Abu Hanifa's view is presented separately: the exit of most of the heel (if intentionally brought out) invalidates, but if the khuff is so wide that the heel naturally lifts and returns during walking, it does not invalidate. The passage then mentions a practical test (istimsha): if the person can walk normally, the mash remains. This test aligns with Abu Yusuf's criterion of most of the foot. The author of Fath al-Qadir supports Abu Hanifa's view because the difficulty of walking indicates the khuff is no longer serving its purpose. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated here, but the text suggests Abu Hanifa's view is logically sound. The passage also mentions that if one foot emerges, the other must also be removed to avoid combining original (washing) and substitute (mash).

Key Terms
العقب (al-'aqib): The heel of the foot; for Abu Hanifa, the exit of most of the heel from the khuff invalidates the mash.
الاستمشاء (al-istimshā'): Trying to walk normally to test if the khuff is still usable; if walking is possible, the mash remains valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following describes the threshold for invalidation of wiping over khuffs due to part of the foot emerging?
A) Any part of the foot emerging, no matter how small.
B) The entire foot must emerge.
C) Most of the foot must emerge (view of Abu Yusuf).
D) Only the heel must emerge.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the correct and relied-upon view is that most of the foot must emerge from the khuff to invalidate the mash, though other opinions exist based on different criteria.

Invalidation of Masah by Foot Removal: Heel or Majority?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nawaqid al-masah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the invalidation of masah by removal of the foot and state the mufta bihi position based on walking ability.

Core Idea
Masah on khuff is invalidated if removal of the foot prevents normal walking — majority or heel, whichever disrupts the purpose.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles a practical question: when does removing your foot from the khuff break your wudu? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement, but the later masters reconcile the positions by focusing on the purpose of the khuff — walking. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the principle that legal rules revolve with their underlying purposes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
What exactly is the point of difference? Abu Hanifa considers exit of the heel (most of it) as invalidating masah, while Abu Yusuf considers exit of the majority of the foot.
The 'heel' ('aqib) is a specific part; the 'majority' (akthar) refers to more than half of the entire foot.
2
State each position and its proof
Abu Hanifa: invalidation by exit of heel. His reasoning focuses on the heel's crucial role in walking — if the heel is out, walking is impaired. Abu Yusuf: invalidation by exit of majority. He uses the principle 'al-akthar yanzi manzilat al-kull' (the majority takes the ruling of the whole).
Both are within the Hanafi school; this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
3
Understand the reconciliation
Later scholars harmonize by using a common criterion: the ability to walk normally. If the foot's exit (whether heel or majority) prevents normal walking, masah is invalidated; otherwise, it remains.
This teleological approach (maqasid al-shariah) aligns with the purpose of wearing khuffs.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Yusuf (invalidation by majority), but conditioned by walking ability. This is preferred because it is more comprehensive and directly tied to the purpose.
Some later texts consider both views valid, but the fatwa is for Abu Yusuf's view.
5
Apply to a scenario
Test your understanding: If a person's heel exits but he can still walk normally, his masah remains valid. If the majority exits and he cannot walk normally, his masah is invalid.
This clarifies the practical thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He did not fear the loss of his foot from cold, and after them both, washing his feet only, and the exit of the majority of the foot is removal, and it is correct. Thus in al-Nisab. And Abu Hanifa said: If the majority of the heel comes out, meaning when he intentionally removes the foot, the masah is invalidated, so even if he intends to return it and returns it, masah is not permissible. Similarly, if he is lame and walks on the fronts of his feet and his heel rises from the place of the heel of the khuff to the shin, he does not wipe. This is an explicit statement of this view, and it is worthy, because if the ruling revolves with the essence in existence and non-existence, it is preferable to give consideration to it. Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the invalidators (nawaqid) of wiping over khuffs, specifically the removal of the foot. It presents a dispute within the Hanafi school. Abu Hanifa holds that if the heel (or most of it) comes out, the masah is invalidated, even if the foot is reinserted. Abu Yusuf considers the majority of the foot as the criterion. However, the commentary reconciles the views by focusing on the purpose of wearing khuffs: walking. If removing the foot prevents normal walking, masah is invalid; otherwise, it remains. The text also discusses related issues: the ruling for a lame person, the case of a wide khuff, and whether washing the foot invalidates masah (the correct view is that washing the majority does invalidate, but al-Siraj al-Wahhaj holds it does not). Finally, it summarizes that there are four invalidators, with a fifth (exit of prayer time for those with excuse) added by al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.

Key Terms
عقب ('aqib): The heel of the foot; its exit from the khuff.
أكثر القدم (akthar al-qadam): The majority of the foot (more than half) considered as the criterion for invalidation by Abu Yusuf.
نقض المسح (naqd al-masah): Invalidation of the legal wiping on khuff; requires removal of khuff and washing feet for subsequent wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Whether the entire foot comes out
B) Whether the heel alone comes out
C) Whether the person can still walk normally after the foot's removal
D) Whether the foot is washed afterward

Key Takeaway
The invalidation of masah by foot removal hinges on the ability to walk normally, reconciling Abu Hanifa's focus on the heel with Abu Yusuf's on the majority.

Effect of Travel on Masah Period: Resident Traveling Before Completion
Explaining that a resident who travels before completing the masah period switches to the traveler's period of three days.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school allows a resident who travels during the masah period to switch to the traveler's period of three days, and distinguish the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A resident who travels before finishing masah wipes three days from travel; travel status governs the concession.

Imagine you perform wudu and wipe over your khuff at home, then within a few hours you travel for work. How long can you continue wiping? The Hanafi school teaches that your period changes to that of a traveler. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the disagreement with the Shafi'i school, helping you understand why the ruling adapts to your circumstances.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that if a resident wipes over his khuff and then travels before completing one day and one night, he switches to the traveler's period of three days from the moment of travel.
This applies whether the travel occurs before or after the hadath (invalidation of wudu).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) disagrees. He argues that since the act of worship began in residency, the initial ruling (one day) should persist.
His analogy: prayer begun in a resident's ship continues even if the ship travels.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i's proof is based on qiyas: he compares masah to prayer and fasting begun in residency, where the initial ruling remains unchanged.
For Shafi'is, the state at the beginning of the act determines the entire ruling.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that masah is not a single act but a period concession, analogous to the days of Ramadan rather than a single fast. Each day of wiping is independent, and the hadith 'The traveler wipes for three days' applies absolutely.
Additionally, intention (niyyah) is not a condition for masah in the Hanafi school, so the initial intention does not fix the period.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is clear: a Hanafi follower wipes for three days after travel, while a Shafi'i follower wipes for only one day total.
This affects daily practice, especially for frequent travelers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولو مسح مقيم فسافر قبل تمام يوم وليلة مسح ثلاثاً) سواء سافر قبل انتقاض الطهارة أو بعدها قبل كمال مدة المقيم، ولا خلاف في أن مدته تتحوّل إلى مدة المسافر في الأول وفي الثاني خلاف الشافعي لنا العمل بإطلاق قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «يمسح المسافر» الحديث. وهذا مسافر فيمسحها بخلاف ما بعد كمال مدة المقيم لأن الحدث قد سرى إلى القدم وإنما يمسح على خف رجل حدث فيها إجماعاً. وأما ما استدل به الشافعي من أن هذه عبادة ابتدأت حالة الإقامة فيعتبر فيها حالة الابتداء كصلاة ابتدأها مقيماً في سفينة فسافرت، وصوم شرع فيه مقيماً فسافر، حيث يعتبر فيه حكم الإقامة فغني عن تكلف الفرق لعدم ظهور وجه الجمع بالمشترك المؤثر في الحكم. كذا في فتح القدير وبيانه أن أئمتنا لا يرون العبادة وصفاً لازماً للمسح بل إذا كان الوضوء منوياً والنية ليست بشرط فيه عندهم، ولأن المسحات المدة بمنزلة الصيام في السفر لا بمنزلة صوم اليوم بدلالة أن فساد بعض المسحات لا فساد بعض الآخر كما في صيام أيام رمضان ولا شك في أن من سافر في أواخر رمضان يسقط عنه وجوب الأداء فيما بقي ما دام مسافراً ولا يمنع كونه مقيماً في أوله من ترخصه بترك أداء الصوم في تلك الحالة، فكذا كون الماسح مقيماً في أول المدة لا يمنع من ترخصه رخصة المسافر بالمسح إذا كان في آخرها مسافراً. قال في السراج الوهاج : فلو أنه لما جاوز العمران قبل مضي يوم وليلة ودخل في الصلاة سبقه الحدث فيها وعاد إلى مصره ليتوضأ وليلة قبل أن يعود إلى مصلاه، فالقياس أن تفسد صلاته لأن لما عاد إلى مصره فقد صار مقيماً وقد انقضت مدته وهو في الصلاة ففسدت إلا أن الصدر الشهيد ذكر في الواقعات أن الماسح إذا انقضت مدته وهو في حال انصرافه مع الحدث لا تبطل صلاته استحساناً، ولو عاد إلى مصلاه في مسألتنا قبل مضي يوم وليلة انتقلت مدته إلى السفر ووجب عليه الإتمام في هذه الصلاة وهذا مسألة عجيبة وهو أنه مسافر في حق المسح مقيم في حق اتمام الصلاة. كذا في ايضاح الصيرفي .اهـ. وقد علمت فيما قدمناه أن الصحيح بطلان الصلاة، ومسألة الإتمام المذكورة مذكورة في الخلاصة من باب المسافر. قوله (ولو أقام المسافر بعد يوم وليلة نزع وإلا يتم يوماً وليلة لأن رخصة السفر لا تبقى بدونه، والشافعي يوافقنا في هذه على ما هو المنصوص عليه.
His statement: (If a resident wipes and then travels before the completion of a day and night, he wipes for three days) — regardless of whether he traveled before the invalidation of his purification or after it, before the completion of the resident's period. There is no disagreement that his period changes to the traveler's period in the first case. In the second case, al-Shafi'i disagrees. Our proof is the absolute application of the hadith: 'The traveler wipes...' and this person is a traveler, so he wipes accordingly, unlike after the completion of the resident's period because the hadath has already reached the foot, and one wipes only over a khuff of a foot in which hadath occurred, by consensus. As for what al-Shafi'i argued — that this act of worship began in the state of residency, so the initial state should be considered, like a prayer begun as a resident in a ship that then travels, or a fast commenced as a resident who then travels, where the ruling of residency is observed — we do not need to strain to find a distinction because no common effective cause appears. Thus in Fath al-Qadir, explaining that our imams do not consider the act of worship as an inherent quality of wiping; rather, if the wudu is intended, intention is not a condition for it according to them. Moreover, the periods of wiping are analogous to fasting during travel, not to a single day's fast, indicated by the fact that the corruption of some wipings does not corrupt others, just as in the days of Ramadan. There is no doubt that one who travels at the end of Ramadan is no longer obligated to perform the remaining days while traveling, and his being a resident at the beginning does not prevent him from availing the traveler's concession to omit fasting in that state. Similarly, the fact that the wiper was a resident at the beginning of the period does not prevent him from availing the traveler's concession of wiping if he is a traveler at the end of it. Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj says: If he passed the built-up area before the passing of a day and night and entered prayer, then hadath overtook him during it, and he returned to his town to perform wudu and (to complete) a night before returning to his prayer place, the analogy is that his prayer becomes invalid because when he returned to his town he became a resident and his period ended while in prayer, so it becomes invalid. However, al-Sadr al-Shahid mentioned in al-Waqi'at that if the wiper's period ends while he is returning with hadath, his prayer is not invalidated by istihsan. And if he returned to his prayer place in our issue before the passing of a day and night, his period changed to the travel period and he is obliged to complete in this prayer. This is a remarkable issue: he is a traveler with respect to wiping but a resident with respect to completing the prayer. Thus in Idah al-Sayrafi. And you have known from what we presented that the correct view is the invalidation of the prayer, and the aforementioned issue of completion is mentioned in al-Khulasa in the chapter on the traveler. His statement: (If a traveler takes up residence after a day and night, he removes [the khuff]; otherwise he completes a day and night, because the travel concession does not remain without it. Al-Shafi'i agrees with us on this, according to the authoritative text.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the situation where a person performs masah as a resident (one day and night period) and then travels before completing that period. The Hanafi ruling is that he then wipes for the traveler's period (three days) from the time he traveled, regardless of whether the travel occurs before or after the hadath (the initial wudu that brought about the masah). The text presents a disagreement with al-Shafi'i, who analogizes this to prayer and fasting begun in residency, where the initial ruling persists. The Hanafi response is that masah is different: it is not a single act but a concession for the duration, analogous to the days of Ramadan rather than a single fast. The commentary illustrates with cases: if the period ends while the person is in prayer and has hadath, the prayer may be invalid or saved by istihsan. An interesting case is where one is simultaneously a traveler for masah but a resident for completion of prayer. Finally, the converse case: if a traveler becomes resident after a day and night, he must remove the khuff and wash his feet; otherwise he completes the day and night. Al-Shafi'i agrees with this.

Key Terms
مدة المقيم (muddat al-muqim): The period of masah for a resident: one day and one night from the time of hadath.
مدة المسافر (muddat al-musafir): The period of masah for a traveler: three days and nights from the time of hadath.
رخصة السفر (rukhsat al-safar): The legal concession granted to travelers, such as extending the masah period to three days.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only for the remaining part of the resident's period
B) For three days from the moment of travel
C) For one day from the moment of travel
D) He cannot wipe on travel; he must remove the khuff

Key Takeaway
A resident who travels before completing the one-day masah period wipes for three days from the moment of travel, per the Hanafi school.

A Resident Who Travels Before Completing the One-Day Wiping Period
Ruling on change of status during wiping period with Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a resident who travels before completing the one-day wiping period and explain the dispute with al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
A resident who travels before completing one day wipes for three; Shafi'i says he must complete the resident's period.

When a person performs wudu and wipes over khuffs as a resident, then travels before completing the 24-hour period, does the wiping duration change? The Hanafi school says yes—his period converts to that of a traveler (three days). However, al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the initial state of residence should govern. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the evidence from both sides.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling from the matn: a resident who travels before completing one day and night wipes for three days as a traveler.
The ruling is from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and is confirmed in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i argues that since the act of wiping began in residence, the initial state should bind the entire period, analogous to prayer and fasting.
The objection is based on qiyas with continuous acts of worship.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school cites the general hadith 'The traveler wipes' and argues that wiping over khuffs is not a single continuous act but a series of independent concessions tied to the state at the time of each wipe.
They compare it to fasting in Ramadan, where travel lifts obligation for remaining days even if started as resident.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response distinguishes wiping from prayer/fasting: each wipe in the period is independent, and the concession attaches to the state of the person at the time of the act.
Also, intention is not a condition for the validity of masah in the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Hanafi, the traveler may wipe for three full days; under Shafi'i, he must complete the resident's one day first, then may wipe for three additional days if still traveling.
This affects how long the person can delay washing the feet.

الطهارة أو بعدها قبل كمال مدة المقيم، ولا خلاف في أن مدته تتحوّل إلى مدة المسافر في الأول وفي الثاني خلاف الشافعي لنا العمل بإطلاق قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «يمسح المسافر» الحديث. وهذا مسافر فيمسحها بخلاف ما بعد كمال مدة المقيم لأن الحدث قد سرى إلى القدم وإنما يمسح على خف رجل حدث فيها إجماعاً. وأما ما استدل به الشافعي من أن هذه عبادة ابتدأت حالة الإقامة فيعتبر فيها حالة الابتداء كصلاة ابتدأها مقيماً في سفينة فسافرت، وصوم شرع فيه مقيماً فسافر، حيث يعتبر فيه حكم الإقامة فغني عن تكلف الفرق لعدم ظهور وجه الجمع بالمشترك المؤثر في الحكم. كذا في فتح القدير وبيانه أن أئمتنا لا يرون العبادة وصفاً لازماً للمسح بل إذا كان الوضوء منوياً والنية ليست بشرط فيه عندهم، ولأن المسحات المدة بمنزلة الصيام في السفر لا بمنزلة صوم اليوم بدلالة أن فساد بعض المسحات لا فساد بعض الآخر كما في صيام أيام رمضان ولا شك في أن من سافر في أواخر رمضان يسقط عنه وجوب الأداء فيما بقي ما دام مسافراً ولا يمنع كونه مقيماً في أوله من ترخصه بترك أداء الصوم في تلك الحالة، فكذا كون الماسح مقيماً في أول المدة لا يمنع من ترخصه رخصة المسافر بالمسح إذا كان في آخرها مسافراً. قال في السراج الوهاج : فلو أنه لما جاوز العمران قبل مضي يوم وليلة ودخل في الصلاة سبقه الحدث فيها وعاد إلى مصره ليتوضأ وليلة قبل أن يعود إلى مصلاه، فالقياس أن تفسد صلاته لأن لما عاد إلى مصره فقد صار مقيماً وقد انقضت مدته وهو في الصلاة ففسدت إلا أن الصدر الشهيد ذكر في الواقعات أن الماسح إذا انقضت مدته وهو في حال انصرافه مع الحدث لا تبطل صلاته استحساناً، ولو عاد إلى مصلاه في مسألتنا قبل مضي يوم وليلة انتقلت مدته إلى السفر ووجب عليه الإتمام في هذه الصلاة وهذا مسألة عجيبة وهو أنه مسافر في حق المسح مقيم في حق اتمام الصلاة. كذا في ايضاح الصيرفي .اهـ. وقد علمت فيما قدمناه أن الصحيح بطلان الصلاة، ومسألة الإتمام المذكورة مذكورة في الخلاصة من باب المسافر. قوله (ولو أقام المسافر بعد يوم وليلة نزع وإلا يتم يوماً وليلة لأن رخصة السفر لا تبقى بدونه، والشافعي يوافقنا في هذه على ما هو المنصوص عليه.
فمضى
yوم
بعده مفوّت لتقييد محل الخلاف على أن قول القدوري ومن ابتدأ مدة المسح فسافر يدفع هذا لما أن ابتداءها من وقت الحدث قوله: (وفي الثاني خلاف الشافعي رحمه الله قال بعض الفضلاء: قلت خلاف الشافعي إنما هو فيما إذا سافر بعد الحدث والمسح قبل كمال مدة المقيم. وأما إذا سافر بعد ومسح في السفر قبل خروج وقت الصلاة أو بعد خروجه في الصحيح فإنه يتم مسح مسافر من حين أحدث في الحضر لأنه بدأ بالعبادة في السفر فثبت له رخصة السفر. كذا في المهذب وشرحه للنووي اهـ . قلت : ونحوه في شرح المنهج للقاضي زكريا الأنصاري وهو المفهوم أيضاً من
الحدث
The book of purification - Chapter on wiping over khuffs. A resident who travels before completing a day and night wipes three [days and nights]; and if a traveler resides after a day and night, he removes [his khuffs], otherwise he completes a day and night. ... and in the second there is disagreement of al-Shafi'i. Our evidence is acting upon the generality of his saying, peace be upon him: 'The traveler wipes' the hadith. And this is a traveler so he wipes, unlike after completing the resident's period because the impurity has spread to the foot, and it is only wiped over the khuff of a man who had impurity in it by consensus. As for what al-Shafi'i argued, that this is an act of worship begun in the state of residence, so the initial state is considered like a prayer begun while resident on a ship that then travels, and a fast commenced while resident then traveled, where the ruling of residence is considered, so he is independent of the trouble of distinguishing because there is no apparent common factor affecting the ruling. Thus in Fath al-Qadir...
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on wiping over khuffs when the status (resident/traveler) changes during the wiping period. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that a resident who travels before completing the one-day period wipes for three days as a traveler, while a traveler who resides after one day must remove his khuffs and wash his feet. The commentator expands on the dispute with al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi position relies on the general hadith of the Prophet ﷺ: 'The traveler wipes...' and argues that the act of wiping is not a continuous worship like prayer or fasting but a concession tied to the state of travel. Al-Shafi'i analogizes to prayer and fasting, but the Hanafis differentiate by noting that wiping, like fasting in Ramadan, is a series of independent acts (each wipe in a period is separate) and thus the status at the time of each wipe matters. The passage also discusses an interesting scenario: a person who travels after the event but before completing the resident's period; the correct view is that his period converts to travel. There is also a discussion about a person whose period expires during prayer – the preferred view is that the prayer is invalidated.

Key Terms
مسح (masah): Wiping over the khuff with wet hand as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.
مقيم (muqeem): A person not on a journey of travel distance (approx. 48 miles/78 km) or intending to stay 15+ days.
مسافر (musafir): One who travels a distance of three days (approx. 48 miles) with intention to travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A resident makes wudu and wipes over his khuffs. After 10 hours, he travels before completing 24 hours. How long may he now wipe?
A) He must remove his khuffs and wash his feet because his period as resident has started.
B) He may continue wiping for a total of 3 days from the time of his wudu.
C) He may wipe only for the remaining 14 hours of the resident's period.
D) He must stop wiping and wash his feet at the next prayer time.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a resident who travels before completing the one-day wiping period becomes subject to the traveler's concession (three days), because the concession is tied to the status at the time of each wipe, not the initial state.

Wiping Over Jarmuq: Hanafi Position and Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling with conditions and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over jarmuq, identify the conditions for a valid khuff, and explain the basis for disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Wiping over jarmuq is permissible; the khuff must be suitable for walking and cover the ankles.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on wiping over jarmuq — a short boot worn over the khuff — and the conditions that make a khuff valid for wiping. The text also presents the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response, supported by hadith and analogy. By the end, you will understand both the practical ruling and the legal reasoning behind the ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding wiping on jarmuq and the basic conditions of the khuff.
The jarmuq is permissible to wipe over when worn over a valid khuff.
2
Identify the Opponent's View
State the Shafi'i position: wiping on jarmuq is not permissible, and khuffs made of non-leather materials are invalid.
Al-Shafi'i argues that jarmuq would become a substitute for the khuff, which has no substitute.
3
Examine the Hanafi Proof
Analyze the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ wiping on 'al-muqayn' and the analogy that jarmuq is subsidiary to khuff.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear; the analogy treats jarmuq like a second layer.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
Understand how the Hanafis rebut the Shafi'i argument: the jarmuq is not a substitute but a protector, analogous to a double-layered khuff.
The need for jarmuq exists in cold regions or for extra protection.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
Recognize the real-world difference: Hanafis allow wiping on jarmuq; Shafi'is require its removal to wipe the khuff directly.
This affects travelers and those in cold climates who wear additional footwear.

Source Text

قوله (وصح على الجرموق أي جاز المسح على الجرموق. لما فرغ من بيان المسح على الخف شرع في الجرموق ولا بد من بيانهما فنقول : ذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه : ثم الخف الذي يجوز المسح عليه ما يكون صالحاً لقطع المسافة والمشي المتتابع عادة، ويستر الكعبين وما تحتهما، وما ليس كذك لا يجوز المسح عليه . ثم قال : ويجوز المسح على الخف الذي يكون من اللبد وإن لم يكن منعلاً لأنه يمكن قطع المسافة وفي الخلاصة : وأما المسح على الخفاف به . المتخذة من اللبود التركية فالصحيح أنه يجوز المسح عليه، ولا يجوز المسح حتى يكون الأديم على أصابع الرجل وظاهر القدمين اهـ. فلو اتخذ خفاً من زجاج أو خشب أو حديد لا يجوز المسح عليه عندنا خلافاً للشافعي فيما يمكن متابعة المشي فيه بغير عصا. وأما الجرموق فهو فارسي معرب . ما يلبس فوق الخف وساقه أقصر من الخف. وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز المسح عليه لأن الحاجة لا تدعو إليه ولأن الخف بدل عن الرجل، فلو جاز المسح على الجرموق الصار بدلاً عن الخف والخف لا بدل له ولنا أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مسح على الموقين. رواه أبو داود من حديث بلال وابن خزيمة في صحيحه والحاكم في مستدركه وصححه والطبراني في معجمه والبيهقي من حديث أنس بن مالك. ولأنه تبع للخف استعمالاً من حيث المشي والقيام والقعود وغرضاً فإن الخف وقاية للرجل فكذا الجرموق وقاية للخف تبعاً له وكلاهما تبع للرجل فصار كخف ذي طاقين وهو بدل عن الرجل لا عن الخف، لا يقال كيف بطل المسح بنزع الجرموق ولم يبطل بنزع أحد طاقي الخف لأنا نقول : بالمسح ظهرت أصالة

المتخذ
يمسح
And it is valid on the jarmuq, and the unlined sock, the sandal, and the thick [sock], but not on the turban. His saying (and it is valid on the jarmuq) meaning it is permissible to wipe on the jarmuq... al-Shafi'i said: it is not permissible to wipe on it because there is no need for it and because the khuff is a substitute for the foot; if wiping on the jarmuq were allowed, it would become a substitute for the khuff, and the khuff has no substitute. Our evidence is that the Prophet ﷺ wiped on the muqayn (leather socks worn over khuffs?). It is narrated by Abu Dawud from the hadith of Bilal, and by Ibn Khuzaymah, al-Hakim, al-Tabarani, and al-Bayhaqi from Anas. And because it is subsidiary to the khuff in use...
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on wiping over the jarmuq, a type of footwear worn over the khuff, and the conditions for the khuff itself. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that wiping is valid on the jarmuq, as well as on a lined sock, sandal, and thick sock, but not on a turban. The commentator explains the definition of jarmuq (a Persian word meaning something worn over the khuff with a shorter leg) and presents the Hanafi evidence, including the hadith that the Prophet ﷺ wiped on 'al-muqayn' (a type of footwear). The Shafi'i school opposes, arguing that there is no need and that the jarmuq would become a substitute for the khuff, which itself has no substitute. The Hanafis respond by pointing to the hadith and analogy: the jarmuq serves as protection for the khuff just as the khuff protects the foot, so it is like a double-layered khuff. The passage also discusses the condition for a valid khuff: it must be suitable for walking and cover the ankles. There is a detailed commentary on whether the khuff must be able to walk in by itself or with shoes (muka'ab). The relied-upon view is that it must be able to walk in by itself, and a person must check his khuff periodically to ensure it meets the condition.

Key Terms
جرموق (jarmuq): A Persian word for a short boot or footwear worn over the khuff, with leg shorter than the khuff.
خف (khuff): Leather sock covering the foot and ankle, suitable for walking.
موقين (muqayn): A type of footwear (dual form); the Prophet wiped on them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for a khuff to be valid for wiping according to the Hanafi school?
A) It must cover the ankles.
B) It must be suitable for walking continuously.
C) It must be made of leather.
D) It must not be made of glass, wood, or iron.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over jarmuq is permissible in Hanafi fiqh; the khuff must be walkable and cover the ankles, and the jarmuq is subsidiary to it.

Wiping Over the Jarmuq: Proof, Dispute, and Conditions
Inter-madhhab dispute with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on wiping over the jarmuq, cite the hadith proof, refute the Shafi'i objection, and apply the two conditions for its validity.

Core Idea
The jarmuq follows the khuff: wiping over it is valid like a second layer, proven by the Prophet's own practice.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on wiping over the jarmuq (overshoe), a distinct covering worn over the khuff. The passage defines the jarmuq, provides the prophetic hadith as proof, refutes the Shafi'i objection, and outlines the essential conditions for valid wiping. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate contradictory proofs and distinguish between rulings based on direct text versus qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Define the terms
Identify the khuff (leather sock) and jarmuq (overshoe). Note that the jarmuq is worn over the khuff and is shorter. The linguists confirm this distinction, contrary to al-Nawawi's claim.
The Hanafi school relies on lexicographers like al-Jawhari and al-Mutarrizi.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds that wiping over the jarmuq is permissible. The primary proof is the hadith that the Prophet ﷺ wiped on al-mawqayn (interpreted as the jarmuq), reported by multiple authorities.
The hadith is ahad, zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah, but sufficient for a non-obligatory act.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Al-Shafi'i argues that the jarmuq is unnecessary and would become a substitute for the khuff, which is itself a substitute for the foot. The Hanafi response: the jarmuq is not a substitute for the foot but a protector of the khuff, analogous to a second layer of the khuff. The hadith directly disproves the objection.
The Hanafi also note inconsistency: al-Shafi'i permits wiping on glass/iron khuffs, which also have no genuine need.
4
Extract the conditions for valid wiping
According to al-Siraj, two conditions: (1) No hadath (ritual impurity) occurs between wearing the khuff and wearing the jarmuq; (2) The jarmuq must be worn before wiping on the khuff. The commentator clarifies that wiping on the khuff after wearing the jarmuq transfers the wiping to the jarmuq.
If one wears the jarmuq after hadath, the ruling of wiping is already established on the khuff and cannot be transferred.
5
Apply to a practical scenario
Given a person who performs wudu, wears khuff, then later (without hadath) wears jarmuq, then has hadath — he may wipe on the jarmuq. But if he has hadath first, then wears jarmuq, he cannot wipe on the jarmuq.
The mufta bihi position is that wiping on the jarmuq is permissible with these conditions.

المعتبر ما يصلح لقطع المسافة فيه نفسه، فعلى هذا فالواجب على الشخص أن يتفقد خفه فإنه قد يرق أسفله ويمشي عليه بالمكعب أياماً كثيرة ولا ينقب ولو فرض أنه لو مشى به وحده يتخرق في دون ذلك فإنه يصح المسح عليه والناس عنه غافلون، فإنهم لا يزالون يمسحون حتى يتخرق قدر ثلاث أصابع مع أنه قبل هذا قد لا يمكن المشي عليه في المدة المعتبرة، فعلى الشخص أن يعتبر ذلك قبل الخرق وبعده لئلا يصلي بلا طهارة فليحفظ قوله فالصحيح أنه يجوز المسح عليه قال الرملي : أي على الخف من اللبود التركية، وتمام عبارة الخلاصة بعد قوله عليه : ويمسح على الجرموق فوق الخف عندنا فإن لبسهما وحده لا عليهما ولا يجوز اهـ وقوله فإن لبسهما أي الخفين المتخذة من اللبود التركية وعليك أن تتأمل في عبارة الخلاصة .اهـ. أقول : في كلام المؤلف سقط أو إيجاز محل فإن المسح على الخفاف المتخذة من اللبود التركية جائز كما صرح به في المنية معللاً بإمكان قطع المسافة بها. قال المتخذ يمسح الجرموق فصار نزعه كنزع الخف بخلاف نزع أحد طاقي الخف لأنه جزء من الخف لم يأخذ الأصالة أصلاً كما إذا غسل رجله ثم أزال جلدها لم يجب عليه غسلها ثانياً. ولا يقال أيضاً لو كان بدلاً عن الرجل لكان ينبغي أن لا يجوز المسح على الخف بنزعه لأنا نقول: الخف لم یکن محلاً للمسح حال قيام الجرموق فإذا زال صار محلاً للمسح. وما ذكره النووي من أن الموق هو الخف مخالف لما ذكره أهل اللغة كالجوهري والمطرزي فإنهما قالا: إن الجرموق والموق يلبسان فوق الخف فعلم أنهما غير الخف. وقولهم إن الحاجة لا تدعو إليه ممنوع ومناقض لمذهبهم في الخف من الزجاج أو الحديد كما قدمناه ويشترط لجواز المسح على الجرموقين أن لا يحدث قبل لبسهما حتى لو لبس الخف على طهارة ثم أحدث قبل لبس الجرموق ثم لبسه لا يجوز له أن يمسح عليه، سواء لبسه قبل المسح على الخف أو بعده، حكم الحدث استقر عليه لحلول الحدث به فلا يزال بمسح غيره وكذا لو لبس الموقين قبل لأن شارحها العلامة الحلبي حتى قالوا لو شاهد أبو حنيفة رحمه الله صلابتها لأفتى بالجواز لشدة دلكها وتداخل أجزائها بذلك حتى صارت كالجلد الغليظ، وأجمعوا على جواز المسح عليها بطريق الدلالة اهـ. فقول الخلاصة على الصحيح إشارة إلى خلاف الإمام في اشتراط النعل، وقول الحلبي وأجمعوا الخ» بناء على رجوعه إلى قولهما كما سيأتي، وحينئذ فلا يشترط أن يكون الأديم على أصابع الرجل وظاهر القدم، فعلم أن قول الخلاصة فإن لبسهما أي الجرموقين لا كما قال الرملي، وكذا قوله ولا يجوز المسح حتى يكون الخ» معطوف على قولها «لا يمسح عليهما كما يظهر من مراجعة شرح المنية، فالصواب حذف قول المؤلف ولا يجوز المسح الخ والاقتصار على ما قبله. قوله : ويشترط لجواز المسح على الجرموقين (الخ قال في السراج واعلم أن المسح على الجرموقين إنما يجوز بشرطين: أحدهما أن لا يتخلل بينه وبين الخف حدث كما إذا لبس الخفين على طهارة ولم يمسح عليهما حتى لبس الجرموقين قبل أن تنتقض الطهارة التي لبس عليها الخفين فحينئذ يجوز المسح على الجرموقين. وأما إذا أحدث بعد لبس الخفين أو مسح عليهما ثم لبس الجرموقين بعد ذلك لا يجوز له المسح على الجرموقين لأن حكم المسح قد استقر على الخف وكذا لو أحدث بعد لبس الخف ثم لبس الجرموق قبل أن : يمسح على الخف لا يمسح عليه أيضاً لأن ابتداء مدة المسح من وقت الحدث وقد انعقد ذلك في الخف فلا يتحول عنه إلى الجرموق بعد ذلك والشرط الثاني أن تنيكون إلى آخر ما سيأتي. أقول : قوله (وأما إذا أحدث بعد لبس الخفين أو مسح عليهما الخ» يوهم أنه لو مسح على الخف ولو قبل الحدث كما لو جدد الوضوء ومسح على خفه ثم لبس الجرموق لا يصح المسح على الجرموق بعد ذلك، فيفيد أن لبس الجرموق قبل المسح شرط آخر كما أن لبسه قبل الحدث شرط وهذا بعيد إذ لو كان كذلك لكانت الشروط ثلاثة أنه قال أولاً إنما يجوز بشرطين. وأيضاً فإن حكم المسح لا يستقر على الخف إلا بعد الحدث، أما قبله فإن وجود الخف كعدمه، فالظاهر أن «أو» في قوله أو مسح عليهما بمعنى الواو إن لم تكن الهمزة من زيادة النساخ بقرينة قوله بعده وكذا لو
(Chapter of Purification - Section on Wiping over Khuff) 'It is completed for a day and a night, and wiping is valid over the jarmuq, the leather sock with an upper, the sandal, and the thick [sock], but not over the turban.' He said: '(And valid over the jarmuq) i.e., wiping over the jarmuq is permissible. When he finished explaining wiping over the khuff, he began [discussing] the jarmuq, and we must explain both. We say: Qadikhan mentioned in his Fatawa: 'The khuff on which wiping is permissible is that which is suitable for covering distance and continuous walking customarily, and covers the ankles and what is below them. What is not like that is not permissible to wipe over.' Then he said: 'It is permissible to wipe over the khuff made of felt even if it is not sandaled, because it is possible to cover distance [in it].' And in al-Khulasa: 'As for wiping over khuff made of Turkish felt, the correct [position] is that it is permissible to wipe over them, but it is not permissible to wipe until the leather extends over the toes and the top of the feet.' End. So if one makes a khuff of glass, wood, or iron, it is not permissible to wipe over it according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding what is possible for continuous walking without a stick. As for the jarmuq, it is a Persianized [word]: something worn over the khuff, and its leg is shorter than the khuff. Al-Shafi'i said: 'It is not permissible to wipe over it because need does not call for it, and because the khuff is a substitute for the foot; if wiping over the jarmuq were permissible, then it would become a substitute for the khuff, and the khuff has no substitute.' Our [evidence] is that the Prophet ﷺ wiped over the mawqayn. Abu Dawud narrated it from Bilal, Ibn Khuzaymah in his Sahih, al-Hakim in his Mustadrak and he authenticated it, al-Tabarani in his Mu'jam, and al-Bayhaqi from Anas ibn Malik. And because it is a follower of the khuff in usage in terms of walking, standing, sitting, and purpose; for the khuff is protection for the foot, so similarly the jarmuq is protection for the khuff as a follower of it, and both are followers of the foot, so it becomes like a khuff with two layers, and it is a substitute for the foot, not for the khuff. It cannot be said: How is wiping nullified by removing the jarmuq but not by removing one layer of the khuff? We say: By wiping, the originality appeared... not restricting the author by his saying: '[Wiping of] a resident who then travels before completing a day and a night.' He said: '(What is suitable for covering distance and continuous walking customarily).' I say: Let us consider what is meant by that: is the criterion covering distance by the khuff itself, i.e., that it is suitable for that without being worn in a [wooden] shoe [over it], or what is customary for us of wearing it in a [wooden] shoe? We have hesitated about this for a long time and have not found a transmission despite searching and scrutiny, but our teacher said: What appears from their words in their rationales and proofs is that the criterion is what is suitable for covering distance in itself. Therefore, a person must inspect his khuff, for its bottom may become thin and he walks on it in a shoe for many days without it being pierced, but if it were assumed that if he walked in it alone it would tear in less than that, then wiping over it is valid, and people are heedless of this. Indeed, they continue to wipe until it tears to the extent of three fingers, although before this it may not be possible to walk in it for the considered duration. So a person must consider this before the tear and after, lest he pray without purity. So let him memorize. His saying: 'So the correct [position] is that wiping over it is permissible.' Al-Ramli said: i.e., over the khuff made of Turkish felt. The complete text of al-Khulasa after his statement 'over it': 'And he wipes over the jarmuq above the khuff according to us; if he wears them both alone, no [wiping] on them, and it is not permissible.' End. And his statement: 'For he wears them' means the two khuffs made of Turkish felt. And you must contemplate the phrase of al-Khulasa. End. I say: In the author's speech there is an omission or a place of conciseness, for wiping over khuff made of Turkish felt is permissible as stated in al-Munya, reasoning with the possibility of covering distance in them. He said: '[The one who wears] it wipes the jarmuq, so removing it becomes like removing the khuff, contrary to removing one layer of the khuff because it is a part of the khuff that did not take originality at all, just as if one washed his foot then removed its skin, he is not required to wash it a second time. Nor can it be said: If it were a substitute for the foot, then it would be incumbent that wiping over the khuff is not permissible upon its removal? We say: The khuff was not a place for wiping while the jarmuq was present; when it is removed, it becomes a place for wiping. And what al-Nawawi mentioned that the mawq is the khuff contradicts what the linguists like al-Jawhari and al-Mutarrizi said, for they said: The jarmuq and the mawq are worn above the khuff, so it is known that they are other than the khuff. And their statement that need does not call for it is rejected and contradicts their school regarding the khuff of glass or iron as we have previously mentioned. And it is a condition for the permissibility of wiping over the two jarmuqs that he does not have an event [of hadath] before wearing them, such that if he wore the khuff in a state of purity then had an event before wearing the jarmuq then wore it, he is not permitted to wipe over it, whether he wore it before wiping over the khuff or after; the ruling of the event has become established upon him due to the occurrence of the event, so it is not removed by wiping over another [covering]. Similarly, if he wore the two mawqs before... because its commentator al-Halabi even said: If Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) had seen their roughness, he would have issued a fatwa of permissibility due to the severity of their polishing and the interlocking of their parts such that they became like thick leather, and they agreed on the permissibility of wiping over them by way of indication. End. So the statement of al-Khulasa 'on the correct [position]' is an indication of the Imams disagreement regarding the condition of sandal. And al-Halabi's statement 'and they agreed' is based on his return to their [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's] position as will come. In that case, it is not required that the leather extend over the toes and the top of the foot. So it is known that the statement of al-Khulasa 'for he wears them' means the two jarmuqs, not as al-Ramli said. Similarly, his statement 'and it is not permissible to wipe until...' is coordinated with her statement 'he does not wipe over them' as appears from referring to Sharh al-Munya. So the correct [procedure] is to delete the author's statement 'and it is not permissible to wipe' and restrict to what precedes it. He said: 'And it is a condition for the permissibility of wiping over the two jarmuqs.' Al-Siraj said: Know that wiping over the two jarmuqs is only permissible with two conditions: One of them is that no hadath intervenes between it and the khuff, as when he wears the two khuffs in a state of purity and does not wipe over them until he wears the two jarmuqs before the purity on which he wore the two khuffs is broken; then it is permissible to wipe over the two jarmuqs. But if he has hadath after wearing the two khuffs or wipes over them, then wears the two jarmuqs after that, it is not permissible for him to wipe over the two jarmuqs because the ruling of wiping has become established on the khuff. Similarly, if he had hadath after wearing the khuff then wore the jarmuq before wiping over the khuff, he also does not wipe over it because the beginning of the period of wiping is from the time of hadath, and it has been confirmed on the khuff, so it does not transfer to the jarmuq after that. The second condition will follow. I say: His statement: ('But if he had hadath after wearing the two khuffs or wipes over them') implies that if he wiped over the khuff even before hadath, as if he renewed wudu and wiped over his khuff then wore the jarmuq, wiping over the jarmuq is not valid after that. This would make wearing the jarmuq before wiping an additional condition just as wearing it before hadath is a condition. This is far-fetched because if so, there would be three conditions, whereas he initially said it is only permissible with two conditions. Also, the ruling of wiping is not established on the khuff except after hadath; before that, the existence of the khuff is like its non-existence. So it appears that 'or' in his statement 'or wipes over them' means 'and', unless the hamza is from the addition of copyists, as indicated by his statement afterwards 'Similarly, if'.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of wiping over the jarmuq (an overshoe worn over the khuff). The commentator begins by explaining the matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq: wiping over the jarmuq is valid. He first defines the khuff itself, quoting Qadikhan and al-Khulasa: a khuff must be suitable for walking and cover the ankles. Then he defines the jarmuq as a Persian word, shorter than the khuff, worn over it. The Shafi'i school prohibits wiping on the jarmuq, arguing that there is no need and that the khuff itself is a substitute for the foot—if the jarmuq were also a substitute, it would create a substitute for a substitute. The Hanafi response provides two proofs: first, a hadith from multiple chains that the Prophet ﷺ wiped on the mawqayn (which the Hanafis identify as the jarmuq, not the khuff); second, rational analogy (qiyas): the jarmuq protects the khuff just as the khuff protects the foot, making it like a two-layered khuff. The commentator then addresses potential objections about nullification upon removal and linguistic claims by al-Nawawi. Finally, he discusses the conditions for valid wiping on the jarmuq, quoting al-Siraj: the jarmuq must be worn before any hadath occurs after wearing the khuff, and before wiping on the khuff. He refines the text, noting that the phrase 'or wipes over them' likely means 'and', to avoid implying an extra condition. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that wiping on the jarmuq is permissible subject to these conditions.

Key Terms
الجرموق (al-jarmuq): An overshoe worn over the khuff, Persianized, shorter than the khuff.
الخف (al-khuff): Leather sock that covers the feet and ankles, worn for walking; must be suitable for continuous walking and cover the ankles (according to Qadikhan's definition).
المسح (al-mash): The act of wiping over the khuff (or jarmuq) as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu'.
الموق (al-mawq): Synonym for jarmuq according to Hanafi linguists; worn over the khuff, not the khuff itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a condition for valid wiping over the jarmuq?
A) The jarmuq must be made of leather.
B) The jarmuq must be worn after having hadath.
C) The jarmuq must be worn before any hadath occurs after wearing the khuff.
D) The jarmuq must be thicker than the khuff.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over the jarmuq is valid in the Hanafi school, proven by the Prophet's practice and analogy to a two-layered khuff, provided it is worn before hadath and before wiping on the khuff.

Conditions for Wiping on Jawraq Over Khuff
States conditions for validity of wiping on jawraq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for valid wiping on jawraq over khuff and identify which scenarios invalidate the wiping.

Core Idea
Wiping on jawraq is invalid if any hadath occurred before putting it on.

Wiping over khuffs is a classical dispensation for travelers. But what if you wear an extra layer, the jawraq? Can you wipe on that instead? The Hanafi school details two specific conditions for this substitution to work. This lesson walks through those conditions from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping on jawraq over khuff. Its ruling is sahih (valid) only if the conditions are met; otherwise it is invalid.
2
State the first condition
The jawraq must be put on before any hadath occurs after wearing the khuff. In other words, the khuff must still be in a state of purity when the jawraq is worn.
3
State the second condition
The jawraq must be put on before the khuff is wiped. If the khuff has already been wiped (even if no hadath), the wiping period is tied to the khuff and cannot transfer to the jawraq.
4
Apply to scenarios
Analyze the given scenarios: after hadath but before wiping (invalid), after wiping (invalid), before hadath and before wiping (valid). Understanding why each case is ruled accordingly.
5
Understand the rationale
The hadath 'settles' on the khuff once it occurs, making the khuff the exclusive locus for wiping. The jawraq cannot nullify that settled hadath; it only serves as a substitute if worn while the khuff is still pure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويشترط لجواز المسح على الجرموقين أن لا يحدث قبل لبسهما حتى لو لبس الخف على طهارة ثم أحدث قبل لبس الجرموق ثم لبسه لا يجوز له أن يمسح عليه، سواء لبسه قبل المسح على الخف أو بعده، حكم الحدث استقر عليه لحلول الحدث به فلا يزال بمسح غيره. قال في السراج واعلم أن المسح على الجرموقين إنما يجوز بشرطين: أحدهما أن لا يتخلل بينه وبين الخف حدث كما إذا لبس الخفين على طهارة ولم يمسح عليهما حتى لبس الجرموقين قبل أن تنتقض الطهارة التي لبس عليها الخفين فحينئذ يجوز المسح على الجرموقين. وأما إذا أحدث بعد لبس الخفين أو مسح عليهما ثم لبس الجرموقين بعد ذلك لا يجوز له المسح على الجرموقين لأن حكم المسح قد استقر على الخف وكذا لو أحدث بعد لبس الخف ثم لبس الجرموق قبل أن يمسح على الخف لا يمسح عليه أيضاً لأن ابتداء مدة المسح من وقت الحدث وقد انعقد ذلك في الخف فلا يتحول عنه إلى الجرموق بعد ذلك.
It is a condition for the permissibility of wiping over the two jawraqs that he does not have an event before putting them on. So if he put on the khuff in a state of purity, then had an event before putting on the jawraq, then put them on, he is not permitted to wipe over them, whether he put them on before wiping on the khuff or after. The ruling of the event has become settled upon him due to the occurrence of the event, so it is not removed by wiping on something else. He said in al-Siraj: Know that wiping over the two jawraqs is only permissible with two conditions: one is that no event occurs between them and the khuff, such as if he put on the two khuffs in a state of purity and did not wipe over them until he put on the two jawraqs before the purity in which he put on the khuffs was broken; then it is permissible to wipe over the two jawraqs. But if he had an event after putting on the two khuffs or wiped over them, then put on the two jawraqs after that, it is not permissible for him to wipe over the two jawraqs because the ruling of wiping has become settled on the khuff. Likewise, if he had an event after putting on the khuff, then put on the jawraq before wiping on the khuff, he also does not wipe over it because the beginning of the wiping period is from the time of the event, and that has been established in the khuff, so it does not transfer from it to the jawraq after that.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the conditions for valid wiping over jawraq (a sort of boot or sock worn over the khuff). The text states a key condition: the person must not have had an event (hadath) after putting on the khuff but before putting on the jawraq. In other words, the jawraq must be put on while the original khuff is still in a state of purity (i.e., before the first hadath after wearing the khuff). If a hadath occurs after putting on the khuff, then the ruling of the hadath becomes settled on the khuff, and subsequent wiping on the jawraq would not remove that hadath. The text further elaborates via a quote from al-Siraj: there are two conditions. First, no hadath between the khuff and the jawraq; the example given is wearing khuff with wudu, then putting on jawraq before breaking that wudu – then wiping on jawraq is valid. Second, if one has an event after wearing khuff or wipes on the khuff, then puts on jawraq later, wiping on jawraq is invalid because the effect of wiping is already settled on the khuff. Likewise, if one has an event after wearing khuff and then puts on jawraq before wiping on the khuff, wiping on jawraq is also invalid because the start of the wiping period (from the event) is tied to the khuff. The Hanafi position here is that the jawraq is not the original place of wiping; it is a substitute, and its validity depends on the status of the khuff at the time of wearing the jawraq.

Key Terms
الجرموق (al-jawraq): A sock or boot worn over the khuff (leather sock).
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity that breaks wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, wiping on jawraq over khuff is valid when:
A) The jawraq is put on after wiping on the khuff but before any hadath.
B) The jawraq is put on before any hadath after wearing the khuff and before wiping on the khuff.
C) The jawraq is put on after hadath but before wiping on the khuff.
D) The jawraq is put on after hadath and after wiping on the khuff.

Key Takeaway
Wiping on jawraq is valid only if it is put on while the khuff is still in a state of purity and before any wiping on the khuff.
