Wiping on Khuff Over a Barrier: The Hanafi Position
Explains validity of wiping on khuff when another khuff or wrapping is beneath it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over a khuff when a barrier (another khuff, lifafah, or cloth) is present, and identify the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) from the dispute between al-Shadhi and al-Halabi.

Core Idea
Wiping on an outer khuff is valid even with a barrier beneath, because the barrier is legally disregarded.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuff when a barrier intervenes between the foot and the khuff. The source text from Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses cases where a khuff is worn over another khuff, a wrapping (lifafah), or a sewn cloth (karbas). It also presents an intra-Hanafi difference between an earlier fatwa by al-Shadhi and the later reasoning of al-Halabi, with the latter being relied upon. By the end, you will be able to state the ruling and understand the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
Recognize the two main cases: (1) khuff over khuff (like jawraq) and (2) khuff over wrapping or cloth. The passage treats both similarly.
2
State the general ruling
According to Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Khulasa, wiping on the outer khuff is valid even with a barrier, because the barrier is considered non-existent.
The key principle: 'what is permissible to wipe over if no barrier remains permissible even with a barrier.'
3
Note the exception from al-Kafi
If the inner khuffs are torn and not suitable for wiping, wiping on the outer jawraq is allowed by agreement.
This shows the school's flexibility.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Shadhi's fatwa prohibits wiping when a plain cloth (karbas) is under the khuff. Al-Halabi rebuts by analogy with the jawraq, concluding it is valid.
The dispute centers on whether a cloth barrier is legally equivalent to a wrapping or another khuff.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Halabi's reasoning is accepted; wiping on the khuff over cloth is valid as long as the outer khuff itself is suitable for wiping.
Later Hanafi scholarship relies on al-Halabi's view, as it better fits the school's principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخف على الخف كالجرموق عندنا في سائر أحكامه. كذا في الخلاصة. وكذا الخف فوق اللفافة يدل عليه ما في غاية البيان من أن ما جاز المسح عليه إذا لم يكن بينه وبين الرجل حائل جاز المسح عليه إذا كان بينهما حائل كخف إذا كان تحته خف أو لفافة .اهـ. ووقع في شرح ابن المالك عن الكافي أنه لو لم يكن خفاه صالحين للمسح لخرقهما يجوز على الموقين اتفاقاً. ونقل من فتاوى الشاذي أن ما يلبس من الكرباس المجرد تحت الخف يمنع المسح على الخف. قال العلامة إبراهيم الحلبي شارح المنية : ثم تعليل أئمتنا ههنا بأن الجرموق بدل عن الرجل الخ . يعلم منه جواز المسح على خف لبس فوق مخيط من كرباس أو جوخ أو نحوهما مما لا يجوز عليه المسح لأن الجرموق إذا كان بدلاً عن الرجل وجعل الخف مع جواز المسح عليه في حكم العدم فلأن يكون الخف بدلاً عن الرجل ويجعل ما لا يجوز المسح عليه في حكم العدم أولى كما في اللفافة.
And the khuff over the khuff is like the jawraq according to us in all its rulings. Thus in al-Khulasa. And likewise the khuff over the wrapping (lifafah) is indicated by what is in Ghayat al-Bayan: that whatever is permissible to wipe over if there is no barrier between it and the foot, it is permissible to wipe over if there is a barrier between them, like a khuff if there is another khuff or a wrapping beneath it. End quote. And it occurs in Sharh Ibn al-Malik from al-Kafi that if his two khuffs are not suitable for wiping due to holes, it is permissible to wipe on the two muqs (i.e., jawraqs) by agreement. And it is transmitted from the Fatawa of al-Shadhi that what is worn of plain cloth under the khuff prevents wiping on the khuff. Al-Allama Ibrahim al-Halabi, commentator of al-Munya, said: Then the reasoning of our imams here is that the jawraq is a substitute for the foot... From this is known the permissibility of wiping on a khuff worn over a sewn garment of cloth or broadcloth or similar things that are not permissible to wipe on, because if the jawraq is a substitute for the foot and the khuff, even though wiping on it is permissible, is considered as non-existent, then it is even more appropriate that the khuff be a substitute for the foot and that which is not permissible to wipe on be considered as non-existent, as in the case of the wrapping.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage extends the previous discussion to cases where a khuff is worn over another khuff or over a wrapping (lifafah). The Hanafi ruling is that wiping on the outer khuff is valid even with a barrier beneath, because the inner layer (whether another khuff or a wrapping) is considered legally nonexistent in terms of wiping. This is supported by a quote from Ghayat al-Bayan stating that any item that is permissible to wipe over when in direct contact with the foot remains permissible even when there is a barrier (like another khuff or wrapping) between it and the foot. The text then discusses a scenario from al-Kafi: if the inner khuffs are too torn for wiping, then wiping on the outer jawraq is permissible by agreement. Then a fatwa from al-Shadhi is noted: if a plain cloth (karbas) is worn under the khuff, it prevents wiping on the khuff. However, al-Halabi counters by reasoning that the jawraq is a substitute for the foot; therefore, if the jawraq can make the khuff under it considered nonexistent, then a khuff over a cloth should also be valid, as the cloth is even less worthy of consideration. This shows an intra-Hanafi difference: the earlier fatwa restricts, while later reasoning from al-Halabi allows it by analogy with the jawraq case. The relied-upon position seems to be that wiping on khuff over a wrapping or cloth is valid as long as the outer khuff itself is fit for wiping.

Key Terms
اللفافة (al-lifafah): A wrapping or bandage around the foot, often used as a barrier.
الكرباس (al-karbas): Plain cloth, often used as a sock-like covering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it valid to wipe on a khuff that is worn over a wrapping (lifafah) on the foot?
A) No, because there is a barrier.
B) Yes, because the wrapping is considered non-existent for the ruling of wiping.
C) Only if the wrapping is made of leather.
D) Only if the khuff is made of leather.

Key Takeaway
Wiping on an outer khuff is valid even with a barrier (another khuff, lifafah, or cloth) because the barrier is legally disregarded; the later Hanafi position follows al-Halabi's reasoning.

Wiping Over a Khuff with a Cloth Underneath
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of wiping over khuff with cloth underneath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on wiping over a khuff with a cloth underneath and apply the Hanafi tarjih methodology to determine the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A cloth under the khuff does not prevent wiping – the khuff remains the outer layer.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a piece of cloth worn under a leather sock (khuff) invalidates wiping during wudhu. Some Hanafi scholars, citing Fatāwā al-Shādhī, consider the cloth a barrier. However, the author of al-Bahr al-Rā'iq argues that the cloth is analogous to a foot wrapping (lifafah), which does not prevent wiping, and thus the wiping remains valid. We will trace the evidence presented and learn how to weigh conflicting views within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Disputed Issue
State the exact ruling being contested: is the wiping over a khuff valid when a cloth (karbas) is worn under it? Note that both sides agree on the permissibility of wiping over the khuff itself when no barrier exists.
2
Analyze the Pro-Permissibility Argument
Examine the analogy presented in Ghāyat al-Bayān: if wiping is valid without a barrier, it is also valid with a barrier like a lifafah. Recognize that the karbas is equated to lifafah.
The author cites the case of a khuff over another khuff or lifafah as precedent.
3
Analyze the Opposition Argument
Understand that scholars following Fatāwā al-Shādhī argue that the karbas is a stitched garment that explicitly prevents wiping.
They also challenge the chain of transmission: the claim is not found in al-Kāfī as Ibn al-Mālik asserted.
4
Follow the Tarjih Process
See how the author weighs the evidence: Ghāyat al-Bayān is a stronger source than Fatāwā al-Shādhī; the analogy to lifafah is sound; additional support from commentators' responses to al-Shāfiʿī. Conclude that permissibility is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
Note that many Roman jurists sided with permissibility, and Yaʿqūb Pāshā confirmed it from al-Hidāyah and al-Kāfī.
5
Apply the Ruling
Determine the practical consequence: if the mufta bihi position is permissibility, then a person wearing a khuff over a cloth may wipe over the khuff, and their wudhu is valid. If they followed the prohibition view, they would need to remove the cloth or not wear it.
This is a clear thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووقع في شرح ابن المالك عن الكافي أنه لو لم يكن خفاه صالحين للمسح لخرقهما يجوز على الموقين اتفاقاً. ونقل من فتاوى الشاذي أن ما يلبس من الكرباس المجرد تحت الخف يمنع المسح. ويدل عليه ما في غاية البيان من أن ما جاز المسح عليه إذا لم يكن بينه وبين الرجل حائل جاز المسح عليه إذا كان بينهما حائل كخف إذا كان تحته خف أو لفافة. اهـ. فهذا صريح في أن اللفافة على الرجل لا تمنع المسح على الخف فوقها. وقد وقع في عصرنا بين فقهاء الروم بالروم كلام كثير في هذه المسألة فمنهم من تمسك بما في فتاوى الشاذي وأفتى بمنع المسح على الخف الذي تحته الكرباس ورد على ابن المالك في عزوه للكافي إذ الظاهر أن المراد به كافي النسفي ولم يوجد فيه ومنهم من أفتى بالجواز وهو الحق لما قدمناه عن غاية البيان ولهذا قال يعقوب باشا إنه مفهوم من الهداية والكافي. ويدل عليه أيضاً ما ذكره الشارحون في مسألة نزع الخف في الكلام مع الشافعي في قوله إنه إذا أعادهما يجوز له المسح من غير غسل الرجلين معللاً بأنه لم يظهر من محل الفرض شيء فقالوا في الرد عليه: إن قوله لم يظهر من محل الفرض شيء يشكل بما لو أخرج الخفين عن رجليه وعلى الرجلين لفافة فإنه يبطل المسح وإن لم يظهر من محل الفرض شيء. اهـ. فهذا ظاهر في صحة المسح على الخف فوق اللفافة.
And it occurred in the commentary of Ibn al-Mālik from al-Kāfī that if his two khuffs are not fit for wiping due to holes, then wiping upon the two mawq (socks) is permissible by agreement. And it is transmitted from the Fatāwā al-Shādhī that what is worn of plain cloth (karbas) under the khuff prevents wiping. And it is indicated by what is in Ghāyat al-Bayān: that what permits wiping when there is no barrier between it and the foot also permits wiping when there is a barrier between them, like a khuff if there is under it another khuff or a lifafah. End. So this is explicit that the lifafah on the foot does not prevent wiping upon the khuff over it. And in our time, there occurred among the jurists of the Romans (Rūm) much discussion in this issue. Some of them clung to what is in Fatāwā al-Shādhī and gave fatwa of prohibition of wiping upon the khuff that has cloth under it, and they refuted Ibn al-Mālik's attribution to al-Kāfī, since apparently what is meant is Kāfī al-Nasafī and it is not found therein. And some of them gave fatwa of permissibility, and it is the truth, due to what we presented from Ghāyat al-Bayān, and for this Yaʿqūb Pāshā said it is understood from al-Hidāyah and al-Kāfī. And it is also indicated by what the commentators mentioned in the issue of removing the khuff in the discussion with al-Shāfiʿī, in his statement that if he replaces them, he may wipe without washing the feet, reasoning that nothing from the place of the obligatory act has appeared. They responded to him: ‘His statement that nothing from the place of the obligatory act has appeared is problematic, for if he removes the two khuffs from his feet while on his feet there is a lifafah, then wiping becomes invalid even though nothing from the place of the obligatory act has appeared.’ End. So this is apparent regarding the validity of wiping upon the khuff over the lifafah.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether wiping over a khuff is valid when a piece of cloth (karbas) is worn under it. The author begins by citing Ibn al-Mālik's commentary on al-Kāfī, where it states that if the khuffs themselves are porous (not fit for wiping), one may wipe over the outer socks (mawq) by agreement. Then he quotes Fatāwā al-Shādhī, which asserts that a plain cloth under the khuff prevents wiping. However, the author immediately counters this with a principle from Ghāyat al-Bayān: if wiping is valid when there is no barrier between the foot and the khuff, it is also valid when there is a barrier, such as another khuff or a lifafah (foot wrapping). Thus, the lifafah does not prevent wiping, and by analogy, the karbas cloth should not either. The author then reports a contemporary debate among Roman jurists: some follow al-Shādhī and prohibit wiping, criticizing Ibn al-Mālik's reference to al-Kāfī (claiming it is not found there), while others permit it, which the author calls 'the truth.' He supports this with the argument that the karbas is like a lifafah, and also cites a response to al-Shāfiʿī's reasoning about removing khuffs: if one removes khuffs and has only a lifafah on the feet, wiping is invalid – this shows that the lifafah is not a barrier for wiping over the khuff when it is worn. The relied-upon position (muftā bihī) is permissibility, as it aligns with the stronger textual evidence from Ghāyat al-Bayān, al-Hidāyah, and al-Kāfī. The opposing view from al-Shādhī is considered weak and not authoritative.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): A leather sock or boot worn over the foot, upon which wiping is permitted in wudhu under certain conditions.
الكرباس (al-karbās): A coarse cloth worn as a foot wrapping under the khuff.
اللفافة (al-lifāfah): A cloth bandage or wrapping wound around the foot.
الموق / الجرموق (al-mawq / al-jarmūq): An outer sock worn over the khuff, often made of thick material.
فتاوى الشاذي (Fatāwā al-Shādhī): A collection of fatwas by a Hanafi scholar (possibly al-Shādhī), cited here as a source for the prohibition view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on wiping over a khuff that is worn over a cloth (karbas) wrapping?
A) It is not valid because the cloth is a barrier.
B) It is valid because the cloth is like a lifafah and does not prevent wiping.
C) It is valid only if the cloth is not stitched.
D) It is not valid unless the cloth is made of leather.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a cloth worn under the khuff does not prevent valid wiping, because it is analogous to a lifafah which is not a barrier.

Wiping over Khuff with a Linen Barrier: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on linen barrier under khuff.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on wiping over a khuff that has a linen barrier and identify the mufta bihi with its evidence.

Core Idea
A linen wrap under the khuff is not a barrier because it is not intended as footwear.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: may one wipe over a khuff if there is a piece of linen (karbas) wrapped around the foot beneath it? The source presents two views among later Hanafi scholars and explains why the majority permissive view is relied upon. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between intended barriers (like a torn jarmuq) and incidental coverings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The core question is whether a linen wrap (karbas) that is not itself considered footwear prevents the validity of wiping over the khuff. Pinpoint the exact point of disagreement.
The dispute is not about the khuff itself but about the effect of an unintended barrier.
2
State the two positions
One group (following al-Shādhī) prohibits wiping unless the linen is cut away. The majority (including al-Ḥalabī, Mulla Khusraw) permit wiping without cutting. Write each position in one sentence.
The opposing view is based on a fatwa from an unknown source, which weakens its authority.
3
Examine the majority's proof
The majority uses an argument from the earlier text of al-Kāfī: if a khuff that is unfit for wiping (e.g., torn) is not a barrier, then linen (which is even less intended as footwear) is also not a barrier. Also, the commentators' discussion on removing khuff with a foot wrapping (lifāfah) shows that a wrapping does not invalidate the wipe.
This is an analogy (qiyas) or istihsan based on the lesser status of linen compared to a khuff.
4
Analyze the opposing proof
The opponent claims the linen is sewn and thus acts as a deliberate barrier, requiring removal. The author refutes this by noting that cutting it is either futile (if it becomes like a torn khuff) or sinful (waste).
The author labels the opposing view as relying on an unknown authority and being contrary to principles.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The permissive view is the relied-upon position for fatwa. It is supported by al-Hidāyah, al-Kāfī, and the reasoning of later great scholars like al-Ḥalabī and Mulla Khusraw.
The conflict is resolved in favor of the majority, ensuring ease for the community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسح على الخف لكونه فاصلاً وقطعة كرباس تلف على الرجل لا يمنع لأنه غير مقصود باللبس لكن يفهم مما ذكر في الكافي أنه يجوز المسح عليه لأن الخف الغير الصالح للمسح إذا لم يكن فاصلاً فلأن لا يكون الكرباس فاصلاً أولى اهـ . . وقد وقع في عصرنا بين فقهاء الروم بالروم كلام كثير في هذه المسألة فمنهم من بما في فتاوى الشاذي وأفتى بمنع المسح على الخف الذي تحته الكرباس ورد على ابن المالك في عزوه للكافي إذ الظاهر أن المراد به كافي النسفي ولم يوجد فيه ومنهم من أفتى بالجواز وهو الحق لما قدمناه عن غاية البيان ولهذا قال يعقوب باشا إنه مفهوم من الهداية والكافي، ويدل عليه أيضاً ما ذكره الشارحون في مسألة نزع الخف في الكلام مع الشافعي في قوله إنه إذا أعادهما يجوز له المسح من غير غسل الرجلين معللاً بأنه لم يظهر من محل الفرض شيء فقالوا في الرد عليه : إن قوله لم يظهر من محل الفرض شيء» يشكل بما لو أخرج الخفين عن رجليه وعلى الرجلين لفافة فإنه يبطل المسح وإن لم يظهر من محل الفرض شيء اهـ. فهذا ظاهر في صحة المسح على الخف فوق اللفافة. وفي المبتغى بالغين المعجمة : ولو أدخل يده تحت الجرموق ومسح على ظهر الخف لم يجز بخلاف ما لو كان الخرق المانع ظاهر الجرموق وقد ظهر الخف فله المسح على الخف أو على الجرموق لأنهما كخف واحد، وإن كان الخرق يسيراً فمسح على بعض الصحيح وعلى بعض الخرق وهو كله ثلاثة أصابع لم يجزه اهـ. وفي منية المصلي ولا يجوز المسح على الجرموق المتخرق وإن كان خفاه غير متخرق يقال : إن كان الخرق في الجرموق مانعاً لا يجوز المسح عليه وإنما يجوز المسح على الخف لا غير لما علم أن المتخرق خرقاً مانعاً وجوده كعدمه فكانت الوظيفة للخف فلا يجوز المسح على غيره، وقد صرح به في السراج الوهاج فقال : والشرط الثاني لجواز المسح على الجرموق أن يكون الجرموق لو انفرد جاز المسح عليه حتى لو كان به خرق كثير لايجوز المسح عليه. ولا يجوز المسح على الجرموق إذا كان من كرباس ونحوه لأنه لا يمكن قطع السفر وتتابع المشي عليهما كما لو لبسهما على الانفراد إلا أن يكونا رقيقين يصل البلل إلى ما الخف فحينئذ يجوز ويكون مسحاً على الخف كذا في الذخيرة وغيرها. وفي الخلاصة وغيرها ولو كان الجرموقان واسعين يفضل الجرموق من الخف ثلاثة أصابع فمسح على تلك الفضلة لم يجز إلا إذا مسح على الفضلة بعد أن يقدم رجليه على تلك الفضلة فحينئذ جاز، ولو أزال رجليه عن أن أعاد المسح اهـ. وفي التنجيس بعد ذلك الموضع أبي علي الدقاق قال : وفيه نظر ولم يذكر وجهه. وفي القنية جعل الخف كالجرموق في هذا أنه إذا فضل من الجرموق أو الخف قدر ثلاثة أصابع لم يجز المسح عليها. وينبغي اشتهر من كتبهم اكتفاء بما قالوا في مسألة الجرموق من كونه خلفاً عن الرجل. كذا أفاده المولى خسرو في الدرر شرح الغرر، ولا يلتفت إلى ما نقل في شرح المجمع عن فتاوى الشاذي أنه لا يجوز إلا أن يقطع ذلك الملبوس تحت الخف لأنه نقل عن رجل مجهول وهو بعيد عن الفقه خارج عن الأصول لأن قطعه إن كان ليصير كالخف المخروق في عدم جواز المسح عليه فهو بمنزلته بدون خرق لأنه لا يجوز المسح عليه، وإن كان لأجل أن يتصل جزء من الرجل بالخف فهو ليس بشرط وإلا لما جاز المسح على الجرموق ونحوه مع حيلولة الخف فإنه أشد منعاً للاتصال بالرجل. وبهذا ظهر فساد من أيده من الجهال بأن جواز مسح الخف على خلاف القياس فلا يقاس عليه ما لم يرد به نص . فإن هذا كما ترى بطريق الدلالة الراجحة لا بطريق القياس وإلا لما جاز المسح على المكعب واللبود التركية ونحوها لأنها غير منصوص عليها ثم يقال : بل قطع ذلك المخيط قصداً حرام لأنه إضاعة وهي منهي عليها . اهـ كلام الحلبي رحمه الله تعالى قوله : (ويدل عليه أيضاً ما ذكره الشارحون الخ قد يقال : إن ما ذكره الشارحون لا يرد على الشاذي لأن مراده بالمانع ما يلبس وذلك بأن يكون مخيطاً كما في الدرر ، وكلام الشارحين في اللفافة ولم يقل بمنعها بدليل قوله «وقطعة كرباس الخ، إلا أن يقال إن لفظ اللفافة يشمل المخيط أيضاً تأمل قوله : (وينبغي أن يقال الخ) قول المال من غير فائدة
Wiping over the khuff because it is a barrier: a piece of linen wrapped around the foot does not prevent [wiping] because it is not intended for wearing. However, it is understood from what was mentioned in al-Kafi that it is permissible to wipe over it, because if a khuff that is not suitable for wiping is not a barrier, then it is even more apt that linen not be a barrier. End. There occurred in our time among the jurists of the Romans much discussion on this issue. Some of them followed what is in the Fatāwā al-Shādhī and gave fatwa prohibiting wiping over the khuff that has linen underneath, and they rejected Ibn al-Mālik's attribution to al-Kāfī, since it is apparent that what is meant is Kāfī al-Nasafī, and it is not found therein. Some of them gave fatwa permitting it, and that is the correct view, based on what we previously mentioned from Ghāyat al-Bayān. For this reason, Ya'qūb Pasha said that it is understood from al-Hidāyah and al-Kāfī. It is also indicated by what the commentators mentioned in the issue of removing the khuff in the discussion with al-Shāfi'ī about his statement that if one puts them back on, it is permissible to wipe without washing the feet, reasoning that nothing of the place of obligation has appeared. They responded to him: His statement 'nothing of the place of obligation has appeared' is problematic if one takes off the khuffs from his feet and there is a wrapping on the feet, because the wiping would be invalidated even though nothing of the place of obligation has appeared. So this is clear evidence for the validity of wiping over the khuff above the wrapping. In al-Mubtagha: If one inserts his hand under the jarmuq and wipes over the surface of the khuff, it is not valid, unlike if the tearing barrier is on the outer part of the jarmuq and the khuff has appeared, then he may wipe over the khuff or over the jarmuq because they are like a single khuff. But if the tear is small and he wipes over part of the sound part and part of the tear, and the whole is three fingers, it is not valid. End. In Munyat al-Muṣallī: It is not permissible to wipe over a torn jarmuq even if his khuffs are not torn. It is said: If the tear in the jarmuq is a preventer, it is not permissible to wipe over it; rather, it is only permissible to wipe over the khuff, because it is known that a torn tear that is a preventer is as if nonexistent, so the function is for the khuff, and it is not permissible to wipe over other than it. This has been stated explicitly in Sirāj al-Wahhāj: The second condition for the permissibility of wiping over the jarmuq is that if the jarmuq were alone, it would be permissible to wipe over it; such that if it had many tears, it is not permissible to wipe over it. It is not permissible to wipe over a jarmuq made of linen or the like because one cannot perform travel and continuous walking on them, as if one wore them alone, unless they are thin such that moisture reaches the khuff, in which case it is permissible and it is wiping over the khuff. Thus in al-Dhakhīrah and others. In al-Khulāṣah and others: If the jarmuqs are wide, with an excess of three fingers from the jarmuq over the khuff, and one wipes over that excess, it is not valid, unless one wipes over the excess after moving his feet onto that excess, in which case it is valid. If he removes his feet from it and then repeats the wipe? End. In al-Tanjīs after that spot, Abū 'Alī al-Daqqāq said: There is a problem with it, but he did not mention his reason. In al-Qunyah, the khuff is considered like the jarmuq in this: if there is an excess of three fingers from the jarmuq or the khuff, it is not permissible to wipe over it. And it should be: it is well-known from their books that they are satisfied with what they said about the jarmuq being a deputy for the foot. Thus Mulla Khusraw in al-Durar Sharḥ al-Ghurur. And no attention is paid to what is transmitted in Sharḥ al-Majma' from Fatāwā al-Shādhī that it is not permissible unless one cuts that garment under the khuff, because it is transmitted from an unknown man and is far from fiqh and outside the principles. Because if cutting it would make it like a torn khuff in the impermissibility of wiping over it, then it is in the same position without tearing, because wiping over it is not permissible. If it is so that part of the foot can connect to the khuff, that is not a condition; otherwise, it would not be permissible to wipe over the jarmuq and the like with the khuff intervening, which is a stronger prevention of connection to the foot. Thus the invalidity of those who support it from the ignorant by saying that the permissibility of wiping over the khuff is contrary to analogy, so it cannot be analogized to what has no text. For this, as you see, is through preponderant indication, not through analogy; otherwise, it would not be permissible to wipe over the cubed [shoe] and Turkish felt and the like because they are not textually specified. Then it is said: Rather, cutting that sewn material intentionally is forbidden because it is wasting, which is prohibited. End of the statement of al-Halabī, may Allah have mercy on him. His statement: 'And it is also indicated by what the commentators mentioned...' It may be said: 'What the commentators mentioned does not refute al-Shādhī because what he means by preventer is what is worn, and that is by being sewn as in al-Durar, and the commentators' statement is about the wrapping, and he did not say it prevents, evidence being his statement 'and a piece of linen...' unless it is said that the word 'wrapping' includes the sewn also. Consider his statement: 'And it should be said...' The saying of wealth without benefit.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is an extended discussion on the ruling of wiping over khuff (leather socks) when there is a barrier (such as a linen wrapping) underneath the khuff, and also the conditions for wiping over a jarmuq (boot worn over the khuff). The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is presenting arguments from various Hanafi authorities to establish the relied-upon position. The core issue is that a piece of linen (karbas) wrapped around the foot does not prevent wiping over the khuff because it is not intended as footwear. The text then discusses a dispute among later Hanafi jurists (especially from Rum) : some followed the fatwa of al-Shadhi prohibiting wiping if there is linen under the khuff, while others, considered the correct view, permitted it based on al-Hidayah and al-Kafi. The author provides evidence: the discussion by commentators on the case of removing khuff and having a wrapping (lifafah) on the feet, where wiping would be invalidated—showing that a wrapping does not prevent wiping over the khuff. He also cites al-Mubtagha and Munyat al-Musalli regarding jarmuq: if the jarmuq is torn, wiping is not allowed unless the tear is small and the wipe covers three fingers of sound skin, etc. The conditions for jarmuq are detailed: it must be such that if worn alone it would permit wiping (i.e., not torn), it must not be made of linen unless thin enough for moisture to reach the khuff. Also, if the jarmuq is too loose and the excess is more than three fingers, wiping is invalid unless the foot is placed on that excess. The author refutes the view of cutting the material under the khuff as either useless or sinful. Overall, the Hanafi position is that wiping over the khuff is valid despite a non-footwear barrier, and the jarmuq must meet specific conditions.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): Leather sock or boot that covers the feet up to at least the ankles, over which wiping is permissible during wudu.
كرباس (karbas): A piece of linen or coarse cloth wrapped around the foot.
لفافة (lifafah): A wrapping or bandage around the foot, similar to karbas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the main reason the majority of later Hanafis permit wiping over a khuff that has a linen wrap underneath?
A) The linen is thin and moisture can penetrate.
B) The linen is not intended as footwear.
C) The linen is sewn and thus part of the khuff.
D) The linen is a necessary medical covering.

Key Takeaway
A linen wrap under the khuff does not block the validity of wiping because it is not a substitute for footwear.

Conditions for Wiping over Jarmuq (Boots over Khuff)
Conditions for valid wiping over a jarmuq (boot over khuff).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three main conditions for valid wiping over a jarmuq and apply them to real scenarios.

Core Idea
A jarmuq must itself be fit for wiping if worn alone to be a valid surface for wiping.

The source passage also details conditions that make a jarmuq (boot worn over khuff) a valid object for wiping. Understanding these conditions helps avoid invalidating wudu. We will examine the rules for torn jarmuqs, linen jarmuqs, and loose jarmuqs, and how they relate to the khuff underneath.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary condition
The jarmuq must itself be fit for wiping if worn alone. That means it must be thick, untorn, and suitable for continuous walking.
This is the foundational condition; if the jarmuq fails this, wiping on it is invalid.
2
Analyze the condition regarding tears
If the jarmuq has a tear that is a 'preventer' (i.e., significant), wiping over it is not allowed. The author indicates that a tear that is a barrier renders the jarmuq as if nonexistent, so one must wipe the khuff instead.
The condition is that the jarmuq must be sound enough to be considered an independent covering.
3
Examine the material condition
A jarmuq made of linen (karbas) or similar thin material is not permissible for wiping because it cannot withstand continuous walking. However, if it is thin enough that moisture can reach the khuff, then wiping over it is actually wiping over the khuff indirectly, which is valid.
This is a nuanced rule: the jarmuq must either be thick enough to be its own covering or thin enough to transmit moisture.
4
Understand the fit condition
If the jarmuq is too wide, with an excess of three fingers beyond the khuff, wiping on that excess is invalid. The foot must be placed on the excess to bring it into contact, making the wipe valid.
The idea is that the jarmuq should not have loose parts that cannot be considered part of the covering.
5
Apply the rules to a composite scenario
Synthesize the conditions: a valid wipe over a jarmuq requires it to be sound, of appropriate material, and properly fitted. If any condition is missing, one must wipe directly on the khuff.
The khuff always remains the primary object; the jarmuq is only a substitute if it meets all conditions.

Source Text

عن رجليه وعلى الرجلين لفافة فإنه يبطل المسح وإن لم يظهر من محل الفرض شيء اهـ. فهذا ظاهر في صحة المسح على الخف فوق اللفافة. وفي المبتغى بالغين المعجمة : ولو أدخل يده تحت الجرموق ومسح على ظهر الخف لم يجز بخلاف ما لو كان الخرق المانع ظاهر الجرموق وقد ظهر الخف فله المسح على الخف أو على الجرموق لأنهما كخف واحد، وإن كان الخرق يسيراً فمسح على بعض الصحيح وعلى بعض الخرق وهو كله ثلاثة أصابع لم يجزه اهـ. وفي منية المصلي ولا يجوز المسح على الجرموق المتخرق وإن كان خفاه غير متخرق يقال : إن كان الخرق في الجرموق مانعاً لا يجوز المسح عليه وإنما يجوز المسح على الخف لا غير لما علم أن المتخرق خرقاً مانعاً وجوده كعدمه فكانت الوظيفة للخف فلا يجوز المسح على غيره، وقد صرح به في السراج الوهاج فقال : والشرط الثاني لجواز المسح على الجرموق أن يكون الجرموق لو انفرد جاز المسح عليه حتى لو كان به خرق كثير لايجوز المسح عليه. ولا يجوز المسح على الجرموق إذا كان من كرباس ونحوه لأنه لا يمكن قطع السفر وتتابع المشي عليهما كما لو لبسهما على الانفراد إلا أن يكونا رقيقين يصل البلل إلى ما الخف فحينئذ يجوز ويكون مسحاً على الخف كذا في الذخيرة وغيرها. وفي الخلاصة وغيرها ولو كان الجرموقان واسعين يفضل الجرموق من الخف ثلاثة أصابع فمسح على تلك الفضلة لم يجز إلا إذا مسح على الفضلة بعد أن يقدم رجليه على تلك الفضلة فحينئذ جاز، ولو أزال رجليه عن أن أعاد المسح اهـ. وفي التنجيس بعد ذلك الموضع أبي علي الدقاق قال : وفيه نظر ولم يذكر وجهه. وفي القنية جعل الخف كالجرموق في هذا أنه إذا فضل من الجرموق أو الخف قدر ثلاثة أصابع لم يجز المسح عليها. وينبغي اشتهر من كتبهم اكتفاء بما قالوا في مسألة الجرموق من كونه خلفاً عن الرجل. كذا أفاده المولى خسرو في الدرر شرح الغرر، ولا يلتفت إلى ما نقل في شرح المجمع عن فتاوى الشاذي أنه لا يجوز إلا أن يقطع ذلك الملبوس تحت الخف لأنه نقل عن رجل مجهول وهو بعيد عن الفقه خارج عن الأصول لأن قطعه إن كان ليصير كالخف المخروق في عدم جواز المسح عليه فهو بمنزلته بدون خرق لأنه لا يجوز المسح عليه، وإن كان لأجل أن يتصل جزء من الرجل بالخف فهو ليس بشرط وإلا لما جاز المسح على الجرموق ونحوه مع حيلولة الخف فإنه أشد منعاً للاتصال بالرجل. وبهذا ظهر فساد من أيده من الجهال بأن جواز مسح الخف على خلاف القياس فلا يقاس عليه ما لم يرد به نص . فإن هذا كما ترى بطريق الدلالة الراجحة لا بطريق القياس وإلا لما جاز المسح على المكعب واللبود التركية ونحوها لأنها غير منصوص عليها ثم يقال : بل قطع ذلك المخيط قصداً حرام لأنه إضاعة وهي منهي عليها . اهـ كلام الحلبي رحمه الله تعالى قوله : (ويدل عليه أيضاً ما ذكره الشارحون الخ قد يقال : إن ما ذكره الشارحون لا يرد على الشاذي لأن مراده بالمانع ما يلبس وذلك بأن يكون مخيطاً كما في الدرر ، وكلام الشارحين في اللفافة ولم يقل بمنعها بدليل قوله «وقطعة كرباس الخ، إلا أن يقال إن لفظ اللفافة يشمل المخيط أيضاً تأمل قوله : (وينبغي أن يقال الخ) قول المال من غير فائدة
Wiping over the khuff because it is a barrier: a piece of linen wrapped around the foot does not prevent [wiping] because it is not intended for wearing. However, it is understood from what was mentioned in al-Kafi that it is permissible to wipe over it, because if a khuff that is not suitable for wiping is not a barrier, then it is even more apt that linen not be a barrier. End. There occurred in our time among the jurists of the Romans much discussion on this issue. Some of them followed what is in the Fatāwā al-Shādhī and gave fatwa prohibiting wiping over the khuff that has linen underneath, and they rejected Ibn al-Mālik's attribution to al-Kāfī, since it is apparent that what is meant is Kāfī al-Nasafī, and it is not found therein. Some of them gave fatwa permitting it, and that is the correct view, based on what we previously mentioned from Ghāyat al-Bayān. For this reason, Ya'qūb Pasha said that it is understood from al-Hidāyah and al-Kāfī. It is also indicated by what the commentators mentioned in the issue of removing the khuff in the discussion with al-Shāfi'ī about his statement that if one puts them back on, it is permissible to wipe without washing the feet, reasoning that nothing of the place of obligation has appeared. They responded to him: His statement 'nothing of the place of obligation has appeared' is problematic if one takes off the khuffs from his feet and there is a wrapping on the feet, because the wiping would be invalidated even though nothing of the place of obligation has appeared. So this is clear evidence for the validity of wiping over the khuff above the wrapping. In al-Mubtagha: If one inserts his hand under the jarmuq and wipes over the surface of the khuff, it is not valid, unlike if the tearing barrier is on the outer part of the jarmuq and the khuff has appeared, then he may wipe over the khuff or over the jarmuq because they are like a single khuff. But if the tear is small and he wipes over part of the sound part and part of the tear, and the whole is three fingers, it is not valid. End. Key Terms
جرموق (jarmuq): A boot or overshoe worn over the khuff, often made of leather or cloth.
خرق (kharq): A tear or hole in the jarmuq
كرباس (karbas): Linen or coarse cloth

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Wiping over Thick, Soled, or Leather-Lined Socks
States the ruling on wiping over socks with intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of socks that allow wiping in the Hanafi school and explain the intra-madhhab disagreement regarding thick socks.

Core Idea
Leather-lined and soled socks are agreed upon; thick socks are disputed between Abu Hanifah and his two disciples.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq explains the conditions under which a sock (jurab) may be wiped over in place of washing the feet. It distinguishes three types: leather-lined (mujallad), soled (mun‘al), and thick (thakhīn). While the first two are unanimously permissible, the third type—a thick sock without a sole—is disputed between Imam Abu Hanifah and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The passage also clarifies the precise definitions and conditions for each type.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the opening sentence: the text mentions mujallad, mun‘al, and thakhīn. Recognize these as the three types of socks that may be wiped over.
These are not khuffs, but socks that resemble khuffs in function.
2
Define each type
Understand the definitions: mujallad has leather on top and bottom; mun‘al has a leather sole on the bottom; thakhīn is thick, stays on without tying, and is not transparent.
Pronunciation variants for mun‘al are noted in the text.
3
Note the conditions
For the soled sock, the sole must reach at least the bottom of the foot (Zahir al-Riwayah), or the ankles according to a narration from Hasan. For the thick sock, it must stand on its own and not reveal the skin.
These conditions affect validity.
4
Locate the dispute
The text states: 'If it is thick, it is impermissible according to Abu Hanifah. They (Sahibayn) said: It is permissible.' This is the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
The dispute only applies to thick socks without a sole or leather lining.
5
Analyze the evidence
The Sahibayn cite a hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) wiping over socks (narrated by al-Mughirah). Abu Hanifah argues via qiyas that socks are not khuffs and require a sole or lining to serve the same purpose.
The passage ends mid-sentence but the dalil is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والجورب المجلد والمنعل والثخين) أي يجوز المسح على الجورب إذا كان مجلداً أو منعلاً أو ثخيناً. ويقال جورب مجلد إذا وضع الجلد على أعلاه وأسفله، وجورب مُنَعل ومَنْعَل الذي وضع على أسفله جلدة كالنعل للقدم. وفي المستصفى أنعل الخف ونعله جعل له نعلاً، وهكذا في كثير من الكتب، فيجوز في المنعل تشديد العين مع فتح النون كما يجوز تسكين النون وتخفيف العين. وفي معراج الدراية والمنعل بالتخفيف وسكون النون والظاهر ما قدمناه كما لا يخفى. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان ثم على رواية الحسن ينبغي أن يكون النعل إلى الكعبين، وفي ظاهر الرواية إذا بلغ النعل إلى أسفل القدم جاز، والثخين أن يقوم على الساق من غير شد ولا يسقط ولا يشف .اهـ. وفي التبيين ولا يرى ما تحته. ثم المسح على الجورب إذا كان منعلاً جائز اتفاقاً، وإذا كان لم يكن منعلاً وكان رقيقاً غير جائز اتفاقاً، وإن كان ثخيناً فهو غير جائز عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : يجوز لما رواه الترمذي عن المغيرة بن شعبة
His statement: 'And the sock that is leather-lined, soled, and thick' means it is permissible to wipe over the sock if it is leather-lined, soled, or thick. It is said: a leather-lined sock is one with leather on its upper and lower parts; a soled sock is one with a piece of leather on its lower part like a sole for the foot. In al-Mustasfa: 'anna'la al-khuff and na'lahu means he made a sole for it, and similarly in many books. So in 'al-mun'al' (with shaddah on 'ayn and fatha on noon) is permissible, as is 'al-man'al' (with sukun on noon and tashdid on 'ayn). In Mi'raj al-Diraya: 'al-mun'al' is with tashdid and sukun on noon, but the apparent is what we presented. In Fatawa Qadikhan: According to the narration of Hasan, the sole should reach the ankles; according to Zahir al-Riwayah, if the sole reaches the bottom of the foot, it is permissible. The thick [sock] is one that stays on the shin without tying, does not fall down, and is not transparent. End. In al-Tabyin: And nothing underneath it is visible. Then: Wiping over a sock that is soled is permissible by consensus; if it is not soled and is thin, it is impermissible by consensus; if it is thick, it is impermissible according to Abu Hanifah. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is permissible, based on what al-Tirmidhi narrated from al-Mughirah bin Shu'bah.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on wiping over socks (jawārib) during wudu. The author states three categories: (1) mujallad – lined with leather on top and bottom; (2) munʿal – having a leather sole; (3) thakhīn – thick enough to stay on the leg without slipping and non-transparent. The ruling is that wiping over these types is permissible. The author clarifies the pronunciation of 'munʿal' and refers to Fatawa Qadikhan for the condition that the sole must reach at least the bottom of the foot in the apparent narration, while in the narration of Hasan, it should reach the ankles. The thick sock must also not reveal the skin. An intra-madhhab dispute is noted: if the sock is thick but not soled, Abu Hanifah rules it impermissible to wipe over, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule it permissible, citing a hadith from al-Tirmidhi narrated by al-Mughirah bin Shu'bah (that the Prophet wiped over socks). This ikhtilaf hinges on whether thick socks are considered analogous to khuffs. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the commentary in the original book likely continues with the hadith and the Hanafi response.

Key Terms
الجورب المجلد (al-jawrab al-mujallad): A sock that has leather on both its upper and lower parts, making it like a khuff.
المنعل (al-munʿal): A sock that has a leather sole attached to the bottom, like a shoe.
الثخين (al-thakhīn): A thick sock that stays on the shin without tying, does not fall, and is not transparent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling of Abu Hanifah regarding wiping over a thick sock (thakhīn) that is not soled or leather-lined?
A) Permissible by consensus.
B) Permissible, based on a hadith.
C) Not permissible.
D) Permissible only if it reaches the ankles.

Key Takeaway
Thick socks are permissible for wiping only according to the Sahibayn; Abu Hanifah restricts to soled or leather-lined socks.

Wiping Over Overshoes (Jarmaq): Conditions and Rulings
States conditions for valid wiping over overshoes (jarmaq) and rulings on material and fit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid wiping over a jarmaq and apply them to determine whether a particular wiping is valid.

Core Idea
A jarmaq is valid for wiping only if it itself meets the conditions of a khuff — material, fit, and no large holes.

Wiping over the khuff is a well-known concession in wudu. However, when an overshoe (jarmaq) is worn over the khuff, additional conditions must be met. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details those conditions, emphasizing that the jarmaq must itself be a valid wiping surface, of appropriate material without excessive protrusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object and ruling
The passage discusses wiping over a jarmaq (overshoe) worn over a khuff. The basic ruling is that wiping is on the khuff; the jarmaq is secondary.
Remember, the khuff is the primary surface.
2
Check the jarmaq's own validity
The jarmaq must itself be valid for wiping if worn alone. This means it must meet the conditions of a khuff: made of leather or similar material, no large holes, and capable of supporting travel.
If the jarmaq has many holes, it is as if it does not exist.
3
Inspect the material
If the jarmaq is made of karbas (coarse cloth) or similar, wiping is impermissible because it cannot be used for travel. The exception is if the material is thin enough that moisture can pass through to the khuff.
The principle: the jarmaq must be suitable for walking, not flimsy.
4
Examine the fit (protrusion)
If the jarmaq is too wide so that three fingers of it protrude beyond the khuff, wiping on that protrusion alone is invalid. However, if the wearer positions the foot over the protrusion (i.e., moves the foot forward) and then wipes, it becomes valid.
The same rule applies to the khuff itself.
5
Consider the critical note
Abu Ali al-Daqqaq found consideration in the ruling on protrusion, but did not elaborate. This shows the text is open to scholarly scrutiny.
Not all scholars agree on every detail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على الخف لا غير لما علم أن المتخرق خرقاً مانعاً وجوده كعدمه فكانت الوظيفة للخف فلا يجوز المسح على غيره، وقد صرح به في السراج الوهاج فقال : والشرط الثاني لجواز المسح على الجرموق أن يكون الجرموق لو انفرد جاز المسح عليه حتى لو كان به خرق كثير لايجوز المسح عليه. ولا يجوز المسح على الجرموق إذا كان من كرباس ونحوه لأنه لا يمكن قطع السفر وتتابع المشي عليهما كما لو لبسهما على الانفراد إلا أن يكونا رقيقين يصل البلل إلى ما الخف فحينئذ يجوز ويكون مسحاً على الخف كذا في الذخيرة وغيرها. وفي الخلاصة وغيرها ولو كان الجرموقان واسعين يفضل الجرموق من الخف ثلاثة أصابع فمسح على تلك الفضلة لم يجز إلا إذا مسح على الفضلة بعد أن يقدم رجليه على تلك الفضلة فحينئذ جاز، ولو أزال رجليه عن أن أعاد المسح اهـ. وفي التنجيس بعد ذلك الموضع أبي علي الدقاق قال : وفيه نظر ولم يذكر وجهه. وفي القنية جعل الخف كالجرموق في هذا أنه إذا فضل من الجرموق أو الخف قدر ثلاثة أصابع لم يجز المسح عليها.
On the khuff only, because it is known that a khuff torn with a tear that prevents [wiping] is like nonexistent, so the function is for the khuff, and wiping on other than it is not permissible. It is stated explicitly in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The second condition for the permissibility of wiping on the jarmaq (overshoe) is that if the jarmaq were alone, wiping on it would be permissible; even if it had many holes, wiping on it is not permissible. And wiping on the jarmaq is not permissible if it is made of karbas (coarse cloth) or similar, because it is not possible to travel and walk continuously on them, just as if they were worn alone, unless they are thin so that moisture reaches the khuff; then it is permissible and it is wiping on the khuff. Thus in al-Dhakhira and others. And in al-Khulasa and others: If the two jarmaqs are wide such that three fingers of the jarmaq protrude beyond the khuff, and he wipes on that protruding part, it is not valid unless he wipes after placing his feet on that protrusion [i.e., after moving them forward] then it is valid. If he removes his feet without repeating the wiping, [it is not valid]. In al-Tanqih after that, Abu 'Ali al-Daqqaq said: There is consideration in this, but he did not mention its aspect. And in al-Qunyah, the khuff is treated like the jarmaq in this: if three fingers' length protrudes from the jarmaq or the khuff, wiping on it is not permissible.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the conditions for wiping over overshoes (jarmaq) worn over the khuff. The commentator explains that the basic principle is that wiping is on the khuff alone; if the jarmaq has a defect that prevents wiping (like large holes), it is treated as nonexistent. He then quotes al-Siraj al-Wahhaj stating the second condition: the jarmaq itself must be valid for wiping if worn alone. This means it must meet the requirements of a khuff (e.g., leather, covering the feet ankles, permissible to wipe). If it has many holes, it is not valid. Next, he discusses material: jarmaq made of karbas (a coarse cloth) or similar is not permissible because it cannot support walking over long distances, unless it is thin enough that moisture can pass through, then wiping directly on the khuff is allowed. Then he addresses fit: if the jarmaq is wide so that three fingers of it protrude beyond the khuff, wiping only on that part is not valid unless one first positions the feet so that the protrusion is covered by the foot. Finally, he notes a review by Abu 'Ali al-Daqqaq who found consideration in this ruling but did not elaborate. The passage also equates the khuff with the jarmaq regarding protrusion: if three fingers protrude, wiping is invalid.

Key Terms
الجرموق (al-jarmuq): An overshoe worn over the khuff, made of leather or similar material.
الخف (al-khuff): A leather sock or boot covering the foot up to the ankle, over which wiping is permissible.
كرباس (karbas): A coarse cloth material; jarmaq of this is invalid for wiping unless thin enough to transmit moisture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is wiping on a jarmaq that protrudes three fingers beyond the khuff valid?
A) When the jarmaq is made of leather.
B) When the foot is positioned over the protrusion before wiping.
C) When the jarmaq has no holes.
D) When the jarmaq is thick.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over a jarmaq is only valid if the jarmaq itself meets the conditions of a valid wiping surface, including material, no large holes, and proper fit.

Wiping Over Socks (Jurab): The Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Final Fatwa
Defines sock types and presents intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the types of socks that permit wiping, explain the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and state the relied-upon Hanafi fatwa.

Core Idea
The Hanafi fatwa permits wiping on thick or soled socks, despite Abu Hanifa's initial objection — his retraction settled the school.

Wiping over socks (jurab) during wudu is a practical necessity in cold climates. The Hanafi school has detailed rules on which socks qualify, including a famous intra-school disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson clarifies the definitions, the points of consensus and dispute, and the final operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of socks
The passage defines three types that are relevant: mujallad (leathered on top and bottom), mun'al (soled with leather on the bottom), and thakhin (thick, self-standing, not transparent).
Also note the five-fold classification of sock materials: mar'azi, ghazl, sha'r, jild raqiq, and karbas.
2
State what is agreed upon
All scholars agree: wiping on a soled or leathered sock is permissible; wiping on a thin unsoled sock is impermissible.
These are the extreme cases with no disagreement.
3
Present the dispute
The disagreement is over thick unsoled socks. Abu Hanifa initially said impermissible; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said permissible. Then note Abu Hanifa's reported retraction.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute, later resolved.
4
Examine the proofs
The Sahibayn relied on the hadith of al-Mughira (Tirmidhi) and the analogy that a thick sock allows walking. Abu Hanifa argued that a thick sock without a sole does not permit continuous walking, so it is not like a khuff.
The text also defends the hadith's authenticity against criticisms.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The majority of Hanafi books and the final fatwa follow the Sahibayn, reinforced by Abu Hanifa's retraction. Wiping on any thick or soled sock is permissible.
Exceptions: thin socks, mar'azi (fine goat hair), and karbas (coarse cloth) are never permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والجورب المجلد والمنعل والثخين) أي يجوز المسح على الجورب إذا كان مجلداً أو منعلاً أو ثخيناً. ويقال جورب مجلد إذا وضع الجلد على أعلاه وأسفله، وجورب مُنَعل ومَنْعَل الذي وضع على أسفله جلدة كالنعل للقدم. وفي المستصفى أنعل الخف ونعله جعل له نعلاً، وهكذا في كثير من الكتب، فيجوز في المنعل تشديد العين مع فتح النون كما يجوز تسكين النون وتخفيف العين. وفي معراج الدراية والمنعل بالتخفيف وسكون النون والظاهر ما قدمناه كما لا يخفى. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان ثم على رواية الحسن ينبغي أن يكون النعل إلى الكعبين، وفي ظاهر الرواية إذا بلغ النعل إلى أسفل القدم جاز، والثخين أن يقوم على الساق من غير شد ولا يسقط ولا يشف .اهـ. وفي التبيين ولا يرى ما تحته. ثم المسح على الجورب إذا كان منعلاً جائز اتفاقاً، وإذا كان لم يكن منعلاً وكان رقيقاً غير جائز اتفاقاً، وإن كان ثخيناً فهو غير جائز عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : يجوز لما رواه الترمذي عن المغيرة بن شعبة قال : توضأ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ومسح على الجوربين. وقال حديث حسن صحيح. ورواه ابن حبان في صحيحه أيضاً. ولأنه يمكن المشي فيه إذا كان ثخيناً. وله أنه ليس في معنى الخف لأنه لا يمكن مواظبة المشي فيه إلا إذا كان منعلاً وهو محمل الحديث. وعنه أنه رجع إلى قولهما وعليه الفتوى. كذا في الهداية وأكثر الكتب لأنه في معنى الخف، فالتأويل المذكور للحديث قصر لدلالته عن مقتضاه بغیر سبب فلا يسمع على أن الظاهر أنه لو كان المراد به ذلك لنص عليه الراوي، هذا بخلاف الرقيق فإن الدليل يفيد إخراجه من الاطلاق لكونه ليس في معنى الخف، وما نقل من تضعيفه عن الإمام أحمد وابن مهدي ومسلم حتى قال النووي كل منهم لو انفرد قدم على الترمذي مع أن الجرح مقدم على التعديل فلا يضر لكونه روي من طرق متعددة ذكرها الزيلعي المخرج وهي وإن كانت كلها ضعيفة اعتضد بعضها ببعض، والضعيف إذا روي من طرق صار حسناً . الصحابة من غير نكير منهم على فاعله كما ذكره أبو داود في سننه. ثم مع هذا كله لم يوجد من المعنى ما يقوى على الاستقلال بالمنع فلا جرم إن كان الفتوى على الجواز وما في البدائع من أنها حكاية حال لا عموم لها فمسلم لو لم يرد ما رواه الطبراني عن بلال قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يمسح الخفين والجوربين. وفي الخلاصة : فإن كان الجورب من مرعزي وصوف لا يجوز المسح عليه عندهم. المزعِز بميم مكسورة وقد تفتح فراء ساكنة فمهملة مكسورة فزاي مشددة مفتوحة فالف مقصورة وقد تمد مع تخفيف الزاي وقد تحذف مع بقاء التشديد: الزغب الذي تحت شعر العنز. كذا في شرح النقاية. وفي المجتبى : لا يجوز المسح على الجورب الرقيق من غزل أو شعر بلا خلاف، ولو كان ثخيناً يمشي معه فرسخاً فصاعداً كجورب أهل مرو فعلى الخلاف. وكذا الجورب من جلد رقيق على الخلاف، ويجوز على الجوارب اللبدية. وعن أبي ما ظهر من مسح كثير من على تقسيماً في ا الجورب فقال : ذكر نجم الدين الزاهدي عن شمس الأئمة الحلواني أن الجورب خمسة أنواع : من المرعزي والغزل والشعر والجلد الرقيق والكرباس. قال : وذكر التفاصيل في الأربعة من الثخين والرقيق والمنعل وغير المنعل والمبطن وغير المبطن، وأما الخامس فلا يجوز المسح عليه كيفما كان اهـ. ونحوه في التتارخانية عنه : والمراد من التفصيل في الأربعة أن ما كان رقيقاً منها لا يجوز المسح عليه اتفاقاً إلا أن يكون مجلداً أو منعلاً أو مبطناً، وما كان ثخيناً منها فإن لم يكن مجلداً أو منعلاً أو مبطناً فمختلف فيه، وما كان فلا خلاف فيه اهـ. والمرعزي كما سيأتي مضبوطاً الزغب الذي تحت شعر العنز، والغزل ما غزل من الصوف والكرباس ما نسج من مغزول القطن قال الحلبي : ويلحق بالكرباس كل ما كان من نوع الخيط كالكتان والإبريسم أي الحرير ثم قال بعد ما تقدم: فعلم من هذا أن ما يعمل من الجوخ إذا جلد أو نعل أو بطن يجوز المسح عليه لأنه أحد الأربعة وليس من الكرباس فهو داخل فيما يجوز المسح عليه لو كان ثخيناً بحيث يمكن أن يمشي معه فرسخ من غير
His saying (and the sock that is leathered, soled, or thick): i.e., it is permissible to wipe over the sock if it is leathered, soled, or thick. It is said a sock is "mujallad" (leathered) if leather is placed on its upper and lower parts, and a sock is "mun'al" or "man'al" (soled) which is one on whose lower part a piece of leather is placed like a sole for the foot. In al-Mustasfa: 'ana'ala al-khuff wa na'alahu' means he put a sole on it; similarly in many books. So it is permissible in 'al-mun'al' with shaddah on the 'ayn and fathah on the nun, as well as with sukun on the nun and tashdid on the 'ayn. In Mi'raj al-Dirayah, 'al-mun'al' is with tashdid and sukun on the nun, but the apparent is what we presented. In Fatawa Qadikhan: on the narration of al-Hasan, the sole should reach the ankles; in Zahir al-Riwayah, if the sole reaches the bottom of the foot, it is permissible. The thick (al-thakhin) is that which stands on the leg without tying, does not fall, and does not become transparent. In al-Tabyin: one cannot see what is beneath it. Then wiping on a sock if it is soled is permissible by agreement; if it is not soled and is thin, it is impermissible by agreement. If it is thick, it is impermissible according to Abu Hanifa. But the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is permissible, because of what al-Tirmidhi narrated from al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba: The Prophet (peace be upon him) performed ablution and wiped over the socks. He said: a hasan sahih hadith. Ibn Hibban also narrated it in his Sahih. And because one can walk while wearing them if they are thick. (Abu Hanifa) argued that it is not analogous to the khuff because one cannot continuously walk wearing it unless it is soled, and that is the interpretation of the hadith. It is reported that he (Abu Hanifa) retracted to the view of the two, and the fatwa is upon that. Thus in al-Hidayah and most books, because it is analogous to the khuff, and the mentioned interpretation of the hadith restricts its indication without reason, so it is not accepted. Moreover, the apparent meaning is that if it were intended to restrict, the narrator would have stated it. This is unlike the thin sock because the evidence excludes it from the general scope as it is not analogous to the khuff. As for the criticism of the hadith by Imam Ahmad, Ibn Mahdi, and Muslim, even al-Nawawi said that each of them, if alone, would be preferred over al-Tirmidhi, but jarh (criticism) takes precedence over ta'dil (commendation); however, it does not harm because it is narrated through multiple chains which al-Zayla'i mentioned, and although each chain is weak, they support each other, and a weak hadith narrated through multiple chains becomes hasan. The Companions did not object to one who did it, as Abu Dawood mentioned in his Sunan. Moreover, with all this, no meaning was found strong enough to independently prevent it, so inevitably the fatwa is on permissibility. What is in al-Bada'i that it is a report of a specific incident with no general application is conceded, even if al-Tabarani's narration from Bilal were not reported: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to wipe over the khuffs and the socks. In al-Khulasa: if the sock is made of mar'azi and wool, wiping is not permissible according to them. Al-mar'azi (spelling variants) is the fine hair under goat hair. Thus in Sharh al-Nuqayah. In al-Mujtaba: wiping is not permissible on a thin sock of spun yarn or hair without dispute. If it is thick so that one can walk a farsakh or more, like the socks of the people of Marw, then it is subject to dispute. Similarly, a sock of thin leather is subject to dispute. And it is permissible on felt socks. From Abu... Najm al-Din al-Zahidi narrated from Shams al-A'imma al-Hilwani that socks are of five types: mar'azi, spun yarn, hair, thin leather, and karbas. He said: details are mentioned for the four: thick, thin, soled, unsoled, lined, unlined. As for the fifth (karbas), wiping on it is not permissible in any case. Similar in al-Tatar Khaniyya: the meaning of the detail for the four is that whatever is thin among them, wiping is not permissible by agreement unless it is leathered, soled, or lined. Whatever is thick among them, if not leathered, soled, or lined, it is disputed. As for (the remaining cases), there is no dispute. Al-mar'azi is the fine hair under goat hair; al-ghazl is spun wool; al-karbas is woven from spun cotton. Al-Halabi said: karbas includes everything of the type of thread, like linen and silk. Then he said: from this it is understood that what is made of cloth (jūkh) if leathered, soled, or lined, wiping on it is permissible because it is among the four and not karbas; it is included in what is permissible to wipe on if it is thick such that one can walk a farsakh in it without (difficulty).
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with wiping over socks (jurab). It begins by defining three types of socks that permit wiping: mujallad (leathered on top and bottom), mun'al (soled with a piece of leather on the bottom), and thakhin (thick enough to stand without falling and not transparent). The author discusses the pronunciation and details of these types. He then states the agreement: wiping is permissible on a soled sock by consensus, and on a thin unsoled sock impermissible by consensus. The dispute concerns thick unsoled socks: Abu Hanifa initially ruled it impermissible because such socks are not analogous to the khuff (leather boot) since they cannot support continuous walking. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) ruled it permissible, citing the hadith of al-Mughira that the Prophet wiped over socks, and because a thick sock can be walked in. They also note that Abu Hanifa later retracted to their view, and the fatwa is on permissibility. The text then defends the hadith against criticisms of weakness by noting multiple chains. It further categorizes socks into five types according to al-Hilwani: mar'azi (fine goat hair), spun yarn, hair, thin leather, and karbas (coarse cloth). The first four are subject to detail based on thickness, soling, and lining; the fifth (karbas) is never permissible. The passage concludes that any material, like felt or cloth (jūkh), if leathered, soled, or lined, and thick enough to walk a farsakh, becomes permissible.

Key Terms
الجورب (al-jurab): A sock or foot covering, usually of cloth or felt, over which wiping during ablution is debated.
المجلد (al-mujallad): A sock that has leather attached to its upper and lower parts.
المنعل (al-mun'al): A sock with a leather sole attached to its bottom, like a slipper.
الثخين (al-thakhin): A thick sock that stands on its own without falling and is not transparent.
المرعزي (al-mar'azi): Fine hair under goat hair, used to make soft socks.
الكرباس (al-karbas): Coarse woven cloth (from cotton, linen, or silk), used for socks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi fatwa (mufta bihi), which of the following socks is permissible to wipe over during wudu?
A) A thin cotton sock.
B) A thick woollen sock without a sole.
C) A sock made of fine goat hair (mar'azi).
D) A sock made of karbas (coarse woven cloth).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits wiping on thick or soled socks; the initial opposition by Abu Hanifa was overruled by his own retraction and the stronger evidence of the Sahibayn.

Ruling on Wiping over Jorab (Socks) in Wudu
Explaining the permissibility and conditions of wiping over socks in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over socks and identify the conditions (thickness, lining) that determine permissibility, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Wiping over socks is permissible only if the socks are thick and lined/soled — the later Hanafi position mufta bihi.

Wiping over khuff (leather socks) is well-known, but what about ordinary socks? The Hanafi school has a detailed ruling based on the Prophet's practice. In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, we explore the conditions and the intra-Hanafi dispute that led to the current fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is wiping over socks (jorab) in wudu. The ruling is permissible (ja'iz) under certain conditions.
The act is a substitute for washing the feet.
2
Trace the dispute within the Hanafi school
Imam Abu Hanifa initially did not allow wiping over socks unless they were soled like a khuff. He later retracted and adopted the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, allowing it if the socks are thick and can be walked in.
The fatwa is on the latter view.
3
Analyze the conditions for permissibility
The key conditions: the sock must be thick enough to walk a farsakh (approx. 5 km) and must be lined (mujallad), soled (mun'al), or quilted (mubattan). Thin socks are not allowed by consensus.
The text provides a classification of five sock types.
4
Apply the conditions to classify sock types
From the classification: socks made of mar'azi, yarn, hair, leather, and cotton fabric (kirbas). For the first four, thin ones require lining; thick ones are disputed unless lined. The fifth (kirbas) is never allowed.
Modern examples: woolen socks with leather patches fall under permissible.

Source Text

كتاب الطهارة - باب المسح على
قال : توضأ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ومسح على الجوربين. وقال حديث حسن صحيح. ورواه ابن حبان في صحيحه أيضاً. ولأنه يمكن المشي فيه إذا كان ثخيناً. وله أنه ليس في معنى الخف لأنه لا يمكن مواظبة المشي فيه إلا إذا كان منعلاً وهو محمل الحديث. وعنه أنه رجع إلى قولهما وعليه الفتوى. كذا في الهداية وأكثر الكتب لأنه في معنى الخف، فالتأويل المذكور للحديث قصر لدلالته عن مقتضاه بغیر سبب فلا يسمع على أن الظاهر أنه لو كان المراد به ذلك لنص عليه الراوي، هذا بخلاف الرقيق فإن الدليل يفيد إخراجه من الاطلاق لكونه ليس في معنى الخف، وما نقل من تضعيفه عن الإمام أحمد وابن مهدي ومسلم حتى قال النووي كل منهم لو انفرد قدم على الترمذي مع أن الجرح مقدم على التعديل فلا يضر لكونه روي من طرق متعددة ذكرها الزيلعي المخرج وهي وإن كانت كلها ضعيفة اعتضد بعضها ببعض، والضعيف إذا روي من طرق صار حسناً . الصحابة من غير نكير منهم على فاعله كما ذكره أبو داود في سننه. ثم مع هذا كله لم يوجد من المعنى ما يقوى على الاستقلال بالمنع فلا جرم إن كان الفتوى على الجواز وما في البدائع من أنها حكاية حال لا عموم لها فمسلم لو لم يرد ما رواه الطبراني عن بلال قال : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يمسح الخفين والجوربين. وفي الخلاصة : فإن كان الجورب من مرعزي وصوف لا يجوز المسح عليه عندهم. المزعِز بميم مكسورة وقد تفتح فراء ساكنة فمهملة مكسورة فزاي مشددة مفتوحة فالف مقصورة وقد تمد مع تخفيف الزاي وقد تحذف مع بقاء التشديد: الزغب الذي تحت شعر العنز. كذا في شرح النقاية. وفي المجتبى : لا يجوز المسح على الجورب الرقيق من غزل أو شعر بلا خلاف، ولو كان ثخيناً يمشي معه فرسخاً فصاعداً كجورب أهل مرو فعلى الخلاف. وكذا الجورب من جلد رقيق على الخلاف، ويجوز على الجوارب اللبدية. وعن أبي [؟] ما ظهر من مسح كثير من على تقسيماً في ا الجورب فقال : ذكر نجم الدين الزاهدي عن شمس الأئمة الحلواني أن الجورب خمسة أنواع : من المرعزي والغزل والشعر والجلد الرقيق والكرباس. قال : وذكر التفاصيل في الأربعة من الثخين والرقيق والمنعل وغير المنعل والمبطن وغير المبطن، وأما الخامس فلا يجوز المسح عليه كيفما كان اهـ. ونحوه في التتارخانية عنه : والمراد من التفصيل في الأربعة أن ما كان رقيقاً منها لا يجوز المسح عليه اتفاقاً إلا أن يكون مجلداً أو منعلاً أو مبطناً، وما كان ثخيناً منها فإن لم يكن مجلداً أو منعلاً أو مبطناً فمختلف فيه، وما كان فلا خلاف فيه اهـ. والمرعزي كما سيأتي مضبوطاً الزغب الذي تحت شعر العنز، والغزل ما غزل من الصوف والكرباس ما نسج من مغزول القطن قال الحلبي : ويلحق بالكرباس كل ما كان من نوع الخيط كالكتان والإبريسم أي الحرير ثم قال بعد ما تقدم: فعلم من هذا أن ما يعمل من الجوخ إذا جلد أو نعل أو بطن يجوز المسح عليه لأنه أحد الأربعة وليس من الكرباس فهو داخل فيما يجوز المسح عليه لو كان ثخيناً بحيث يمكن أن يمشي معه فرسخ من غير
كتاب الطهارة - باب المسح على الخفين
حنيفة لا يجوز قالوا ولو شاهد أبو حنيفة صلابتها لأفتى بالجواز. ويجوز على الجاروق المشقوق على ظهر القدم وله أزرار يشده عليه يسده لأنه كغير المشقوق، وإن ظهر القدم شيء فهو كخروق الخف . قلت : وأما لخف الدوراني الذي يعتاده فقهاء زماننا فإن كان مجلداً يستر جلده الكعب يجوز وإلا فلا. كذا في معراج الدراية. وفي الخلاصة : المسح على الجاروق إن كان يستر القدم ولا يرى من الكعب ولا من ظهر القدم إلا قدر أصبع أو أصبعين جاز المسح عليه، وإن لم يكن كذلك ولكن ستر القدم بالجلد إن كان الجلد متصلاً بالجاروق بالخرز جاز المسح عليه، وإن شد بشيء لا . ولو ستر القدم باللفافة جوزه مشايخ سمرقند ولم يجوزه مشايخ بخاری .اهـ. ثم ذكر التفصيل المذكور للجورق عن المجتبى في الجورب من الشعر. وفيها أيضاً: وتفسير النعل أن يكون الجورب المنعل كجوارب الصبيان الذين يمشون عليها في تخونة الجورب وغلظ النعل . وفي فتاوى قاضيخان: إن الجورق اسم فارسي لخف معروف، وعامة المشايخ على أنه إذا كان يظهر من ظهر القدم قدر ثلاثة أصابع لا يجوز، وبعضهم جوزوا ذلك لأن عوام الناس يسافرون به خصوصاً في بلاد المشرق، أما إذا كان يظهر منه قدر أصبع أو أصبعين فإنه يجوز في قولهم.
Chapter of Purification – Section on Wiping. He said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) performed wudu and wiped over the two socks. And he said it is a good authentic hadith. Ibn Hibban also narrated it in his Sahih. And because one can walk in them if they are thick. And it is for him that it is not analogous to the khuff because continual walking in it is not possible unless it is soled (mun'al), and that is the interpretation of the hadith. And it is reported from him that he returned to their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) opinion, and the fatwa is upon that. This is in al-Hidayah and most books because it is analogous to the khuff. Thus the mentioned interpretation of the hadith restricts its indication from its requirement without cause, so it is not accepted. Moreover, it is apparent that if that were intended, the narrator would have stated it. This is unlike the thin (sock) because the evidence indicates its exclusion from the general ruling since it is not analogous to the khuff. What is narrated about its weakening from Imam Ahmad, Ibn Mahdi, and Muslim, to the extent that al-Nawawi said each one of them if alone would take precedence over al-Tirmidhi despite that jarh (criticism) takes precedence over ta'dil (validation), does not harm because it has been narrated through multiple chains mentioned by al-Zayla'i in al-Mukharraj, and although all are weak, they strengthen each other, and a weak hadith narrated through multiple chains becomes hasan. The Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) did not disapprove of the one who did it, as Abu Dawud mentioned in his Sunan. Then, despite all this, there is no (legal) meaning strong enough to independently necessitate prohibition, so the fatwa is on permissibility. What is in al-Bada'i' that it is a description of a situation and not general is valid if the hadith of al-Tabarani from Bilal had not been narrated: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to wipe over khuffs and socks.' In al-Khulasa: If the sock is of mar'azi (a type of wool) and wool, it is not permissible to wipe over it according to them. Al-Mar'azi: with a kasra on the meem, sometimes fatha, sukun on the ra, kasra on the 'ayn, shadda on the za, fatha, then alif maqsura, sometimes elongated with tashil of za, sometimes omitted while keeping the shadda: the down under the goat hair. This is in Sharh al-Niqaya. In al-Mujtaba: It is not permissible to wipe over a thin sock made of yarn or hair without dispute, but if it is thick and one can walk a farsakh or more with it, like the socks of the people of Marw, then there is dispute. Similarly, a sock of thin leather is disputed. And wiping over felt socks is permissible. From Abu [?] there appeared a detailed classification of the sock. He said: Najm al-Din al-Zahidi narrated from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani that the sock is of five types: mar'azi, yarn, hair, thin leather, and cotton fabric (kirbas). He said: And he mentioned the details for the four (types) regarding thick and thin, soled and unsoled, lined and unlined. As for the fifth, it is not permissible to wipe over it in any case. End quote. Similar is in al-Tatarkhaniyya from him: The meaning of the detail for the four is that what is thin among them is not permissible to wipe over by consensus unless it is lined (mujallad) or soled (mun'al) or lined (mubattan). And what is thick among them, if it is not lined, soled, or lined, then there is dispute, and what is (thick and lined/soled) there is no dispute about its permissibility. End quote. Mar'azi, as will come, is defined as the down under the goat hair. Yarn is what is spun from wool. Kirbas is what is woven from spun cotton. Al-Halabi said: To kirbas is attached everything that is of the type of thread, like linen and silk (ibrism = silk). Then he said after what preceded: From this it is known that what is made of broadcloth (jukh) if it is lined, soled, or quilted, it is permissible to wipe over it because it is one of the four and not of kirbas, so it falls under what is permissible to wipe over if it is thick such that one can walk with it a farsakh without (hindrance).
Chapter of Purification – Section on Wiping over Khuffs. Hanifa (Abu Hanifa) said it is not permissible. They said: If Abu Hanifa had seen their firmness (solidity), he would have ruled permissibility. And wiping over the jaroq (a type of sock) that is slit on the top of the foot and has buttons that the wearer fastens is permissible because it is like a non-slit (sock). If something of the top of the foot appears, it is like holes in the khuff. I (the commentator) say: As for the durani khuff that the jurists of our time are accustomed to, if it is lined and its leather covers the ankle, it is permissible; otherwise not. This is in Mi'raj al-Diraya. In al-Khulasa: Wiping over the jaroq if it covers the foot and nothing is seen of the ankle or the top of the foot except the amount of a finger or two fingers, wiping over it is permissible. If it is not like that but the foot is covered with leather and the leather is attached to the jaroq with stitching, wiping over it is permissible. If it is tied with something, it is not. If the foot is covered with a wrapper, the scholars of Samarkand permitted it, but the scholars of Bukhara did not. End quote. Then he mentioned the aforementioned detail for the joroq from al-Mujtaba regarding the sock of hair. And in it also: The interpretation of being soled (na'l) is that the sock is soled like the socks of boys who walk on them in the thickness of the sock and the coarseness of the sole. In Fatawa Qadikhan: Joroq is a Persian name for a well-known khuff. The general body of scholars hold that if there appears from the top of the foot the amount of three fingers, it is not permissible. Some permitted it because the common people travel with it, especially in the lands of the East. If there appears from it the amount of a finger or two fingers, then it is permissible according to their saying.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion on the ruling of wiping over socks (jorab) during wudu. The author begins by citing the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) wiping over his socks, which is the primary proof. He then addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa initially did not allow wiping over socks unless they were soled (mun'al), but he later reverted to the opinion of his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, that it is permissible if the socks are thick enough to walk in. The fatwa is now on this latter view. The author explains that the hadith cannot be interpreted restrictively without cause, and the practice of the Companions supports permissibility. He then discusses the conditions: thin socks are not allowed by consensus, but thick socks that can be walked in are subject to dispute. He provides a detailed classification of sock types (mar'azi, yarn, hair, leather, cotton fabric) and outlines the conditions for each: even thick socks are not allowed unless they are lined, soled, or quilted. The passage concludes with additional considerations for jaroq (a type of sock) and the opinion that if less than three fingers of the foot are exposed, wiping is allowed. The overall ruling is that wiping over thick, lined/ soled socks is permissible and is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
جورب (jorab): A sock worn on the foot, which may be made of various materials like wool, cotton, or leather.
نعل (na'l): A sole attached to the sock, making it like a shoe.
مرعزي (mar'azi): A type of fine wool from under the goat's hair, used for making socks.
ثخين (thakhin): Thick; a condition for the sock to be permissible for wiping.
مجلد (mujallad): Lined; a sock that has an inner lining, often of leather or thick material.
مبطن (mubattan): Quilted; a sock that is padded or has an extra layer.
منعل (mun'al): Soled; a sock with a separate sole attached.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi fatwa, which of the following socks is valid for wiping in wudu?
A) A thin cotton sock with a leather sole.
B) A thick wool sock without any lining or sole.
C) A thick felt sock that is lined with leather.
D) A sock made of silk (ibrism) that is thick and lined.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over socks in wudu is permissible in the Hanafi school only if the socks are thick and lined, soled, or quilted; the fatwa follows the later view of Abu Hanifa adopting the Sahibayn's position.
