هذه لا يصلح فيها شيء من كلام الناس فلا يكون الحكم بالفساد من باب العلم فيجوز ثبوته بظني. كذا في التوشيح. وقد يقال : إن الحكم بالفساد بسبب الكلام ليس ثابتاً بالحديث لأنه إنما أفاد كونه محظوراً فيها والاتفاق على أنه حظر يرتفع إلى الافساد فهو إنما ثبت بالاتفاق لا بالحديث ولا يخفى أنه على القول بوجوبه لا الفساد بتركه إذا لم يمسح وصلى
منلا خسرو.
وإلا لا يترك والله تعالى أعلم. وفي شروح الوقاية : المسح على الجبيرة إن ضر جاز تركه، وإن لم يضر فقد اختلف الروايات عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله في جواز تركه والمأخوذ أنه لا يجوز تركه اهـ. وبه جزم اهـ كلام المنح. وتابعه الشيخ علاء الدين الحصكفي وأقول : أما ما نسبه إلى المجمع من أن الوجوب بمعنى الافتراض فليس الموجود فيه كذلك، بل ظاهر كلامه خلافه كما علمت. وأما عبارة الخلاصة فقد علمت تأويلها، وأما ما استشهد به من كلام شروح الوقاية ومنلاخسرو من عدم جواز الترك فلا يلزم منه الفرضية لأن المراد لا يحل تركه والواجب كذلك لما مر، وليس المراد بعدم الجواز عدم الصحة الإسنادهم إياه إلى الترك، ولا يقال لا يصح تركه فتعين أن المراد به عدم الحل ولذا عطف في المحيط قوله ولا تجوز الصلاة بدونه على قوله لم يجز تركه بناء على قولهما بالفرضية. ثم قال : وقيل عنده يجوز تركه أي يحل بناء على قوله بالاستحباب أو الجواز ولذا قال بعده والصحيح أنه عنده واجب أي فلا يجوز تركه فقول شراح الوقاية لا يجوز تركه» هو ما عبر به في المحيط بقوله (والصحيح أنه واجب فظهر أن مرادهم تصحيح الوجوب لا الفرضية. ويتفرع عليه أنه لو ترك المسح فصلاته صحيحة اتفاقاً على الصحيح وهو الذي اعتمده المؤلف في الفروق من كتاب الأشباه والنظائر هذا ما ظهر لفهمي القاصر في هذا المقام ولا تقتصر عليه بل ارجع أيضاً إلى رأيك منصفاً، وابحث مع ذوي الأفهام والله تعالى أعلم. قوله : (وقد جنح المحقق الخ) قال في النهر : وما في فتح القدير من اختيار القول بالوجوب الخ ففيه نظر، إذ الفرائض العملية تثبت بالظن والاشتهار في الرجوع بعد ثبوت أصله غير لازم .اهـ. وفيه أن الفرض العملي يثبت بالظن القوي لا مطلقاً لما قال المؤلف في الكلام على فرائض الوضوء إن المفروض على نوعين قطعي وظني هو في قوة القطعي في العمل بحيث يفوت الجواز بفوته، وعند الإطلاق ينصرف إلى الأول لكماله، والفرق بين
،
(۱) رواه النسائي في كتاب السهو باب ۲۰ أحمد في مسنده (٤٤٧/٥، ٤٤٨).
Book of Purity - Chapter on Wiping over Khuffs. And this is more correct and upon it is the fatwa because wiping over a splint is like washing what is under it, and the function of this limb is washing when possible, and wiping over the splint when unable, like tayammum. Just as it is not said that wudu is not obligatory when water is present, so tayammum is not obligatory, similarly it is not said that washing what is under it is waived, so wiping is waived; rather it is obligatory by its evidence just as tayammum became obligatory by its evidence. End. So its summary: there has been disagreement in authentication (tashih) regarding its being fard or wajib... The summary is that the obligation affirmed by the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in the first and second statements is in its real sense, not the third; as for what is negated from him (Abu Hanifa), in the first statement it is in its real sense, not the last two. Then what is meant in the first is merely istihbab, in the third merely wujub, and in the second either one of these or wujub... And in Fath al-Qadir: it was said wajib according to them, mustahab according to him, and it was said wajib according to him, fard according to them... So the conclusion: he (Abu Hanifa) has no statement of fardiyyah, since no one explicitly attributed it to him; rather they explicitly negated it as a statement from him, let alone verifying it. And by this, what is in the author's statement and his brother's statement in al-Nahr becomes clear, where he agreed with him and even added to it and proceeded upon fardiyyah... And I say: one must rely on what occurred in al-Majma and its commentary that wujub is in the meaning of iftirad (making fard) is agreed upon... And no one has authenticated istihbab as a statement. And the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir inclined to strengthen the statement of wujub... And in the commentaries of al-Wiqayah: wiping over a splint: if there is harm, it is permissible to leave it, and if no harm, the narrations from Abu Hanifa differ on permissibility of leaving it, and the taken position is that it is not permissible to leave it. End. And this is what appeared to my limited understanding in this context...
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of wiping over a splint (jabirah) during wudu. The core issue is whether this wiping is fard (obligatory with certainty), wajib (obligatory but with less certainty), or mustahab (recommended). The author analyzes various rulings attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The passage opens by stating that the correct view, upon which fatwa is given, is that wiping over a splint is wajib and not permissible to omit. It compares wiping over a splint to tayammum: just as tayammum becomes obligatory when water is absent, wiping over a splint becomes obligatory when washing the limb is not possible. The author then cites al-Zayla'i, who states that according to the two disciples, wiping over a splint is wajib and cannot be left, based on the hadith of 'Ali, while according to Abu Hanifa, it is not wajib, so it can be left without excuse. Another source (al-Ghayah) says the correct view is that it is wajib according to Abu Hanifa, but not fard, so his prayer is valid without it. The passage then presents several different characterizations: some say it is mustahab according to Abu Hanifa and wajib according to the two; others say it is wajib according to Abu Hanifa and fard according to the two; still others say it is merely permissible. The author attempts to reconcile these by interpreting the term 'wajib' in different contexts. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is wajib, but not fard, meaning that if one omits it, the prayer is still valid but sinful. The author criticizes those who claimed it is fard, stating that Abu Hanifa never held this view. The passage also discusses the criteria for establishing rulings: fard in practice can be established by strong conjecture (zann), not necessarily certainty. The final conclusion is that the correct view is wujub, not fardiyyah, and that the commentaries of al-Wiqayah confirm that it is not permissible to leave it when there is no harm, but this does not mean it is fard. Therefore, if one leaves the wiping, his prayer is valid by agreement.

Key Terms
المسح على الجبيرة (al-masḥu ʿalā al-jabīrah): Wiping with wet hands over a medical splint or bandage that covers a wound or fracture, performed instead of washing the affected limb during wudu or ghusl.
الوجوب (al-wujūb): Legal obligation; an act that is demanded by the Lawgiver in a non-absolutely binding way, such that omitting it is sinful but does not invalidate the act of worship.
الفرضية (al-farḍiyyah): The quality of being fard, i.e., an absolutely obligatory act that must be performed and omission renders the worship invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of wiping over a splint (jabirah) during wudu?
A) Fard; omitting it invalidates wudu.
B) Wajib; omitting it is sinful but wudu and prayer are valid.
C) Mustahab; omitting it is not sinful and prayer is valid.
D) Mubah; it is optional with no reward or sin.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over a splint is wajib, not fard; omitting it is sinful but does not invalidate prayer, in accordance with the mufta bihi of the Hanafi school.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Wiping Over a Splint: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the differing views on the obligation of wiping over a splint within the Hanafi school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three intra-Hanafi positions on wiping over a splint (wajib, fard, mustahabb), explain why the relied-upon position is wajib, and apply the rule that omitting a wajib does not invalidate prayer but requires repetition.

Core Idea
Wiping over a splint is wajib; omitting it does not break the prayer, but you must repeat it.

Within the Hanafi school, the ruling on wiping over a splint (jabirah) is a classic dispute that illustrates the crucial distinction between fard and wajib. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines the differing narrations from Abu Hanifa and his students, and clarifies the relied-upon position. By the end, you will understand why the correct view is that it is wajib and what that means in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State the views of Abu Hanifa (wajib), the Sahibayn (fard), and some narrations (mustahabb).
These are all within the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the usul distinction
Recall that in Hanafi usul, fard is based on qat'i proof, wajib on zanni proof. This distinction is key.
The passage discusses whether zanni proof can establish fard.
3
Analyze the evidence
The hadith on wiping over a splint is zanni, so it cannot establish fard. Hence the obligation is wajib.
The argument about speech in prayer is used to show that corruption can be based on zanni proof indirectly.
4
Apply the rule: consequence of omission
Omitting a wajib does not invalidate the prayer, but requires repetition if intentional. This is the practical outcome.
The author concludes that prayer is valid but must be repeated.
5
Note the conditional cases
Abu Bakr al-Razi distinguished: if the wound could be washed if exposed, wiping is wajib; if not, it is not wajib. Also conditions from Qadi Khan on sequence.
These are additional rulings derived from the same dispute.

Book of Purification - Chapter on Wiping Over Khuffain. ... Its obligation, and I have not seen anyone correct its recommendation according to a saying. The Muhaddith in Fath al-Qadir leaned toward strengthening the saying of its obligation, saying in meaning: The utmost that the transmitted reports on wiping over the splint indicate is obligation, so the absence of corruption by leaving it is more consistent with the principles. He ruled on the saying of al-Khulasah al-Madi that it is well-known from Abu Hanifa that the opposite of it is well-known from him, and perhaps that is the meaning of what was said: there are two narrations from him. End. This is based on what was mentioned in al-Muhit that ruling with corruption goes back to knowledge, so it is not established by a zanni proof. There is discussion in it, for speech in prayer corrupts it while leaving speech therein is established by khabar wahid, and it is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Indeed this prayer of ours is not fit for any speech of people,' so the ruling of corruption is not from the category of knowledge, so it is permissible for it to be established by a zanni proof. Thus in al-Tawshih. It may be said: The ruling of corruption due to speech is not established by the hadith because it only indicates it being prohibited therein, and the consensus that a prohibition rises to corruption, so it is established by consensus, not by the hadith. It is not hidden that according to the saying of its obligation, there is no corruption by leaving it if he did not wipe and prayed (Mulla Khusraw). Otherwise, he does not leave it, and Allah knows best. In the commentaries of al-Wiqayah: Wiping over the splint: if it is harmful, it is permissible to leave it; if not harmful, then the narrations from Abu Hanifa vary regarding the permissibility of leaving it, and the taken position is that it is not permissible to leave it. End. He affirmed it. End of the speech of al-Mannah. Shaykh Ala' al-Din al-Haskafi followed him. I say: As for what he attributed to al-Majma' that obligation means imperativeness (fardiyyah), the text is not like that, rather the apparent meaning of his speech is contrary to it as you know. As for the phrase of al-Khulasah, you know its interpretation. As for what he cited from the speech of the commentaries of al-Wiqayah and Mulla Khusraw of the impermissibility of leaving it, imperativity does not necessarily follow, because what is meant is that it is not permissible to leave it, and wajib is like that as mentioned before. What is meant by impermissibility is not the lack of validity, because they attribute it to leaving. It is not said that its leaving is not valid, so it is determined that what is meant is the lack of permissibility. Therefore, in al-Muhit, he appended his saying 'and it is not permissible to pray without it' after his saying 'it is not permissible to leave it' based on their saying of imperativity. Then he said: It is said that according to him it is permissible to leave it, meaning permissible, based on his saying of recommendation or permissibility. Therefore, he said after that: And the correct view according to him is that it is obligatory, so it is not permissible to leave it. So the saying of the commentators of al-Wiqayah 'it is not permissible to leave it' is what is expressed in al-Muhit as 'and the correct view is that it is wajib.' So it appears that what they mean is to affirm obligation (wujub) not imperativity (fardiyyah). It branches from this that if he left wiping, his prayer is sound by agreement upon the correct view, and this is what the author relied upon in al-Furuq from the book al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir. This is what appeared to my humble understanding in this situation, and do not confine yourself to it, rather also refer to your opinion fairly, and research with intelligent people, and Allah knows best. His saying: 'And the Muhaddith leaned...' He said in al-Nahr: What is in Fath al-Qadir of choosing the saying of obligation has some consideration, indeed practical mandatory acts (fara'id) are established by zann, and fame in returning after the establishment of its origin is not necessary. End. In it is that practical fard is established by strong zann, not absolutely, as the author said in the discussion on the obligatory acts of wudu: The mandatory act (mafrud) is of two types: definite (qat'i) and presumptive (zanni). The presumptive is like the definite in practice so that the validity is lost by its omission, and when used absolutely it is applied to the first due to its perfection, and the difference between the two is as he said: For indeed he must repeat that prayer because it is known that every prayer performed with the omission of a wajib requires its repetition. This and Abu Bakr al-Razi mentioned a distinction according to Abu Hanifa. He said: If what is under the splint, if exposed, could be washed, then wiping is obligatory by the original ruling because it relates to what stands in its place like wiping over the khuff. And if what is under it, if exposed, cannot be washed, then wiping over it is not obligatory because the original obligation has fallen, so what stands in its place is not required, like the amputated foot if he wears a khuff. Al-Sayrafi said: This is the best of sayings, and it is supported by what the author mentioned in al-Mustafa that the difference is regarding the wounded, while the one with a fracture is obliged to wipe by agreement. Similarly in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. So what is in al-Mustafa is based on the distinction of al-Razi, not as imagined in Fath al-Qadir that it is based on the hadith of wiping from 'Ali regarding the fracture. End. All of this includes when the wound is on the head, and it is stated in al-Bada'i: If the wounds are on his head and some of it is healthy, then if the healthy part is of the amount that allows wiping, which is the amount of three fingers, he is not permitted except to wipe on it because the obligatory part of wiping the head is this amount, and this amount of the head is healthy, so there is no need to wipe over the splints. If it is less than that, he does not wipe, because its existence and non-existence are alike, and he wipes over the splints. End. In al-Mustabqa (with the letter ghain): If he is wounded all over, wiping over them is not obligatory because wiping is a substitute for washing, and the object of substitution has no substitute. It is said: It is obligatory. End. The correct view is obligation. His saying 'wiping is a substitute for washing' is not correct, because wiping on the head is an original act in itself, not a substitute, as is obvious. In Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by Qadi Khan: Wiping over splints has conditions: If washing what is under it does not harm him, he is obligated to wash. If washing with cold water harms him and washing with hot water does not harm him, he is obligated to wash with hot water. If washing harms him and wiping under the splint does not harm him, then he wipes under it and does not wipe over it. End. They said: This should be memorized, for people are heedless of it. But it is said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he can only wash the wound with hot water? (Commentary continues on the distinction between strong zanni establishing fard and zanni establishing wajib as terminological difference in this context). End, let it be considered. His saying: 'And Abu Bakr al-Razi mentioned...' He said in al-Sharnabaliyyah: His saying 'if exposed could be washed' etc. must be interpreted as when he cannot remove the splint, as he will mention from Qadi Khan, otherwise the wiping on them is not valid. His saying: 'not as imagined in Fath al-Qadir...' He said in al-Nahr: It is not hidden that the distinction is also based on the athar of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) based on that the one with a fracture is not harmed by washing, so what is in Fath al-Qadir is appropriate. His saying: 'And the correct view is obligation' implies that its opposite is wrong, and you have known the difference of opinion between the Imam and his two companions, so it would have been appropriate to express it as 'and the correct view is obligation.' And in his saying 'wiping is a substitute for washing' there is an apparent consideration, because what al-Mustabqa means is wiping over the splint, i.e., that wiping over it is a substitute for washing, and wiping has no substitute because what is obligatory on the head is only wiping. So if there is a splint on the head, it necessarily follows that wiping over it is a substitute for washing.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an intra-Hanafi dispute discussing whether wiping over a splint (jabirah) is obligatory (wajib) or mandatory (fard), and whether omitting it invalidates the prayer. The author begins by noting the differing views: some schollars consider it mustahabb (recommended), but the author states he has not seen anyone correct that view. Al-Marghinani in Fath al-Qadir leans towards obligation (wujub). The passage then enters a technical discussion: when an obligation is established by a zanni (probable) proof, does its omission render the worship invalid? Al-Muhit argued that corruption (fasād) of prayer is a ruling requiring certain knowledge, so it cannot be based on a zanni proof. However, the author objects that the prohibition of speech in prayer is established by a single narration (khabar wahid), yet speech corrupts the prayer by consensus. Therefore, corruption can be based on zanni proof indirectly. The conclusion is that even if wiping is wajib, leaving it does not corrupt the prayer; the prayer remains valid but the person must repeat it if he left a wajib act intentionally. The passage then contrasts the views of Abu Hanifa and his two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad considered wiping over the splint as farḍ (obligatory), while the relied-upon narration from Abu Hanifa is that it is wajib. The author clarifies that the phrase 'impermissible to leave' means not permissible (i.e., it is wajib), not that the prayer is invalid. Then a famous distinction by Abu Bakr al-Razi is presented: if the wound could be washed if exposed, then wiping is obligatory by analogy to wiping over khuff; if the wound could not be washed (e.g., open fracture), then wiping is not obligatory because the original obligation of washing has fallen. This distinction is preferred by al-Sayrafi and supported by al-Mustafa. Further details: if the healthy part of the head is equal to or larger than three fingers (the obligatory area), then one must wipe on the healthy part, and wiping over splints is not needed. If the healthy part is less, one wipes over the splints. The passage ends with a ruling from Qadi Khan on sequential options: first, wash without harm; second, wash with hot water; third, wipe under the splint. The final comment emphasizes that wiping on the head is an original act, not a substitute, contrary to the claim in al-Mustabqa. Throughout, the author argues that the correct view is obligation (wajib), which does not cause invalidity if omitted, but requires repetition.

Key Terms
المسح على الجبيرة (al-mash 'ala al-jabirah): Wiping with wet hand over a splint or bandage placed on a wound or fracture, as a substitute for washing or wiping the affected part during wudu or ghusl.
الفرض (al-fard): A mandatory act established by a definitive proof (qat'i al-thubut), e.g., Quran or mutawatir Sunnah. Its omission invalidates the worship.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation, but in Hanafi usul, it is a category between fard and sunnah, established by probable (zanni) evidence. Omitting a wajib intentionally requires repetition but does not invalidate the act if done unwittingly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the consequence of praying without wiping over a splint (jabirah) when it was wajib?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but must be repeated.
C) The prayer is valid and no repetition is needed.
D) The prayer is invalid and no repetition is possible.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that wiping over a splint is wajib, and omitting it requires repetition but does not invalidate the prayer.

Conditions for Wiping Over a Bandage – Detail of Abu Bakr al-Razi
Explores the obligation of wiping over a bandage based on a talil analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the obligation of wiping over a bandage according to the Hanafi school and apply the talil to determine the ruling in specific cases.

Core Idea
Wiping over a bandage is obligatory only if the wound could be washed without harm; otherwise the obligation falls.

This lesson unpacks Abu Bakr al-Razi's precise distinction on wiping over a bandage. Understanding his talil is key to applying the ruling correctly in cases of injury. We will see how the ability to wash the wound determines whether wiping is wajib or not, and how this applies even to head injuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage divides cases: (1) the wound under the bandage could be washed if uncovered, (2) it cannot be washed. Identify these as the basis for the ruling.
The condition is about possibility of washing, not actual washing.
2
Apply the talil
For scenario 1: wiping is wajib because it stands in place of the original washing that is possible. For scenario 2: not wajib because the original obligation falls, so its substitute falls too.
This is the core logical reasoning (talil) linking obligation to possibility.
3
Examine the analogies
Al-Razi compares scenario 1 to wiping over khuff (wajib) and scenario 2 to a cut-foot wearing khuff (not wajib). Understand how these analogies support the talil.
The cut-foot analogy: washing the foot is impossible, so wiping over khuff is not required.
4
Apply to the head
When the wound is on the head: if the healthy part is ≥3 fingers, wipe the healthy part and not the bandage; if less, wipe the bandage. This follows the same talil.
The healthy part's size determines if the original obligation remains.
5
Rebutt the badal argument
Some claim wiping is a substitute (badal) and thus not obligatory. The commentator rejects this, stating that wiping on the head is an original act (asl), not a substitute.
This clarifies that the ruling is based on the nature of the act, not a chain of substitutes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا وقد ذكر الشيخ أبو بكر الرازي تفصيلاً على قول أبي حنيفة فقال : إن كان ما تحت الجبيرة لو ظهر أمكن غسله فالمسح واجب بالأصل ليتعلق بما قام مقامه كمسح الخف، وإن كان ما تحتها لو ظهر لا يمكن غسله فالمسح عليها غير واجب لأن فرض الأصل قد سقط فلا يلزم ما قام مقامه كالمقطوع القدم إذا لبس الخف. قال الصيرفي : وهذا أحسن الأقوال ويؤيده ما ذكره المصنف في المصفى أن الخلاف في المجروح، أما المكسور فيجب عليه المسح بالاتفاق. كذا في السراج الوهاج. فبنى ما في المصفى على تفصيل الرازي لا كما توهمه في فتح القدير من أنه مبني على أن خبر المسح عن علي في المكسور .اهـ. وهذا كله بإطلاقه شامل لما إذا كانت الجراحة بالرأس وقد صرح به في البدائع فقال : ولو كانت الجراح على رأسه وبعضه صحيح فإن كان الصحيح قدر ما يجوز عليه المسح وهو قدر ثلاث أصابع لا يجوز إلا يمسح عليه لأن المفروض من مسح الرأس هذا القدر، وهذا القدر من الرأس صحيح فلا حاجة إلى المسح على الجبائر، وإن كان أقل من ذلك لم يمسح لأن وجوده وعدمه بمنزلة ويمسح على الجبائر .اهـ. وفي المبتغى بالغين المعجمة يجب : كان ومن جميع مجروحاً لا يجب المسح عليها لأن المسح بدل عن الغسل ولا بدل له وقيل يجب ا هـ . والصواب هو الوجوب . وقوله المسح بدل عن الغسل غير صحيح لأن المسح على الرأس أصل بنفسه لا بدل كما لا يخفى.
And indeed Sheikh Abu Bakr al-Razi mentioned a detail on the statement of Abu Hanifa and said: If what is under the bandage, if it appeared, it would be possible to wash it, then wiping is obligatory based on the original (act) because what has taken its place is attached to it, like wiping over the khuff. And if what is under it, if it appeared, it is not possible to wash it, then wiping upon it is not obligatory because the original obligation has fallen, so what has taken its place is not required, like the cut-off foot when he wears the khuff. Al-Sayrafi said: This is the best of the statements, and it is supported by what the author mentioned in Al-Musaffa that the disagreement is concerning the wounded person, but the broken one, it is obligatory upon him to wipe by agreement. Similarly in Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. So he based what is in Al-Musaffa on the detail of al-Razi, not as imagined in Fath al-Qadir that it is based on the report of wiping from Ali concerning the broken one. End. And this all in its generality includes when the wound is on the head, and it is explicitly stated in Al-Bada'i: And if the wounds are on his head and part of it is healthy, then if the healthy part is an amount that permits wiping, which is the amount of three fingers, it is not permissible except to wipe upon it because the obligatory part of wiping the head is this amount, and this amount of the head is healthy, so there is no need to wipe over the bandages. And if it is less than that, he does not wipe because its existence and non-existence are equivalent, and he wipes over the bandages. End. And in Al-Mubtagha (with the dotted ghain): It is obligatory? Or: it is not obligatory to wipe upon them because wiping is a substitute for washing and it has no substitute; and it was said: it is obligatory. End. And the correct is obligation. And his saying: wiping is a substitute for washing is incorrect because wiping on the head is an original in itself, not a substitute, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed ruling on wiping over a bandage (جبيرة) from Sheikh Abu Bakr al-Razi, analyzing the obligation based on a talil (effective cause). The passage type is a ruling with proof, expanded by the commentator. Al-Razi distinguishes: if the wound could be washed if unveiled, then wiping over the bandage is wajib because it stands in place of the original washing (like khuff). But if the wound cannot be washed (e.g., broken bone that cannot get wet), then wiping is not wajib because the original obligation (washing that part) has fallen. This is supported by al-Sayrafi and the author of Al-Musaffa, who note that disagreement applies only to the wounded, not the broken. The commentator then applies this to the head: if the healthy part of the head is at least the size of three fingers (the minimal wipe area), one must wipe the healthy part and need not wipe the bandage; if less, the healthy part is negligible, and one wipes the bandage. Finally, the passage rebuts the view in Al-Mubtagha that wiping on a completely wounded person is not obligatory because it is a substitute (badal) with no substitute. The commentator insists it is obligatory because wiping on the head is an original act (أصل), not a substitute. All examples follow the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
الجبيرة (al-jabirah): The bandage or splint applied to a wound or broken bone for treatment.
بدل (badal): A substitute that takes the place of the original obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Bakr al-Razi's detail, when is wiping over a bandage wajib?
A) Whenever there is a wound or fracture.
B) Only if the wound would be washable if the bandage were removed.
C) Only if the bandage covers the entire head.
D) It is never wajib.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of wiping over a bandage hinges on whether the underlying wound could be washed if the bandage were removed.

Distinctive Rules of Wiping Over Bandage and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains three unique rules of wiping over bandage and an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three distinctive rules of wiping over a bandage, apply the three harm-based scenarios, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Wiping over a bandage has three unique rules and an intra-Hanafi dispute over its obligation.

In this passage, the author outlines three scenarios for dealing with a wound or bandage based on the level of harm from washing, then highlights three features that distinguish wiping over a bandage from wiping over khuff. Finally, an intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: Abu Hanifa permits leaving the wiping if no harm, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, deem it obligatory. Let us work through the text to understand these practical distinctions and the scholarly difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three harm-based scenarios
Read the first part of the passage from Qadikhan. It presents three situations: (1) washing the wound causes no harm → washing is obligatory; (2) cold water harms but hot water does not → wash with hot water; (3) washing harms but wiping under the bandage does not → wash under and do not wipe over. Note the progression of harm.
The passage emphasizes memorizing these scenarios as people are often heedless.
2
Extract the three distinctive features of wiping over bandage
The author then lists three rules that differ from wiping over khuff: (i) no fixed time limit – it lasts until recovery; (ii) it can be combined with washing (e.g. wipe bandage on one limb while washing another); (iii) it is valid even if the bandage was tied without wudu. Identify each and understand the reasoning given.
The phrase 'يجوز وإن شدها بلا وضوء' is key for the third feature.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on obligation
The commentator notes that the author used 'يجوز' (it is valid) rather than 'يجب' (it is obligatory), which hints that wiping is not fard. Then al-Munyah is quoted: Abu Hanifa says it is permissible to leave wiping if it does not harm (no sin), while the two companions (Sahibayn) say it is obligatory. Identify the evidence for each side.
Abu Hanifa's view: necessity is lifted if no harm, so original washing returns. Sahibayn: bandage remains a constraint, so wiping is wajib.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamar al-khilaf)
The dispute affects whether leaving the wiping without harm incurs sin. According to Sahibayn, it is sinful; according to Abu Hanifa, it is not. The passage does not explicitly choose, but the structure favors the majority (Sahibayn).
The commentator in al-Nahr criticizes interpreting 'يجوز' as permissibility without harm, as no one preferred that view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي شرح الجامع الصغير لقاضيخان: والمسح على الجبائر على وجوه إن كان لا يضره غسل ما تحته يلزمه الغسل، وإن كان يضره الغسل بالماء البارد ولا يضره الغسل بالماء الحار يلزمه الغسل بالماء الحار، وإن كان يضره الغسل ولا يضره المسح ما تحت الجبيرة ولا يمسح فوقها .اهـ. قالوا ينبغي أن يحفظ هذا فإن الناس عنه غافلون. ولكن قال في السراج الوهاج ولو كان لا يمكنه غسل الجراحة إلا بالماء الحار الظني القوي المثبت للفرض وبين الظني المثبت للواجب اصطلاحاً خصوص المقام اهـ فليتأمل. قوله : (فلا يتوقت) أي لا يتوقت المسح على الجبيرة بوقت معين لأن كالغسل لما تحتها، وإنما قيدنا بالوقت المعين لأنه موقت بالبرء كما سيجيء، وهذه من المسائل التي يخالف فيها مسح الجبيرة مسح الخف قوله (ويجمع مع الغسل) أي يجمع المسح على الجبيرة مع الغسل وقد الثانية من المسائل قوله ( ويجوز وإن شدها بلا وضوء) لأن في اعتبارها في تلك الحالة حرجاً ولأن غسل ما تحتها بسقط وانتقل إلى الجبيرة بخلاف الخف، وهذه هي الثالثة. وفي تعبيره بـ«يجوز» دون «يجب إشارة إلى أن المسح على الجبيرة ليس بفرض قوله (ويمسح على كل العصابة كان تحتها جراحة أو لا وفيه مسألتان : الأولى أن استيعاب مسح قدمناه وهذه هي مع أنه المسح على الرأس والمسح لا بدل له قوله: (وفي تعبيره بيجوز دون يجب إشارة الخ) قال في النهر : فيه نظر إذ لا داعي إلى حمل الجواز على ما ذكره وتخريجه على قول لم يرجحه أحد فيما علمت . منافٍ لقوله كالغسل» على ما مر .اهـ. وفيه نظر فقد قال في المنية : وإن ترك المسح على الجبيرة والمسح لا يضره جاز له عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لهما، فإن كان مراد المنية بالجواز الحل وعدم الإثم فلا
And in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by Qadikhan: Wiping over bandages is on aspects: if washing what is under it does not harm him, he is obligated to wash; if washing with cold water harms him but washing with hot water does not harm him, he is obligated to wash with hot water; if washing harms him and wiping (under the bandage) does not harm him, he washes what is under the bandage and does not wipe over it. End. They said: It is fitting to memorize this, for the people are heedless of it. But he said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: And if he cannot wash the wound except with hot water (that is zanni qawi [strongly probable] which establishes a fard, and there is a distinction between the zanni that establishes wajib in terminology particularly in this context, so let it be considered. His statement: (So it is not time-limited) meaning the wiping over the bandage is not time-limited because it is like washing for what is under it; we only limited it to a specific time because it is time-limited by recovery, as will come, and this is one of the matters in which wiping over a bandage differs from wiping over khuff. His statement: (And it is combined with washing) meaning wiping over the bandage is combined with washing, and this is the second of the matters. His statement: (And it is valid even if he tied it without wudu) because considering it in that state is hardship, and because the washing of what is under it has fallen and transferred to the bandage, contrary to khuff, and this is the third. His statement: (And he wipes over the entire bandage, whether there is a wound under it or not) and in it are two matters: the first is that the comprehensive wiping we have mentioned and this is with it that it is wiping upon the head and wiping has no substitute. His statement: (And in his expression 'it is valid' instead of 'it is obligatory' is an indication...) He said in al-Nahr: There is consideration, for there is no reason to interpret 'valid' as he mentioned and to base it on a statement that no one has preferred, as far as I know. It contradicts his statement 'like washing' as previously. End. And there is consideration, for he said in al-Munyah: And if he leaves wiping over the bandage while it does not harm him, it is permissible for him according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). If what is meant by 'permissible' in al-Munyah is the legal permissibility and lack of sin, then...
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage, from Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by Qadikhan, details the ruling on wiping over bandages based on levels of harm. It first presents three scenarios: 1) if washing the wound causes no harm, washing is obligatory (not wiping); 2) if cold water harms but hot does not, hot water washing is obligatory; 3) if both washing and wiping harm, but wiping under the bandage (i.e., washing the wound without removing bandage?) is less harmful, then one washes the wound and does not wipe on top. The commentator emphasizes memorizing this. Then three unique features of wiping over a bandage (as opposed to khuff) are listed: 1) No fixed time (فلا يتوقت) — valid until recovery; 2) Can be combined with washing (يجمع مع الغسل) — e.g., one wipes bandage on one limb while washing another; 3) Valid even if bandage was tied without wudu (يجوز وإن شدها بلا وضوء). There is a debate over whether the expression 'يجوز' (it is valid) indicates it is not fard; some argue it contradicts the idea that it is like washing. The passage ends with an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa allows leaving the wiping if it doesn't harm (i.e., no sin), while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding it obligatory. The commentator notes this is the relied-upon position. The discussion underscores that the ruling is not a pure substitute (badal) but has its own independent nature.

Key Terms
الخُف (al-khuff): Leather sock worn on the foot, over which one may wipe in wudu.
الوضوء (al-wudu): Ablution required for prayer, involving washing specific parts and wiping head and feet.
الجبيرة (al-jabira): Bandage or splint applied to a wound or fracture, over which wiping is allowed when washing is harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It has no fixed time limit; it lasts until recovery.
B) It can be combined with washing of other limbs.
C) It is only valid if the bandage was tied in a state of wudu.
D) It may be valid even if the bandage was tied without wudu.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over a bandage has three unique rules (no time limit, combined with washing, valid without prior wudu) and involves an intra-Hanafi dispute on its obligation versus permissibility.

Is Mash on Jabirah a Substitute or Original Ruling?
Intra-Hanafi debate on the legal nature of wiping over a splint.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on mash over jabirah from mash over khuff and explain the legal reasoning behind treating it as an original ruling.

Core Idea
Mash on jabirah is legally treated as washing, not a substitute – thus it can be combined with washing.

When a person has a wound covered by a splint (jabirah), they may wipe over it instead of washing. But does this wiping replace washing entirely, like wiping over khuffs does, or does it have a different legal nature? The answer determines whether one can combine this wipe with actual washing on another limb. This lesson unpacks the internal Hanafi debate on whether mash on jabirah is a pure substitute (badal) or is elevated to the status of an original (asl) due to necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Some Hanafis (e.g., the author of al-Hidayah) consider mash on jabirah a pure substitute (badal) for washing, exactly like mash on khuff. The majority (including the commentator and the author of Fath al-Qadir) hold that it is not a substitute but is given the legal effect of an original (asl hukman) due to necessity.
Both views are within the Hanafi school; the disagreement is about the legal classification.
2
Examine the key evidence: combining with washing
If mash on jabirah were a pure substitute, combining it with washing on another limb would be prohibited (like khuff). But the texts permit combining (e.g., wiping over a splint on one foot and washing the other). This indicates mash on jabirah is not a pure substitute.
Also, if one puts a khuff over a foot that has been wiped (jabirah-treated), upon hadath the khuff must be removed, because the foot is legally washed.
3
Analyze the response to the counter-evidence
Opponents argue that mash on jabirah is invalid when one is able to wash, proving it is a substitute. The majority responds: while it is a substitute in essence (badal fi nafsihi), it is given the status of an original due to inability (darurah), so it is like an original in its legal effect.
This is why it differs from khuff, which remains a pure substitute even during inability.
4
Apply the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The key practical difference: if a substitute, one cannot combine mash on jabirah with washing on another limb; if an original, such combination is valid. The mufta bihi (relied-upon view) allows combination.
Also, no time limit on mash on jabirah, unlike khuff (one day+night for resident, three for traveler).
5
Determine the tarjih and its basis
The majority view is preferred because it aligns with the practical rulings found in later authoritative texts (al-Muhit, Fath al-Qadir). The commentator in al-Bahr al-Raiq explicitly sides with the majority and rebuts the Hidayah's stance.
The tarjih is based on consistency: the detailed furu' (subsidiary rulings) all support the original-status view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الغسل ويجوز وإن شدها بلا وضوء ويمسح على كل العصابة كان تحتها جراحة أو خاصة ولا يمكنه بما سواء لم يجب عليه تكلف الغسل الحار ويجزئه المسح لأجل المشقة اهـ . والظاهر الأول كما لا يخفى ولهذا اقتصر المحقق في فتح القدير عليه ولم ينقل غيره وقيده بأن يكون قادراً عليه وهو ظاهر، وقد قدمنا أن المسح على الجبيرة ليس ببدل بخلاف المسح على الخفين، ولهذا لا يمسح على الخف في أحد الرجلين ويغسل الأخرى لأنه يؤدي إلى الجمع بين الأصل والبدل. ولو كانت الجبيرة على إحدى رجليه ومسح عليها وغسل الأخرى لا يكون ذلك جمعاً بين الأصل والبدل، ولهذا أيضاً لو مسح على خرقة المجروحة وغسل الصحيحة ولبس الخف عليها ثم أحدث فإنه يتوضأ وينزع الخف لأن المجروحة مغسولة حكماً ولا يجتمع الوظيفتان في الرجل وعلى قياس ما روي عن أبي حنيفة «إن ترك المسح على الجبائر وهو لا يضره يجوز ينبغي أن يجوز لأنه لما سقط غسل المجروحة صارت كالذاهبة. هذا إذا لبس الخف على الصحيحة لا غير، فإن لبس على الجريحة أيضاً بعدما مسح على جبيرتها فإنه يمسح عليها لأن المسح عليها كالغسل لما تحتها كذا في الخلاصة. وهذا كله ظاهر في أن هذا المسح ليس ببدل عن الغسل، وظاهر ما في الهداية أنه بدل، وتعقبه بعض الشارحين بأنه ليس ببدل بدليل ما ذكرنا من الفرق بينه وبين مسح الخف فكان أصلاً لا بدلاً. وأجيب بأنه في نفسه بدل بدليل أنه لا يجوز عند القدرة على الغسل لكن نزل منزلة الأصل لعدم القدرة عليه فكان كالأصل بخلاف المسح على الخفين فإنه لم يعط له حكم الغسل بل هو بدل محض، ولهذا لو جمع بينه وبين الغسل أو بين المسح على الجبيرة يلزم الجمع بين الأصل والبدل حقيقة أو حكماً.
Washing, and it is permissible even if he tied it without wudu, and he wipes over the entire bandage whether there is a wound under it or a particular [condition?], and he cannot [manage] it otherwise, he is not required to trouble himself with hot water, and wiping suffices him due to hardship. End. And the apparent [view] is the first, as is not hidden, and for this reason the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir confined himself to it and did not transmit other, and he restricted it to being capable of it, and that is apparent. And we have already mentioned that wiping over the splint is not a substitute, contrary to wiping over the khuffs, and for this reason one does not wipe over the khuff on one foot and wash the other because it leads to combining the original and the substitute. And if the splint was on one of his feet and he wiped over it and washed the other, that is not combining the original and the substitute. And for this reason also, if he wiped over the cloth of the wounded [foot] and washed the healthy [foot] and put a khuff over it, then he had an event [that breaks wudu], he performs wudu and removes the khuff because the wounded [foot] is legally washed and the two functions do not combine in one foot. And by analogy with what is narrated from Abu Hanifa: 'If he leaves wiping over the splints while it does not harm him, it is permissible; it should be permissible because when washing the wounded [area] is waived, it becomes like a missing [limb].' This is if he put the khuff on the healthy foot only. If he also put it on the wounded foot after wiping over its splint, then he wipes over it because wiping over it is like washing for what is under it, as in al-Khulasa. All this is clear that this wiping is not a substitute for washing, but what is apparent in al-Hidaya is that it is a substitute. Some commentators criticized it saying it is not a substitute by the evidence of the difference we mentioned between it and wiping over the khuff, so it is an original, not a substitute. And it was answered that it is in itself a substitute because it is not permissible when able to wash, but it is given the status of the original due to inability, so it is like the original, unlike wiping over the khuffs because it does not have the ruling of washing but is a pure substitute. And for this reason, if he combines between it and washing or between wiping over the splint and washing, it necessitates combining the original and the substitute in reality or legally.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal nature of wiping (mash) on a splint (jabirah). The commentator begins by noting that many scholars, including the author of Fath al-Qadir, hold that mash on jabirah is not a substitute (badal) for washing (ghusl) but rather an original ruling (asl). The key evidence is that if mash were a substitute, one could not combine it with washing on two different limbs (e.g., wiping on a splint on one foot and washing the other). Yet such combination is permitted, unlike with khuffs where one cannot wipe on one khuff and wash the other. Further, if a person wipes over a wound bandage and then puts a khuff on the healthy foot, upon breaking wudu he must remove the khuff because the wounded foot is legally considered washed. This shows mash on jabirah has the effect of washing. The Hidayah apparently considers it a substitute, but the commentator rejects this, arguing that while it is a substitute in essence (since it is not allowed when able to wash), it is elevated to the status of an original due to necessity. Thus it differs from mash on khuffs, which remains a pure substitute and cannot be combined with washing.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabīrah): A splint or bandage used to cover a wound or fracture; the legal ruling applies to any wound covering that cannot be removed without harm.
بدل (badal): A substitute that takes the place of an original act but does not have the same legal effect; in this context, a pure substitute cannot be combined with the original.
أصل (aṣl): The original legal obligation; here, washing is the original, and mash on jabirah is treated as having the same effect as washing due to necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can a person wipe over a splint on one foot and wash the other foot, whereas wiping on a khuff on one foot and washing the other is prohibited according to Hanafis?
A) Because the khuff is a pure substitute for washing, while the splint is not a substitute at all.
B) Because the splint is considered legally washed after wiping, so combining is not seen as combining original and substitute.
C) Because the khuff is worn on a clean foot, while the splint is on a wounded foot.
D) Because washing the other foot would be a violation of the order of wudu.

Key Takeaway
Mash on jabirah is legally considered as washing due to necessity, allowing combination with actual washing and distinguishing it from mash on khuff.

Three Distinctive Rulings of Wiping on Splint
Commentary on three distinctive rulings of jabirah mash and debate on its legal classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rulings that distinguish wiping on a splint from wiping on khuff and explain the significance of the author's choice of 'yajuz' over 'yajib' in indicating the legal classification.

Core Idea
Wiping on a splint has no time limit, combines with washing, and is valid even without prior wudu—yet its obligation is not at the level of fard.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the commentator identifies three key rulings where mash on jabirah differs from mash on khuff. He then addresses a subtle but crucial point about legal terminology: why the author used 'yajuz' instead of 'yajib'. This lesson unpacks those rulings and the debate over the legal classification of the wiping.

Guided Path
1
List the three distinctive rulings
Identify the three points where mash on jabirah differs from mash on khuff as enumerated in the text: no time limit, combines with washing, permissible without prior wudu.
The text uses 'fala yatawaqqat', 'yajma' ma'a al-ghusl', and 'yajuz wa in shaddaha bi-la wudu'.
2
Analyze the rationale for each ruling
For each, identify the underlying legal cause: for no time limit, because it is like washing (until healing); for combining, because it is like washing; for no prior wudu, because of hardship (haraj) and the transfer of obligation to the splint.
The rationales are grounded in the principle of necessity and analogy to washing.
3
Examine the author's choice of 'yajuz' over 'yajib'
The commentator argues that using 'yajuz' (it is permissible) instead of 'yajib' (it is obligatory) indicates that wiping on a splint is not fard. The passage then debates the meaning: does 'yajuz' imply it is not wajib at all? Note the intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa vs. the two companions.
Al-Nahr objects to this interpretation, but the commentary defends it by citing al-Muniya.
4
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
Based on the tarjih, the relied-upon view is that it is wajib but not fard. The commentator defends the author's wording as reflecting that distinction.
The passage shows a sophisticated engagement with legal terminology to avoid implying a higher obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (فلا يتوقت أي لا يتوقت المسح على الجبيرة بوقت معين لأن كالغسل لما تحتها، وإنما قيدنا بالوقت المعين لأنه موقت بالبرء كما سيجيء، وهذه من المسائل التي يخالف فيها مسح الجبيرة مسح الخف قوله (ويجمع مع الغسل أي يجمع المسح على الجبيرة مع الغسل وقد الثانية من المسائل قوله ( ويجوز وإن شدها بلا وضوء) لأن في اعتبارها في تلك الحالة حرجاً ولأن غسل ما تحتها بسقط وانتقل إلى الجبيرة بخلاف الخف، وهذه هي الثالثة. وفي تعبيره بـ«يجوز» دون «يجب إشارة إلى أن المسح على الجبيرة ليس بفرض. قوله: (وفي تعبيره بيجوز دون يجب إشارة الخ) قال في النهر : فيه نظر إذ لا داعي إلى حمل الجواز على ما ذكره وتخريجه على قول لم يرجحه أحد فيما علمت. منافٍ لقوله كالغسل» على ما مر .اهـ. وفيه نظر فقد قال في المنية : وإن ترك المسح على الجبيرة والمسح لا يضره جاز له عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لهما، فإن كان مراد المنية بالجواز الحل وعدم الإثم فلا يكون واجباً ولا فرضاً فهو قد صححه كما تشعر به عبارته وإن كان مراده به الصحة وتفريغ الذمة في الدنيا الصادق بكونه واجباً فقد صححه غير واحد كما . مر، والظاهر أن . مراد المؤلف هذا حيث جعل الإشارة إلى أنه ليس بفرض أي عبر بالجواز ليفيد أنه ليس بفرض ولو عبر بالوجوب لاحتمل التأويل بأن المراد منه الفرض بناء على قولهما ولا نسلم منافاته لقوله كالغسل» لأنه ليس مثله من كل وجه فإن الغسل فرض قطعاً بخلاف المسح فتشبيهه به لا يلزم منه أن يكون فرضاً كما حمله . هو في شرحه.
His statement: 'It is not time-limited' means that wiping over the splint is not limited to a specific time because it is like washing for what is under it. We only limited by a specific time because it is limited by healing as will come. And these are among the issues in which wiping on the splint differs from wiping on the khuff. His statement: 'And he combines with washing' means he combines wiping on the splint with washing, and this is the second issue. His statement: 'And it is permissible even if he tied it without wudu' because requiring wudu in that state would be hardship, and because washing what is under it is waived and transferred to the splint, unlike the khuff. And this is the third. And in his expression 'it is permissible' instead of 'it is obligatory' indicates that wiping on the splint is not a fard. His statement: 'And in his expression it is permissible without it is obligatory indicating etc.' al-Nahr said: There is consideration in it, for there is no reason to interpret 'permissible' as he mentioned and to derive it from a view that no one has preferred as far as I know. It contradicts his statement 'like washing' as above. End. And there is consideration in it, for it is said in al-Muniya: If he leaves wiping on the splint while the wiping does not harm him, it is permissible for him according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two [companions]. If the meaning of permissibility in al-Muniya is permissibility and no sin, then it is neither wajib nor fard, so he has validated it as his expression suggests. And if he meant by it validity and discharge of responsibility in this world, which is true if it is wajib, then many have validated it as has passed. And the apparent [view] is that the author's intention is this, where he makes the indication that it is not a fard, i.e., he used 'permissible' to convey that it is not a fard; if he used 'obligatory' it could be interpreted as fard based on their statement, and we do not concede that it contradicts his statement 'like washing' because it is not like it in every respect, for washing is definitely fard while wiping is not, so likening it to washing does not necessitate that it be fard, as he carried in his commentary.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage expands on three distinct rulings of wiping on a splint that differ from wiping on khuffs, and then addresses the author's choice of the word 'yajuz' (permissible) instead of 'yajib' (obligatory). First, wiping on a splint is not limited to a specific duration (e.g., 24 hours or 3 days) but lasts until the wound heals. Second, one can combine wiping on the splint with washing the rest of the body; this is allowed because the mash functions like washing for the covered area. Third, it is valid even if the bandage was tied without prior wudu, due to hardship in requiring wudu at the time of tying. The commentator emphasizes that the author's use of 'yajuz' signals that this wiping is not a fard (obligatory in the highest sense). Some critics (like al-Nahr) object that this interpretation is forced, but the commentator defends it by citing al-Muniya: Abu Hanifa allows leaving the mash if it does not cause harm, implying it is not mandatory. The commentator concludes that the author deliberately used 'yajuz' to avoid confusion with fard, even though the ruling bears similarities to washing.

Key Terms
توقيت (tawqīt): Limiting the duration of mash to a specific time period; jabirah mash is not time-limited, unlike khuff mash.
فرض (farḍ): A legal obligation established by decisive evidence; the author avoids calling mash on jabirah fard to prevent confusion with washing (ghusl) which is fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position described in this passage, why can a person perform wudu and wipe over a splint even if the splint was tied without prior wudu?
A) Because wiping on the splint is considered a separate act that does not require prior purification.
B) Because requiring wudu at the time of tying would cause hardship, and the washing of the covered area is waived and transferred to the splint.
C) Because the splint is not a barrier; it is like the skin itself.
D) Because the person can simply repeat the wudu without issue.

Key Takeaway
Wiping on a splint differs from wiping on khuff in three ways and its obligation is wajib, not fard, as indicated by the author's choice of 'yajuz'.

The Harm Condition for Wiping on a Bandage: Only Removal or Both Removal and Washing?
Determining whether full wiping on a bandage requires harm in both removal and washing or just removal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on when full wiping over a bandage is required, and identify the condition of harm according to the preferred interpretation of al-Muhit.

Core Idea
Full wiping on a bandage is allowed only when removal causes harm; the condition of harm after removal is not required.

When a wound is covered with a bandage, wiping over it substitutes for washing the affected area. But how much of the bandage must be wiped? The Hanafi school requires wiping over the entire bandage only if removing it would cause harm. A debate arose among later Hanafis: does the harm extend to also washing the wound, or is harm in removal sufficient? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq resolves the issue by analyzing the wording of al-Muhit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over a bandage (ʿiṣābah) during wudu. The ruling under discussion is whether one must wipe over the entire bandage or only the part covering the wound, and what conditions trigger the full extent.
The base ruling from earlier texts is that if removing the bandage would harm the wound, one may wipe over it; otherwise, one must remove it and wash the skin.
2
Locate the source of dispute
The dispute originates from interpreting a passage in al-Muhit, which states: 'if removal and turning to washing harm, he wipes.' The question is whether 'harm' is required in both actions (removal and washing) or only in removal.
The conjunction 'and' (wa) could imply both are required, but the verb 'yadurr' is singular, not dual.
3
Analyze the linguistic argument
The commentator argues that the singular verb 'yadurr' (it harms) indicates that the subject (removal and turning to washing) is considered a single compound action. If harm were required in each separately, the dual form 'yadurān' would have been used, as in 'if Zayd and Amr beat' (dual). Therefore, harm in the overall action of removal-washing is sufficient, and the harm is primarily in the removal step.
This is a classical usul al-fiqh principle: the singular form when referring to multiple items indicates a unified compound action.
4
State the preferred position
The preferred position (mufta bihi) is that harm only in removal suffices to allow wiping over the entire bandage. This is supported by al-Nahr, al-Nabulsi, and the commentator himself. The practical consequence: if removal causes harm, one wipes over the whole bandage, even if washing the wound itself without the bandage would be harmless.
The four categories mentioned are: (1) harm in both - full wiping allowed; (2) harm in removal only - full wiping allowed; (3) harm in washing only - must remove if possible; (4) no harm in either - must remove and wash.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا يخفى أنه يستفاد من عبارة (المحيط) قال في النهر: أقول: هذا العمري غريب إذ صاحب المحيط كما ترى اعتبر الضرر في الحل والغسل لا في الحل فقط، وغير خاف أن جواز المسح دائر مع الضرر وعدمه مع عدمه وعليه تتخرج الأقسام الأربعة. اهـ. أقول: لا يخفى ما فيه بل الظاهر المتبادر من كلام المحيط أن المراد أن كان الحل والعدول إلى الغسل يضر يمسح، ولو كان مراده أن الضرر في كل من الحل والغسل لقال يضران ولم يجزان يقول يضر بالأفراد كما تقول إن كان زيد وعمرو يضربان. ثم رأيت العلامة إسمعيل النابلسي في شرحه على الدرر قال ما نصه: التحقيق ما في البحر كما يدل عليه أفراده الضمير في يضر ولو اعتبر الضرر فيهما لثني وإطلاقه عن اعتبار وعدمه ظاهر لا خفاء فيه فليتأمل. اهـ. وهذا عين ما قلنا والله تعالى الحمد. وقال بعض الفضلاء: لو اعتبر الضرر في الحل والمسح لكان غريباً كما ذكر وأما قران الغسل معه فلا ينافيه
His statement: 'And it is not hidden that it is derived from the expression of al-Muhit.' He said in al-Nahr: I say: This is strange, for the author of al-Muhit, as you see, considered harm in [both] removal and washing, not only in removal. And it is not hidden that the permissibility of wiping revolves around harm and its absence around its absence. And on this basis the four categories are derived. End. I say: There is no hidden flaw in it; rather, the apparent understanding from the words of al-Muhit is that the meaning is: if removal and turning to washing harm, he wipes. If he had meant harm in each of removal and washing, he would have said 'they harm' and not 'it harms' in the singular, as you say 'if Zayd and Amr beat' (dual). Then I saw al-Allama Ismail al-Nabulsi in his commentary on al-Durar saying verbatim: The verification is what is in al-Bahr, as indicated by the singular pronoun in 'it harms'. If he had considered harm in both, he would have used the dual. And its absolute nature regarding considering and not considering is apparent, no concealment in it, so ponder. End. And this is exactly what we said, and praise be to Allah. And some virtuous ones said: If harm were considered in removal and wiping, it would be strange as mentioned; and as for coupling washing with it, it does not negate it.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage discusses the interpretation of a passage from al-Muhit regarding the condition of harm (dharar) for allowing wiping over the bandage. The key question is whether the harm must be present when removing the bandage (hall) and also when washing (ghusl), or only when removing. The commentator argues that al-Muhit's phrase 'if removal and turning to washing harm' uses the singular verb 'yadurr' (it harms), which indicates the harm is in the removal process, not necessarily in washing separately. If both were required, the verb would be dual. Al-Nabulsi agrees with this interpretation. Thus, the permissibility of wiping over additional bandages beyond the wound area depends on whether removing them would cause harm. If removal is harmful, wiping is allowed over everything; if removal is possible without harm but washing causes harm, the ruling differs. This debate impacts the practical extent of wiping required.

Key Terms
عصابة (ʿiṣābah): Bandage or wrapping that covers a wound; the ruling for wiping on it applies to the entire wrapping in case of harm.
ضرر (ḍarar): Harm that prevents removal of the bandage without aggravating the injury; the condition for extended wiping.
حل (ḥall): Removal of the bandage; the act of taking it off.
غسل (ghusl): Washing the wound area; the alternative to wiping if removal is possible without harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator's preferred interpretation of al-Muhit, when does a person need to wipe over the entire bandage (including areas beyond the wound)?
A) Only if both removal and washing cause harm.
B) Only if removal causes harm, even if washing does not.
C) Only if the bandage covers the entire limb.
D) Only if the wound is severe.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of wiping over the entire bandage is tied solely to the harm in removal, not subsequent washing.

Ruling on a bandage (jabeerah) falling off or the wound healing
Explains the ruling when a bandage falls off after recovery or otherwise, with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a bandage falls off after healing versus before healing, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Core Idea
The validity of wiping over a bandage depends on the presence of the excuse; falling before healing does not invalidate it according to Abu Hanifa.

In the Hanafi school, wiping over a bandage (jabeerah) is permitted when washing would cause harm. But what happens if the bandage falls off? Does the wiping become invalid? The answer depends on whether the wound has healed. This lesson examines the detailed ruling and an important disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
Identify whether the bandage fell after the wound healed (bur') or before. The ruling differs based on this.
2
State the ruling for falling after healing
If after healing, the wiping becomes invalid because the excuse no longer exists. The person must wash the area under the bandage.
3
State the ruling for falling before healing
If before healing, the wiping remains valid according to the majority (Abu Hanifa). The person may continue his prayer if he is in it, but it is recommended to re-wipe.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Zahidi reports that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the wiping becomes invalid even if the fall is not due to recovery. Their reasoning: the bandage is no longer in place.
This ikhtilaf is considered nawadir (rare transmission).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is whether a person who is in prayer must restart: according to the companions, yes; according to Abu Hanifa, no.

Book of Purity. Chapter on Wiping over Khuff. No, and if it falls after recovery, the wiping becomes invalid; otherwise not. And intention is not required in the wiping of the khuff and the head. Wrapping it in the prescribed manner necessitates that it be determined accordingly, as is not hidden. Then it is known from this that the author should have said: 'and wipe over most of the bandage and its like, even if there is no wound under some of it, if removing it would harm him.' And his statement includes the bandage of the person undergoing venesection. In al-Khulasa: Conveying water to the area not covered by the bandage between the bandage is obligatory because it is exposed. End. And some said: No, and wiping suffices him, and this is followed in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil, and in al-Dhakhira and others, and it is the most sound because if he were required to wash that area, perhaps the entire bandage would become wet and the moisture would penetrate to the site of venesection, harming him. In Tatimmat al-Fatawa al-Sughra: If he knows with certainty that the site of venesection has closed, he must wash that area and wiping does not suffice him. End. Regarding leading the prayer by the one who had venesection with others, there are sayings, the third being that he should not lead immediately but may lead after some time. The apparent point in Fatawa Qadikhan is the choice of permissibility absolutely. If his nail breaks and he puts medicine or gum on it, or inserts a piece of gall bladder or ointment, then if removing it would harm him, he wipes over it; if wiping would harm him, he leaves it; if there are cracks on his limbs, he pours water over them if able, otherwise he leaves them and washes around them. So in al-Fath. In al-Mughrib: al-Shiqaq (with damm) is the cracking of skin, from it 'he applied ointment for the cracking of his foot,' and it is specific. al-Qadir and others. As for al-shiqq (singular of al-shuqooq), it is general. His statement: 'And if it falls after recovery, the wiping becomes invalid; otherwise not,' meaning: if the bandage falls off after recovery, the wiping becomes invalid due to the removal of the excuse; if it does not fall off after recovery, the wiping does not become invalid due to the existence of the excuse that permits wiping. al-Bur' is the opposite of illness, and it is health. The complete answer in this issue according to what is in most books is that if the bandage falls off after recovery: if he is outside prayer and in a state of purity, he washes the site of the bandage and it is not obligatory for him to wash the rest of the limbs; if he is in prayer, then if after he has sat for the duration of tashahhud, it is one of the twelve issues to come in their place; if before sitting, he washes its site and restarts the prayer because the ruling of the previous hadath on commencement appears, so it becomes as if he began without washing that site. If it falls off not due to recovery, the wiping is not invalidated, whether in prayer or outside, to the extent that if he is in prayer, he continues it and does not restart; therefore if he repeats it or changes it, he is not required to repeat the wiping over it, but it is better to repeat the wiping. So in al-Khulasa, Fatawa Qadikhan, and al-Walwaliji, because the wiping over the first was like washing. Based on this, what is in al-Dhakhira from Abu Yusuf: a man with a wound that harms him... falling under the statement of al-Fath 'no wiping' so reflect on it. His statement: 'It should be determined accordingly' - he said in al-Fath: Among the harm of removing it is if he is in a place where he cannot tie it himself and does not find someone to tie it. End. He said in al-Nahr: Our teacher, may Allah have mercy on him, did not see this, so he said 'should be' etc. End. Sheikh Ismail al-Nabulsi said: What appears is that the statement of Qadikhan is based on the saying of Imam that what others deem easy is not considered easy, as transmitted by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth in al-Ta'sis, and we have mentioned it from others, and what al-Fath followed is their saying. End. His statement: 'Based on this, what... touching water, so he bandaged it with two bandages and wiped over the upper one, then removed it; he said: he wipes over the remaining bandage like the khuff and the jarmuqayn, and it does not suffice him until he wipes.' End. It is not apparent; rather what is apparent from what we have mentioned is that repetition is recommended, not obligatory. And strange is what al-Zahidi transmitted in al-Qunyah: that if it falls not due to recovery, the wiping is not invalidated according to Abu Hanifa, but is invalidated according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). End. The author did not address the case when the site of the bandage heals but it does not fall. Al-Zahidi said: It is not mentioned in most books of fiqh if the site of the bandages heals but does not fall, and it is mentioned in al-Salah by al-Taqi al-Karabisi that the wiping becomes invalid. End. It should be said: This is if removing it does not harm him; as for if removing it harms him due to strong adhesion or the like, then no, and Allah knows best. Medicine is like the bandage; if water is poured over it and then it falls, it is subject to the same detail.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn from Kanz al-Daqaiq. It begins with a short ruling stating that intention is not required for wiping over khuff and head, then immediately moves to the main topic: the ruling on a bandage (jabeerah) when it falls off. The author explains that if the bandage falls after the wound has healed (bur'), the permission of wiping is removed because the excuse no longer exists. If it falls before healing, the wiping remains valid. He then details the practical implications: if one is outside prayer, he merely washes the area; if in prayer, he must consider whether he had sat for tashahhud or not. There is an important intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Zahidi reports that according to Abu Hanifa, falling not due to recovery does not invalidate the wiping, but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it does. The preferred view in the relied-upon books is that of Abu Hanifa, but the author of al-Fath appears to follow the companions, causing confusion. The commentary also addresses the case when the wound heals but the bandage does not fall: the correct view is that it is like falling after recovery unless removal causes harm. Additionally, there are rulings for medicine on a broken nail and for cracks on limbs. Throughout, the reasoning is based on the principle of harm (darar): if removing or washing would cause harm, wiping is permitted; once harm ceases, the original obligation returns.

Key Terms
الجبيرة (al-jabeerah): A bandage or splint applied to a wound or fracture that may be wiped over during wudu due to necessity.
البرء (al-bur'): Recovery or healing of a wound; the end of the excuse that permits wiping over the bandage.
مختارات النوازل (Mukhtarat al-Nawazil): A later Hanafi fatwa collection attributed to al-Sadr al-Shahid, relied upon for many practical rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person with a bandage (jabeerah) is in prayer and the bandage falls off after the wound has healed, what must he do?
A) He continues his prayer and does nothing.
B) He washes the site of the bandage and continues.
C) If he has already sat for tashahhud, his prayer is valid; if not, he must wash the site and restart.
D) He must restart his prayer from the beginning regardless.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on a bandage falling off depends on whether the wound has healed; the excuse of harm is the determining factor.

Twelve Differences Between Wiping Over a Bandage and Over Khuff
Enumeration of twelve differences between jabeerah and khuff rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the twelve differences between wiping over a bandage (jabeerah) and wiping over leather socks (khuff) according to the Hanafi school, and apply each difference to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Jabeerah rulings are more lenient than khuff rulings because medical necessity relaxes the conditions.

Wiping over a bandage (jabeerah) and wiping over leather socks (khuff) are both concessions for purification, but they differ in many details. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq enumerates twelve points of distinction, covering conditions, time limits, nullification, and more. Understanding these differences ensures that you apply the correct ruling in each case.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the differences
Group each of the twelve differences into categories: prerequisites for wiping (e.g., being in wudu, time limit), actions during wiping (extent, repetition, stacking), and post-wiping events (water ingress, removal, nullification).
This helps organize the large list into manageable groups.
2
State the ruling for jabeerah
For each difference, first recall the ruling specific to jabeerah: for example, it has no time limit, does not require intention, and wiping once suffices.
3
State the contrasting ruling for khuff
Then recall the ruling for khuff: it has a time limit (1 day resident, 3 traveler), requires intention, and the wipe must be on the top in a specific manner.
4
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
For differences where the Hanafi school has internal disagreement (e.g., repetition of wipe, extent of coverage), identify the different opinions and the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view.
The source text highlights that the correct view is one wipe and covering most of the bandage.

Source Text
