ثم اعلم أن المسح على الجبيرة يخالف المسح على الخف من وجوه الأول أن الجبيرة لا يشترط شدها على وضوء بخلاف الخف. الثاني أن مسح الجبيرة غير موقت بوقت معين بخلاف الخف. الثالث أن الجبيرة إذا عن غير برء لا ينتقض المسح بخلاف الخف. الرابع إذا سقطت عن برء لا يجب إلا غسل ذلك الموضع إذا كان على وضوء بخلاف الخف فإنه يجب عليه غسل الرجلين. الخامس أن الجبيرة يستوي فيها الحدث الأكبر والأصغر بخلاف الخف. سادسها أن الجبيرة يجب استيعابها في المسح في رواية بخلاف الخف فإنه لا يجب رواية واحدة. هكذا ذكر الزيلعي . وقد يزاد عليها أيضاً فنقول : السابع أن الصحيح وجوب مسح أكثر الجبيرة بخلاف الخف. الثامن أنهم اختلفوا هل يشترط تكرار مسح الجبيرة فمنهم من شرط المسح ثلاثاً إلا أن تكون الجراحة في الرأس فلا يلزمه تكرار المسح ومنهم من قال : التكرار ليس بشرط ويجوز له أن يمسح مرة واحدة كمسح الرأس والخفين وهو الأصح عند علمائنا ـ كذا في الذخيرة - مسح الخف لم يشترط تكراره اتفاقاً. التاسع أنه إذا مسح عليها ثم شدّ عليها أخرى أو عصابة جاز المسح على الفوقاني بخلاف الحق إذا مسح عليه لا يجوز المسح على الفوقاني كما قدمناه العاشر إذا دخل الماء تحت الجبائر لا يبطل المسح بخلاف الخف. ذكره الزاهدي. الحادي عشر أن النية لا تشترط فيه باتفاق الروايات بخلاف المسح على الخف كما سيأتي . الثاني عشر إذا زالت العصابة الفوقانية التي مسح عليها لا يعيد المسح على التحتانية كما قدمناه بخلاف في الذخيرة عن أبي يوسف الخ) حمله في النهر على أنه قول لأبي يوسف لا الإمام وأيده بما يأتي عن القنية، وهذا أولى مما ذكره المؤلف إذ لا شيء مما مر ينافيه قوله : (السابع) أن الصحيح الخ) قال في النهر : : لا ينبغي ذكر هذا . عد الشارح أن الجبيرة يجب استيعابها بالمسح في رواية بخلاف الخف لأن عد ذلك يسقط هذا اهـ. قال بعض الفضلاء : لا يسقطه لأنه لا يلزم من نفي وجوب الاستيعاب نفي وجوب الأكثر تأمل، قوله : (العاشر إذا دخل الماء تحت الجبائر لا يبطل) قال في النهر: الأولى أن يقال لا يبطل اتفاقاً بخلاف الخف لما مر .
Then know that wiping over the bandage differs from wiping over the khuff in several aspects: First: The bandage does not require having been tied in a state of wudu, unlike the khuff. Second: Wiping over the bandage is not limited to a specific time, unlike the khuff. Third: If the bandage falls not due to recovery, the wiping is not nullified, unlike the khuff. Fourth: If it falls after recovery, only that spot must be washed if one is in wudu, unlike the khuff where both feet must be washed. Fifth: Major and minor hadath are equal for the bandage, unlike the khuff. Sixth: Covering the entire bandage in wiping is obligatory in one narration, unlike the khuff where it is not obligatory in one narration. Thus mentioned al-Zayla'i. Additional aspects can be added: Seventh: The correct view is that wiping most of the bandage is obligatory, unlike the khuff. Eighth: They differed on whether repeating the wiping over the bandage is required; some required wiping three times unless the wound is on the head, in which case repetition is not required; others said repetition is not a condition and it is permissible to wipe once like wiping the head and khuff, and this is the most sound according to our scholars—as in al-Dhakhira. Wiping over the khuff does not require repetition by consensus. Ninth: If one wiped over the bandage then wrapped another bandage over it, it is permissible to wipe over the upper one, unlike the khuff where if one wiped over it, it is not permissible to wipe over a second one as we mentioned. Tenth: If water enters under the bandage, it does not invalidate the wiping, unlike the khuff. Mentioned by al-Zahidi. Eleventh: Intention is not required according to all narrations, unlike wiping over the khuff as will come. Twelfth: If the upper bandage that was wiped is removed, one does not repeat the wiping over the lower bandage as we mentioned. Contrary to what is in al-Dhakhira from Abu Yusuf... He interpreted it in al-Nahr as a statement of Abu Yusuf, not the Imam, and supported it with what comes from al-Qunyah, and this is better than what the author mentioned since nothing of what passed contradicts it. His statement: (Seventh) that the correct is... He said in al-Nahr: It is not appropriate to mention this... The commentator considered that the bandage must be completely covered in wiping according to one narration, unlike the khuff, because mentioning that invalidates this. Some virtuous scholars said: It does not invalidate it, because negating the obligation of complete coverage does not negate the obligation of covering most. Contemplate. His statement: (Tenth) if water enters under the bandage it does not invalidate... He said in al-Nahr: It is better to say it does not invalidate by agreement, unlike the khuff as previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the differences between the rulings on wiping over a bandage (jabeerah) and wiping over leather socks (khuff). The commentator first lists six points from al-Zayla'i, then adds six more. Key points include: (1) The bandage need not be applied in a state of wudu. (2) No time limit for wiping on bandage. (3) If the bandage falls before healing, wiping is not nullified. (4) If falls after healing, only the spot needs washing. (5) Both major and minor impurity are treated alike. (6) Covering the entire bandage is obligatory in one narration. (7) The correct view is that most of the bandage must be wiped. (8) There is disagreement on repeating the wipe; the preferred view is that once is enough. (9) If a second bandage is added, wiping on the upper one is valid for bandages but not for khuff. (10) Water entering under the bandage does not break the wiping. (11) Intention is not required for wiping on bandage by consensus. (12) If the upper bandage is removed, one does not repeat the wiping on the lower. The passage also contains a brief comment on the seventh point: al-Nahr criticizes mentioning it because it might be confused with the sixth, but a scholar defends it. Overall, the differences show that rulings for jabeerah are more relaxed due to the greater need for medical treatment.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): Leather socks worn over the feet that can be wiped over during wudu under specific conditions.
الاستيعاب (al-isti'ab): Covering the entire surface of the bandage with the wiping hand; required in one narration but not in the most correct view.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention; not required for wiping over a bandage by consensus, whereas it is required for wiping over khuff according to the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is a valid difference between wiping over jabeerah and wiping over khuff?
A) Water entering under the bandage invalidates the wipe; for khuff it does not.
B) Wiping over jabeerah is time-limited; khuff has no time limit.
C) If the bandage falls without recovery, the wipe is nullified; for khuff it remains.
D) Intention is not required for jabeerah but is required for khuff.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes twelve rulings between wiping over a bandage and wiping over khuff, with jabeerah being more lenient due to necessity.

Foundational Differences Between Splint and Khuff Wiping (Points 1-7)
First seven differences between splint and khuff wiping.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state seven foundational differences between wiping over a splint and wiping over a khuff, and explain the rationale for each difference.

Core Idea
Splint wiping is more lenient than khuff wiping because it is a medical necessity.

Though both splint and khuff involve wiping over a covering in wudu, they are governed by distinct rules. This lesson examines the first seven of twenty-five differences enumerated in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, highlighting how necessity shapes Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identifying the Two Coverings
Recognize that a splint (jabīrah) is a medical bandage, while a khuff is a leather sock. Both allow wiping instead of washing, but under different conditions.
Splint is a necessity; khuff is a concession.
2
Analysing Points 1 and 2: Wudu and Time
Point 1: A splint need not be tied during wudu, unlike a khuff. Point 2: Splint wiping has no time limit, unlike khuff (1 day for resident, 3 for traveller).
The splint's leniency reflects that injury may occur at any time.
3
Points 3-5: Nullification and Coverage
Point 3: If a splint falls off without healing, the wipe is not nullified; for khuff, removal nullifies. Point 4: After healing, only the spot needs washing; for khuff, both feet must be washed. Point 5: Splint covers both major and minor impurity; khuff only covers minor.
Splint rulings are tied to the wound's state.
4
Points 6-7: Extent of Wiping
Point 6: In one narration, comprehensive wiping of the splint is required; for khuff, it is never required. Point 7: The correct view is that wiping most of the splint is obligatory; for khuff, only a minimal wipe suffices.
The splint's wipe is more extensive because it replaces washing the wound.

ثم اعلم أن المسح على الجبيرة يخالف المسح على الخف من وجوه الأول أن الجبيرة لا يشترط شدها على وضوء بخلاف الخف. الثاني أن مسح الجبيرة غير موقت بوقت معين بخلاف الخف. الثالث أن الجبيرة إذا عن غير برء لا ينتقض المسح بخلاف الخف. الرابع إذا سقطت عن برء لا يجب إلا غسل ذلك الموضع إذا كان على وضوء بخلاف الخف فإنه يجب عليه غسل الرجلين. الخامس أن الجبيرة يستوي فيها الحدث الأكبر والأصغر بخلاف الخف. سادسها أن الجبيرة يجب استيعابها في المسح في رواية بخلاف الخف فإنه لا يجب رواية واحدة. السابع أن الصحيح وجوب مسح أكثر الجبيرة بخلاف الخف. الثامن أنهم اختلفوا هل يشترط تكرار مسح الجبيرة فمنهم من شرط المسح ثلاثاً إلا أن تكون الجراحة في الرأس فلا يلزمه تكرار المسح ومنهم من قال التكرار ليس بشرط ويجوز له أن يمسح مرة واحدة كمسح الرأس والخفين وهو الأصح عند علمائنا. التاسع أنه إذا مسح عليها ثم شدّ عليها أخرى أو عصابة جاز المسح على الفوقاني بخلاف الحق إذا مسح عليه لا يجوز المسح على الفوقاني. العاشر إذا دخل الماء تحت الجبائر لا يبطل المسح بخلاف الخف. الحادي عشر أن النية لا تشترط فيه باتفاق الروايات بخلاف المسح على الخف. الثاني عشر إذا زالت العصابة الفوقانية التي مسح عليها لا يعيد المسح على التحتانية. الثالث عشر إذا كان الباقي من العضو المعصوب أقل من ثلاثة أصابع كاليد المقطوعة والرجل جاز المسح عليها بخلاف المسح على الخفين. الرابع عشر أن الجبيرة ليس ثابتاً بالكتاب اتفاقاً بخلاف مسح الخف فإن خلافاً. الخامس عشر أن مسح الجبيرة يجوز تركه في بعض الروايات بخلاف المسح على الخفين فإنه لا يجوز تركه مع إرادة عدم الغسل. السادس عشر أن المسح على الجبيرة ليس خلفاً ولا بدلاً عن الغسل بخلاف الخف. السابع عشر أن المسح على الجبيرة يترك إن ضر وإلا لا بخلاف الخف. الثامن عشر أنه مشروط بالعجز عن مسح نفس الموضع فإن قدر على مسحه فلا مسح عليها. التاسع عشر أنه يبطل ببرء موضعها وإن لم تسقط. العشرون أنه يبطل سقوطها عن برء بخلاف الخف فإنه يبطل بسقوطه بلا شرط. الحادي والعشرون أن جبيرة رجل يجمع مع غسل الأخرى بخلاف الخف. الثاني والعشرون أنه مشروط بالعجز عن مسح الموضع بخلاف الخف. الثالث والعشرون أنه يجوز ولو كانت على غير الرجلين بخلاف الخف. الرابع والعشرون إذا غمس الجبيرة في إناء يريد به المسح عليها لم يجز وأفسد الماء بخلاف الخف، وكذا الرأس فلا يفسد، ويجوز عند الثاني خلافاً لمحمد. والفرق لأبي يوسف أن المسح يتأدى بالبلة فلا يكون الماء مستعملاً ويجوز المسح، أما مسح الجبيرة فكالغسل لما تحته. الخامس والعشرون لو كانت على رجله وسقطت عن برء ويخاف إن غسلها أن تسقط أن يتيمم بخلاف الخف على ما فتدبر والله تعالى أعلم.
Then know that wiping over the splint differs from wiping over the khuff in aspects: First: The splint need not be tied during wudu, unlike the khuff. Second: Splint wiping is not time-limited, unlike the khuff. Third: If the splint falls off without healing, the wipe is not nullified, unlike the khuff. Fourth: If it falls off after healing, only washing that spot is required if one is in wudu, unlike the khuff where washing both feet is required. Fifth: Splint covers both major and minor events equally, unlike the khuff. Sixth: In one narration, comprehensive wiping of the splint is required, unlike the khuff where it is not required in any single narration. Seventh: The correct view is that wiping most of the splint is obligatory, unlike the khuff. Eighth: There is disagreement on repeating the wipe on the splint; some require three unless on the head, others say once is enough, and that is the preferred Hanafi view. Ninth: If one wipes over it and then puts on another or a bandage, wiping over the top is allowed, unlike the khuff where it is not. Tenth: If water enters under the splint, the wipe is not nullified, unlike the khuff. Eleventh: Intention is not required for splint wiping according to all narrations, unlike the khuff. Twelfth: If the upper bandage that was wiped comes off, one does not re-wipe the lower one. Thirteenth: If the remaining part of the bandaged limb is less than three fingers, like a cut hand or foot, wiping over it is allowed, unlike the khuff. Fourteenth: The splint is not established by the Book unanimously, unlike the khuff which is debated. Fifteenth: Splint wiping may be omitted in some narrations, unlike khuff wiping which cannot be omitted if one intends not to wash. Sixteenth: Splint wiping is not a substitute for washing, unlike the khuff. Seventeenth: Splint wiping is left off if harmful, otherwise not, unlike the khuff. Eighteenth: It is conditioned on inability to wipe the spot itself; if able, no wipe over it. Nineteenth: It is nullified by healing of the spot even if the splint does not fall. Twentieth: It is nullified by falling off after healing, unlike the khuff which is nullified by falling without condition. Twenty-first: The splint of one foot is combined with washing the other, unlike the khuff. Twenty-second: It is conditioned on inability to wipe the spot, unlike the khuff. Twenty-third: It is allowed even if not on the feet, unlike the khuff. Twenty-fourth: If one dips the splint in a vessel intending to wipe over it, it is not allowed and spoils the water, unlike the khuff; also for the head it does not spoil, and it is allowed according to Abu Yusuf contrary to Muhammad. The difference for Abu Yusuf is that the wipe is performed with moisture so the water is not used; but for the splint it is like washing what is under it. Twenty-fifth: If the splint is on his leg and falls off after healing, and he fears that washing it may cause it to fall off, he performs tayammum, unlike the khuff; so ponder, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is a comparative list of 25 differences between the rulings on wiping over a splint (جبيرة) and wiping over khuffs (خفين). The author presents these to clarify that despite superficial similarity, the two acts have distinct fiqh rules. The differences span placement conditions, timing, nullification, coverage, and more. For example, splints do not require prior wudu for placement, have no time limit, and are not nullified by falling without healing. The underlying principle is that splints are a medical necessity, so the law shows leniency. The Hanafi school uses these distinctions to guide practice in cases of injury.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabīrah): A splint or bandage applied to a broken or injured limb for medical treatment.
خف (khuff): Leather sock worn on the feet, over which wiping is permitted in wudu under certain conditions.
استيعاب (istī'āb): Comprehensive coverage of the splint or khuff with the wiping hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, if a person's cast falls off after the bone has healed, what do they need to do?
A) Perform wudu again entirely.
B) Only wash the spot that was under the cast if they are in wudu.
C) Wash both feet.
D) Nothing; the wudu remains valid as is.

Key Takeaway
Splint wiping is a lenient ruling due to medical necessity, differing from khuff in many ways such as timing, nullification, and coverage.
